Defining Ikhtilaf in Sanad and Matn
Defining ikhtilaf and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ikhtilaf in hadith terminology and distinguish between the two types: disagreement in sanad and disagreement in matn.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf in hadith is every difference among narrators in either the chain (sanad) or the text (matn).

This passage provides a precise definition of ikhtilaf (disagreement) as used in hadith criticism. The author first notes the absence of a prior definition, then offers his own, dividing it into two fundamental types. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating how differences in transmission affect the authenticity of hadith and, consequently, legal rulings derived from them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the author's definition
Read the proposed definition: ikhtilaf is that concerning which narrators differ in sanad or matn. Note that this is a technical definition specific to hadith transmission.
This definition excludes juristic disagreement (ikhtilaf al-fuqaha) which is addressed later.
2
Recognize the two types
Identify the two divisions: (1) ikhtilaf in sanad (chain) includes additions/omissions of narrators, name changes, connected/disconnected chains. (2) ikhtilaf in matn (text) includes additions/deletions, raising (raf') or stopping (waqf).
These categories help classify any variation encountered in hadith.
3
Analyze Imam Muslim's classification
Examine Muslim's two aspects of error detection: mistaken attribution of lineage/name, and contradiction by a single narrator against a group of reliable memorizers. Note that the group's version is preferred.
This method is a foundational principle in hadith criticism and is applied by early imams like Shu'bah and Sufyan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني تعريف الاختلاف اصطلاحاً لم أجد تعريفاً للعلماء في الاختلاف، لكن يمكنني أن أعرفه بأنه: ما اختلف الرُّوَاة فِيْهِ سنداً أو متناً. وعلى هَذَا التعريف يمكننا أن نقسم الاختلاف على ضربين: الأول: اختلاف الرُّوَاة في السند: وَهُوَ أن يختلف الرُّوَاة في سند ما زيادة أو نقصاناً، بحذف راو، أو إضافته، أو تغيير اسم أو اختلاف بوصل وإرسال، أو اتصال وانقطاع، أو اختلاف في الجمع والإفراد. الثاني: اختلاف الرُّوَاة في الْمَتْن: زيادة ونقصاناً، أو رفعاً ووقفاً. وَقَدْ أحسن وأجاد الإمام مسلم بن الحجاج إذ صوّر لنا الاختلاف تصويراً بديعاً فَقَالَ في كتابه العظيم التمييز: اعلم أرشدك الله، أن الَّذِي يدور بِهِ مَعْرِفَة الخطأ في رِوَايَة ناقل الْحَدِيث - إذا هم اختلفوا فيه – من جهتين: أحدهما: أن ينقل الناقل حديثاً بإسناد فينسب رجلاً مشهوراً بنسب في إسناد خبره خلاف نسبته الَّتِي هِيَ نسبته أو يسميه باسم سوى اسمه، فيكون خطأ ذَلِكَ غَيْر خفي على أهل العلم حين يرد عليهم والجهة الأخرى: أن يروي نفر من حفّاظ الناس حديثاً عن مثل الزهري أو غيره من الحفاظ الأئمة بإسناد واحد ومتن واحد مجتمعون عَلَى روايته في الإسناد والمتن، لا يختلفون فيه في معنى، فيرويه آخر سواهم عمن حدث عَنْهُ النفر الَّذِيْنَ وصفناهم بعينه فيخالفهم في الإسناد أو يقلب الْمَثْن فيجعله بخلاف ما حكى من وصفنا من فيعلم حينئذٍ أنَّ الصَّحِيح من الروايتين ما حدث الجماعة من الحفاظ، دون الواحد المنفرد وإن كَانَ حافظاً، عَلَى هَذَا المذهب رأينا أهل العلم بالحديث يحكمون في الْحَدِيث، مثل شعبة وسفيان بن عيينة ويحيى بن سعيد وعبد الرحمن بن مهدي وغيرهم من أئمة أهل العلم.
The Second Section: Definition of Disagreement Terminologically. I did not find a definition from the scholars for disagreement, but I can define it as: that concerning which the narrators differed in chain or text. According to this definition, we can divide disagreement into two types: First: Disagreement of narrators in the chain: which is that the narrators differ in a chain by addition or deletion, by omitting a narrator, or adding him, or changing a name, or disagreement by connecting or sending, or by continuity or interruption, or disagreement in plural or singular. Second: Disagreement of narrators in the text: by addition or deletion, or by raising or stopping. And Imam Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj excelled when he depicted disagreement in a wonderful way, saying in his great book 'al-Tamyiz': Know, may Allah guide you, that that by which knowledge of error in the narration of a hadith transmitter is achieved - when they disagree about it - is from two aspects: One of them: that the transmitter transmits a hadith with an isnad and attributes a famous man by a lineage in the isnad of his report contrary to his lineage which is his lineage, or names him by a name other than his name, so that error is not hidden from the people of knowledge when it comes to them. And the other aspect: that a group of memorizers of people narrate a hadith from like al-Zuhri or other memorizer imams with one isnad and one text, unanimous upon its narration in the isnad and text, not differing in meaning, then another besides them narrates from the same person from whom the described group narrated, and opposes them in the isnad or turns the text making it contrary to what those we described related, so it is known then that the correct of the two narrations is that which the group of memorizers narrated, not the single individual even if he is a memorizer. Upon this method we saw the people of knowledge of hadith judging regarding hadith, like Shu'bah, Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah, Yahya ibn Sa'id, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, and other imams of the people of knowledge.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a definition section (matlab) on the term 'ikhtilaf' (disagreement) as used in hadith studies. The author begins by stating that he found no prior definition from scholars, so he proposes his own: ikhtilaf is every instance where narrators differ in either the sanad (chain) or the matn (text). He then divides ikhtilaf into two types. The first type is disagreement in the sanad, which includes variations such as adding or omitting a narrator, changing a name, or differences in whether the chain is connected or disconnected. The second type is disagreement in the matn, which includes additions, deletions, or differences in raising (raf') or stopping (waqf) a report. To illustrate, the author quotes Imam Muslim's classification from his book 'al-Tamyiz'. Muslim identifies two ways to detect error: (1) when a transmitter mistakenly attributes a narrator to a wrong lineage or name, and (2) when a single transmitter contradicts a group of reliable memorizers in either chain or text. Muslim emphasizes that the group's version is preferred over the individual's, even if the individual is a memorizer, following the practice of early hadith critics like Shu'bah, Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah, and others. This definition is crucial for understanding how jurists (fuqaha') later evaluate hadiths that may affect legal rulings.

Key Terms
الاختلاف (al-ikhtilāf): The difference among narrators in the chain (sanad) or text (matn) of a hadith.
السند (al-sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting the hadith.
المتن (al-matn): The text or content of the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of ikhtilaf (disagreement) are there?
A) One: in sanad only
B) Two: in sanad and matn
C) Three: sanad, matn, and meaning
D) Four: addition, deletion, change, disconnection

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilaf in hadith terminology is defined as every difference among narrators in either the sanad or the matn, and its resolution relies on preferring the version narrated by the majority of reliable memorizers.

Defining Idhtirab: The Irreconcilable Inconsistency
Defining mudtarib hadith and its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a mudtarib hadith, distinguish it from general ikhtilaf, and explain why idhtirab weakens a hadith in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Idhtirab is irreconcilable inconsistency in transmission that renders a hadith weak.

Not every difference in narration is equal. While some disagreements can be resolved through tarjih, idhtirab refers to a specific kind of inconsistency that cannot be reconciled. Understanding this distinction is critical for evaluating hadith as legal evidence in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term
Locate the term 'muḍṭarib' in the Arabic text. Note the root 'ḍ-r-b' implying disorder.
2
Analyze the definition
Break down the definition: 'a hadith in which its narrator differs, narrating it once in one way, and another time in a contrary way'. Recognize that inconsistency can be from a single narrator or multiple narrators.
3
Distinguish from ikhtilaf
Understand that ikhtilaf is any difference; idhtirab is a subset implying irreconcilability. In Hanafi usul, a mudtarib hadith is rejected as a primary proof.
4
Apply the concept
Given a scenario with conflicting hadith versions, determine if idhtirab exists. If the versions can be harmonized (e.g., by tarjih), it is not idhtirab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثاني الفرق بين الاضطراب والاختلاف الْحَدِيث المضطرب: هُوَ ما اختلف راويه فِيْهِ، فرواه مرة عَلَى وجه، ومرة عَلَى آخر مخالف لَهُ. وهكذا إن اضطرب فِيْهِ راويان فأكثر فرواه كُـلّ واحد عَلَى وجه مخالف للآخر
The Second Research: The Difference between Idhtirab and Ikhtilaf. The mudtarib hadith: it is that in which its narrator differs, narrating it once in one way, and another time in another way contrary to it. Likewise, if two or more narrators are in disarray regarding it, each one narrates it in a way contrary to the other.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a mabhas (research section) that clarifies the distinction between 'idhtirab' (disruption) and 'ikhtilaf' (disagreement). The author defines a 'hadith mudtarib' as a hadith in which a single narrator transmits it inconsistently – narrating it differently on different occasions. The definition also covers cases where two or more narrators transmit the same hadith but in conflicting ways, each version differing from the others. This is a specific type of ikhtilaf, but not all ikhtilaf is idhtirab. Ikhtilaf is broader, including any difference in sanad or matn, while idhtirab specifically involves inconsistency from the same narrator or conflicting versions from multiple narrators that cannot be reconciled. This distinction is important in hadith criticism and impacts how jurists weigh evidence. For example, a mudtarib hadith is considered weak and cannot be used as a primary proof in Hanafi fiqh, whereas a non-mudtarib ikhtilaf may still be resolved through tarjih (preference).

Key Terms
الاضطراب (al-iḍṭirāb): Inconsistency in narration, where a narrator transmits a hadith in different ways or multiple narrators give contradictory versions.
الحديث المضطرب (al-ḥadīth al-muḍṭarib): A hadith that is narrated in conflicting versions by one or more narrators, such that preference is not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the defining characteristic of a hadith mudtarib according to the passage?
A) It has a weak narrator.
B) Its narrator differs in how he transmits it on different occasions.
C) It has a missing link in the chain.
D) It contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
A mudtarib hadith is one with irreconcilable inconsistency in its transmission, rendering it weak in Hanafi usul, unlike general ikhtilaf which may be resolved through tarjih.

Relativity of Ḍabṭ: Memory vs. Book Narration
Textual analysis of how relative precision causes hadith differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the relativity of ḍabṭ in narrators causes hadith variation and evaluate narrations based on the mode of transmission.

Core Idea
Precision is relative: even trustworthy narrators can err from memory, causing hadith differences.

This lesson examines the concept of ḍabṭ (precision) in hadith transmission. The author argues that precision is not absolute; even reliable narrators sometimes make mistakes. The case of Sharīk al-Qāḍī, whose memory deteriorated after becoming a judge, demonstrates that narrations from memory may be unreliable while his written records remain sound. This understanding is vital for usul al-fiqh as it explains why conflicting transmissions occur and guides jurists in weighing evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define ḍabṭ and its relative nature
Understand that precision varies by narrator and circumstance; it is not fixed.
2
Distinguish memory vs. book narration
Recognize that narration from memory is more prone to error than from written records.
3
Analyze Sharīk al-Qāḍī's case
His memory changed after becoming a judge; his books remained sound, but memory-based narrations became problematic.
Quoted scholars confirm this distinction.
4
Recognize the consequence
Such variation leads to differences in hadith texts and chains, impacting juristic rulings.
5
Apply the principle
When evaluating a hadith, consider whether the narrator transmitted from memory or book, and any known memory changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
خاصة، وَهُوَ أمرٌ اعتيادي يحصل لبني الإنسان؛ لأن الضبط كما سبق أمرٌ نسبي. وهذا الباب الذي يمكن من خلاله دخول الوهم في بعض أحاديث الثقات يعد سبباً من أسباب اختلاف الروايات متناً وإسناداً مِمَّا يؤدي بالمحصلة النهائية إلى حصول بعض الاختلافات في بَعْض الأحاديث. وهذا الأمر نراه جلياً في أحاديث الثقات التي أخطؤوا فيها. وما يأتي في كثير من الأمثلة اللاحقة دليل لما أصلناه في أن الضبط أمر نسبي ينفك عَنْ بعض الثقات أحياناً في بعض الأحاديث.
وَكَانَ هناك رواة، لَهُمْ كتب صحيحة متقنة وفي حفظهم شيء وهؤلاء كانوا أحياناً إذا حدثوا من حفظهم غلطوا وإذا حدثوا من كتابهم أصابوا، وهذا أمر أولاه العلماء عناية؛ لأن فِيْهِ مزيد ضبط في رِوَايَة هَذَا الرَّاوِي خاصة، ومن الأمثلة عَلَى ذَلِكَ شريك القاضي وَهُوَ شريك بن عَبْد الله النخعي، الكوفي، القاضي بواسط، ثُمَّ الكوفة، أبـو عبد الله: صدوق يخطئ كثيراً، تغير حفظه منذ ولي القضاء بالكوفة.
قَالَ فِيْهِ مُحَمَّد بن عَبْد الله بن عمار الموصلي: «شريك كتبه صحاح فمن سَمِعَ مِنْهُ من كتبه فهو صَحِيح، قَالَ: وَلَمْ يَسْمَع من شريك من كتابه إلا إسحاق الأزرق. وَقَالَ فِيْهِ يعقوب بن شيبة: كتبه صحاح». وفي رِوَايَة الْخَطِيْب البغدادي عَنْ يعقوب في شريك: «ثقة صدوق، صَحِيح الكتاب رديء الحفظ مضطربه».
ومن الأمور التي يدخل الاختلاف بسببها لعدم الضبط، هو عدم الضبط في بلد معين، وَهُوَ أَن يَكُون الرَّاوِي ضابطاً إلا أنه في سماعه لحديث أهل بلد معين لا يَكُون ضابطاً لحديثهم لعدم تأهبه لِذَلِكَ؛ لأن الضبط كَمَا يَكُون في الأداء يَكُون في التحمل فإن لم يتحمل جيداً لاختلال في السَّمَاع، أو عدم جودة في تقييد الكتاب لم يؤد جيداً، ومثل هَذَا قَدْ حصل لعدد من الرُّوَاة، فتجد أحاديثهم جياداً في روايتهم عَنْ أهل بلد معين، وتجدها دون ذَلِكَ عِنْدَ أهل بلد آخر لخلل طرأ في السَّماع والتحمل.
ومن أولئك الرُّوَاة الَّذِيْنَ تضعف روايتهم في بلد دون آخر إسماعيل بن عياش، وَهُوَ إسماعيل بن عياش بن سليم العنسي - بالنون - أبو عتبة الحمصي: صدوق في روايته عَنْ أهل بلده مُخَلّط في غيرهم. قَالَ يعقوب بن سفيان: «تكلم قوم في إسماعيل وإسماعيل ثقة عدل أعلم الناس بحديث الشام، ولا يدفعه دافع، وأكثر ما تكلموا قالوا: يُغرِبُ عَنْ ثقات المدنيين والمكيين». وَقَالَ أبو بكر بن أبي خيثمة: سُئِلَ يحيى بن معين عَنْ إسماعيل بن عياش، فَقَالَ: «ليس به بأس في أهل الشام. والعراقيون يكرهون حديثه». وَقَالَ مضر بن مُحَمَّد الأسدي، عَنْ يَحْيَى: «إذا حدَّث عن الشاميين وذكر الخبر، فحديثه مستقيم، وإذا حدث عَنْ الحجازيين والعراقيين، خلط ما شئت». وَقَالَ أبو داود: سألت أحمدَ عَنْ إسماعيل بن عياش فَقَالَ: «ما حدّث عَنْ مشايخهم قلت الشاميين؟ قَالَ : نعم. فأما ما حدث عَنْ غيرهم، فعنده مناكير». وَقَالَ أبو طالب أحمد بن حميد: سَمِعْتُ أحمد بن حَنْبَل يَقُول: «إسماعيل بن عياش ما رَوَى عَن الشاميين صَحِيح، وما رَوَى عَنْ أهل الحجاز فليس بصحيح».
The preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of disagreement. Specifically, it is a habitual matter that occurs among humans because precision, as previously mentioned, is relative. This door through which illusion can enter into some narrations of trustworthy (narrators) is considered one of the causes of differences in narrations in text and chain, ultimately leading to some disagreements in some hadiths. We see this clearly in the hadiths of trustworthy narrators in which they made mistakes. What follows in many later examples is evidence for what we have established: that precision is relative and sometimes separates from some trustworthy narrators in some hadiths. There were narrators who had sound, precise books but had some weakness in their memory. These would sometimes err when narrating from memory and be correct when narrating from their books. This matter scholars paid attention to because it involves greater precision in the narration of this particular narrator. Among the examples of that is Sharīk al-Qāḍī, who is Sharīk ibn 'Abdullāh al-Nakha'ī, al-Kūfī, the judge of Wāsiṭ, then Kūfa, Abū 'Abdillāh: truthful (ṣadūq), makes many mistakes, his memory changed since he became judge in Kūfa. Muhammad ibn 'Abdillāh ibn 'Ammār al-Mawṣilī said about him: 'Sharīk's books are sound; whoever heard from him from his books, it is sound. He said: Only Isḥāq al-Azraq heard from Sharīk from his book.' And Ya'qūb ibn Shayba said about him: 'His books are sound.' And in a narration of al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī from Ya'qūb concerning Sharīk: 'Trustworthy, truthful, sound in book, bad in memory, confused.' Among the matters that cause disagreement due to lack of precision is the lack of precision in a specific region, which is that a narrator may be precise except that in his hearing of hadith from the people of a particular region he is not precise due to his lack of preparation for that. Because precision, just as it is in performance, it is in reception. If he did not receive well due to a defect in hearing or lack of quality in recording the book, he will not perform well. Such has occurred with a number of narrators. You find their hadiths good in their narration from people of a specific region, and you find them less than that with people of another region due to a defect that occurred in hearing and reception. Among those narrators whose narration weakens in one region but not another is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, who is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh ibn Sulaym al-'Ansī (with nūn), Abū 'Utba al-Ḥimṣī: truthful in his narration from the people of his town, mixed up in others. Ya'qūb ibn Sufyān said: 'Some people spoke about Ismā'īl, and Ismā'īl is trustworthy, just, most knowledgeable of the people of Shām about hadith, and no one can refute him. Most of what they said is that he reports odd things from trustworthy Madanīs and Makkīs.' Abū Bakr ibn Abī Khaythama said: Yaḥyā ibn Ma'īn was asked about Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, and he said: 'There is no problem with him regarding the people of Shām. The Iraqis dislike his hadith.' Muḍar ibn Muhammad al-Asadī said from Yaḥyā: 'When he narrates from Shāmīs and mentions the report, his hadith is upright. When he narrates from Ḥijāzīs and Iraqīs, he mixes up as much as you want.' Abū Dāwūd said: I asked Aḥmad about Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, and he said: 'What he narrated from their shaykhs – do you mean the Shāmīs? He said: Yes. As for what he narrated from others, he has rejected reports (manākīr).' Abū Ṭālib Aḥmad ibn Ḥamīd said: I heard Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal say: 'Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh: what he narrated from the Shāmīs is sound, and what he narrated from the people of Ḥijāz is not sound.'
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis from a work on the impact of differences in chains and texts on juristic disagreement. The author begins by stating that lack of precision (ḍabṭ) in narrators is a relative matter and a cause of variation in hadith. He then provides examples: Sharīk al-Qāḍī, whose memory deteriorated after becoming a judge, and who had reliable books. Scholars caution that his narrations from memory are problematic but those from his books are sound. The second example is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, who was reliable when narrating from Shāmīs but unreliable when narrating from Ḥijāzīs and Iraqīs, due to defects in his hearing and recording from those regions. This illustrates that precision can be context-dependent, affecting the authenticity of hadith and leading to disagreements among jurists. The author follows the order: first general principle, then example of Sharīk, then general principle about regional precision, then example of Ismā'īl. All examples are from Sunni hadith criticism, with no inter-madhhab disputes mentioned.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Precision and accuracy in narrating hadith, including memory and recording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Sharīk al-Qāḍī become unreliable when narrating from memory?
A) He was a weak liar.
B) His memory changed after he became a judge.
C) He only narrated from Iraqis.
D) He did not have written books.

Key Takeaway
The relativity of ḍabṭ means that even reliable narrators can err, so we must consider context (memory vs. book) when accepting hadith.

Regional Precision: Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh's Case
Textual analysis of regional precision and its impact on hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a narrator's precision can vary by region and apply this to evaluate narrations from narrators with known regional weaknesses.

Core Idea
A narrator may be precise for one region but not another, leading to hadith differences.

Precision is not only a personal trait but can be context-dependent. The author discusses narrators who are reliable when transmitting from certain regions but unreliable from others. The example of Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh illustrates that a narrator can be perfectly accurate for Syrian (Shām) hadith but confused for Hijazi and Iraqi hadith. This regional variation is another cause of differences in hadith texts and chains, which must be accounted for in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand region-specific precision
A narrator may excel in one area but not another due to differences in hearing, recording, or familiarity.
2
Identify factors causing regional weakness
Lack of proper hearing, recording, or preparation when studying from scholars of other regions.
The passage mentions defects in hearing and recording.
3
Analyze the example of Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh
He was praised for Shām hadith but criticized for Ḥijāzī and Iraqi hadith.
Quotes from Yaḥyā ibn Ma'īn and Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal confirm this.
4
Recognize the consequence
Hadith from that narrator about non-Shām regions are unreliable, causing differences in hadith.
5
Apply the principle
When encountering a hadith from a narrator with known regional weakness, verify the geographic origin of the report and weigh accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
خاصة، وَهُوَ أمرٌ اعتيادي يحصل لبني الإنسان؛ لأن الضبط كما سبق أمرٌ نسبي. وهذا الباب الذي يمكن من خلاله دخول الوهم في بعض أحاديث الثقات يعد سبباً من أسباب اختلاف الروايات متناً وإسناداً مِمَّا يؤدي بالمحصلة النهائية إلى حصول بعض الاختلافات في بَعْض الأحاديث. وهذا الأمر نراه جلياً في أحاديث الثقات التي أخطؤوا فيها. وما يأتي في كثير من الأمثلة اللاحقة دليل لما أصلناه في أن الضبط أمر نسبي ينفك عَنْ بعض الثقات أحياناً في بعض الأحاديث.
وَكَانَ هناك رواة، لَهُمْ كتب صحيحة متقنة وفي حفظهم شيء وهؤلاء كانوا أحياناً إذا حدثوا من حفظهم غلطوا وإذا حدثوا من كتابهم أصابوا، وهذا أمر أولاه العلماء عناية؛ لأن فِيْهِ مزيد ضبط في رِوَايَة هَذَا الرَّاوِي خاصة، ومن الأمثلة عَلَى ذَلِكَ شريك القاضي وَهُوَ شريك بن عَبْد الله النخعي، الكوفي، القاضي بواسط، ثُمَّ الكوفة، أبـو عبد الله: صدوق يخطئ كثيراً، تغير حفظه منذ ولي القضاء بالكوفة.
قَالَ فِيْهِ مُحَمَّد بن عَبْد الله بن عمار الموصلي: «شريك كتبه صحاح فمن سَمِعَ مِنْهُ من كتبه فهو صَحِيح، قَالَ: وَلَمْ يَسْمَع من شريك من كتابه إلا إسحاق الأزرق. وَقَالَ فِيْهِ يعقوب بن شيبة: كتبه صحاح». وفي رِوَايَة الْخَطِيْب البغدادي عَنْ يعقوب في شريك: «ثقة صدوق، صَحِيح الكتاب رديء الحفظ مضطربه».
ومن الأمور التي يدخل الاختلاف بسببها لعدم الضبط، هو عدم الضبط في بلد معين، وَهُوَ أَن يَكُون الرَّاوِي ضابطاً إلا أنه في سماعه لحديث أهل بلد معين لا يَكُون ضابطاً لحديثهم لعدم تأهبه لِذَلِكَ؛ لأن الضبط كَمَا يَكُون في الأداء يَكُون في التحمل فإن لم يتحمل جيداً لاختلال في السَّمَاع، أو عدم جودة في تقييد الكتاب لم يؤد جيداً، ومثل هَذَا قَدْ حصل لعدد من الرُّوَاة، فتجد أحاديثهم جياداً في روايتهم عَنْ أهل بلد معين، وتجدها دون ذَلِكَ عِنْدَ أهل بلد آخر لخلل طرأ في السَّماع والتحمل.
ومن أولئك الرُّوَاة الَّذِيْنَ تضعف روايتهم في بلد دون آخر إسماعيل بن عياش، وَهُوَ إسماعيل بن عياش بن سليم العنسي - بالنون - أبو عتبة الحمصي: صدوق في روايته عَنْ أهل بلده مُخَلّط في غيرهم. قَالَ يعقوب بن سفيان: «تكلم قوم في إسماعيل وإسماعيل ثقة عدل أعلم الناس بحديث الشام، ولا يدفعه دافع، وأكثر ما تكلموا قالوا: يُغرِبُ عَنْ ثقات المدنيين والمكيين». وَقَالَ أبو بكر بن أبي خيثمة: سُئِلَ يحيى بن معين عَنْ إسماعيل بن عياش، فَقَالَ: «ليس به بأس في أهل الشام. والعراقيون يكرهون حديثه». وَقَالَ مضر بن مُحَمَّد الأسدي، عَنْ يَحْيَى: «إذا حدَّث عن الشاميين وذكر الخبر، فحديثه مستقيم، وإذا حدث عَنْ الحجازيين والعراقيين، خلط ما شئت». وَقَالَ أبو داود: سألت أحمدَ عَنْ إسماعيل بن عياش فَقَالَ: «ما حدّث عَنْ مشايخهم قلت الشاميين؟ قَالَ : نعم. فأما ما حدث عَنْ غيرهم، فعنده مناكير». وَقَالَ أبو طالب أحمد بن حميد: سَمِعْتُ أحمد بن حَنْبَل يَقُول: «إسماعيل بن عياش ما رَوَى عَن الشاميين صَحِيح، وما رَوَى عَنْ أهل الحجاز فليس بصحيح».
The preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of disagreement. Specifically, it is a habitual matter that occurs among humans because precision, as previously mentioned, is relative. This door through which illusion can enter into some narrations of trustworthy (narrators) is considered one of the causes of differences in narrations in text and chain, ultimately leading to some disagreements in some hadiths. We see this clearly in the hadiths of trustworthy narrators in which they made mistakes. What follows in many later examples is evidence for what we have established: that precision is relative and sometimes separates from some trustworthy narrators in some hadiths. There were narrators who had sound, precise books but had some weakness in their memory. These would sometimes err when narrating from memory and be correct when narrating from their books. This matter scholars paid attention to because it involves greater precision in the narration of this particular narrator. Among the examples of that is Sharīk al-Qāḍī, who is Sharīk ibn 'Abdullāh al-Nakha'ī, al-Kūfī, the judge of Wāsiṭ, then Kūfa, Abū 'Abdillāh: truthful (ṣadūq), makes many mistakes, his memory changed since he became judge in Kūfa. Muhammad ibn 'Abdillāh ibn 'Ammār al-Mawṣilī said about him: 'Sharīk's books are sound; whoever heard from him from his books, it is sound. He said: Only Isḥāq al-Azraq heard from Sharīk from his book.' And Ya'qūb ibn Shayba said about him: 'His books are sound.' And in a narration of al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī from Ya'qūb concerning Sharīk: 'Trustworthy, truthful, sound in book, bad in memory, confused.' Among the matters that cause disagreement due to lack of precision is the lack of precision in a specific region, which is that a narrator may be precise except that in his hearing of hadith from the people of a particular region he is not precise due to his lack of preparation for that. Because precision, just as it is in performance, it is in reception. If he did not receive well due to a defect in hearing or lack of quality in recording the book, he will not perform well. Such has occurred with a number of narrators. You find their hadiths good in their narration from people of a specific region, and you find them less than that with people of another region due to a defect that occurred in hearing and reception. Among those narrators whose narration weakens in one region but not another is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, who is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh ibn Sulaym al-'Ansī (with nūn), Abū 'Utba al-Ḥimṣī: truthful in his narration from the people of his town, mixed up in others. Ya'qūb ibn Sufyān said: 'Some people spoke about Ismā'īl, and Ismā'īl is trustworthy, just, most knowledgeable of the people of Shām about hadith, and no one can refute him. Most of what they said is that he reports odd things from trustworthy Madanīs and Makkīs.' Abū Bakr ibn Abī Khaythama said: Yaḥyā ibn Ma'īn was asked about Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, and he said: 'There is no problem with him regarding the people of Shām. The Iraqis dislike his hadith.' Muḍar ibn Muhammad al-Asadī said from Yaḥyā: 'When he narrates from Shāmīs and mentions the report, his hadith is upright. When he narrates from Ḥijāzīs and Iraqīs, he mixes up as much as you want.' Abū Dāwūd said: I asked Aḥmad about Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, and he said: 'What he narrated from their shaykhs – do you mean the Shāmīs? He said: Yes. As for what he narrated from others, he has rejected reports (manākīr).' Abū Ṭālib Aḥmad ibn Ḥamīd said: I heard Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal say: 'Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh: what he narrated from the Shāmīs is sound, and what he narrated from the people of Ḥijāz is not sound.'
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis from a work on the impact of differences in chains and texts on juristic disagreement. The author begins by stating that lack of precision (ḍabṭ) in narrators is a relative matter and a cause of variation in hadith. He then provides examples: Sharīk al-Qāḍī, whose memory deteriorated after becoming a judge, and who had reliable books. Scholars caution that his narrations from memory are problematic but those from his books are sound. The second example is Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh, who was reliable when narrating from Shāmīs but unreliable when narrating from Ḥijāzīs and Iraqīs, due to defects in his hearing and recording from those regions. This illustrates that precision can be context-dependent, affecting the authenticity of hadith and leading to disagreements among jurists. The author follows the order: first general principle, then example of Sharīk, then general principle about regional precision, then example of Ismā'īl. All examples are from Sunni hadith criticism, with no inter-madhhab disputes mentioned.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Precision and accuracy in narrating hadith, including memory and recording.
الاختلاف (al-ikhtilāf): Disagreement or variation in hadith texts or chains due to narrator issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All his narrations.
B) Those from Hijaz.
C) Those from Shām.
D) Those from Iraq.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's precision can vary by region, so usulis must consider geographic origin when evaluating hadith.

Types of Tadlis (2-7) and Their Definitions
Listing and defining six types of tadlis (types 2-7) in hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and define each of the six types of tadlis described, and distinguish between them based on the method of concealment.

Core Idea
Six distinct types of tadlis, each hiding a different flaw in the chain; recognizing them is key to evaluating hadith authenticity.

In this lesson, we continue our exploration of tadlis by examining six specific types beyond the commonly known first type. Each type employs a different technique to obscure a defect in the isnad, from altering a shaykh's name to misrepresenting the mode of transmission. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for any student of usul who wishes to assess the reliability of prophetic narrations.

Guided Path
1
Tadlis al-Shuyukh (Type 2)
Define it as altering the name or kunyah of one's shaykh to obscure his identity. Note that it is considered lighter than the first type. Explore possible motivations (weak shaykh, younger, etc.).
2
Tadlis al-Taswiyah (Type 3)
Define it as dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones and using a plausible transmission formula. Note that it requires the mudallis to use explicit wording of tahdith. Mention famous practitioners: al-Walid ibn Muslim and Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid.
3
Tadlis al-'Atf (Type 4) and Tadlis al-Sukut (Type 5)
Tadlis al-'Atf: falsely claiming to have heard from two narrators when only heard from one. Tadlis al-Sukut: using a pause and then naming narrators to imply hearing.
4
Tadlis al-Qat' (Type 6) and Tadlis al-Siyagh al-Ada' (Type 7)
Tadlis al-Qat': omitting the transmission formula entirely (e.g., saying 'al-Zuhri from Anas'). Tadlis al-Siyagh al-Ada': using words like 'haddathana' for an ijazah, implying direct hearing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: تدليس الشيوخ: وَهُوَ أن يأتي باسم شيخه أو كنيته عَلَى خلاف المشهور به تعمية لأمره وتوعيراً للوقوف على حاله. وهذا النوع حكمه أخف من السابق، وفي هذا النوع تضييع للمروي عَنْهُ وللمروي وتوعير لطريق مَعْرِفَة حالهما. ثُمَّ إن الحال في كراهيته يختلف بحسب الغرض الحامل عَلَيْهِ، إِذْ إن من يدلس هَذَا التدليس قد يحمله كون شيخه الَّذِي غيّر سمته غَيْر ثقة، أو أصغر من الرَّاوِي عَنْهُ، أو متأخر الوفاة قد شاركه في السَّمَاعَ مِنْهُ جَمَاعَة دونه، أو كونه كثير الرِّوَايَة عَنْهُ فلا يحب تكرار شخص عَلَى صورة واحدة. الثالث: تدليس التسوية: وَهُوَ أن يروي عَنْ شيخه، ثُمَّ يسقط ضعيفاً بَيْنَ ثقتين قَدْ سَمِعَ أحدهما من الآخر أو لقيه، ويرويه بصيغة محتملة بَيْنَ الثقتين. وممن اشتهر بهذا النوع: الوليد بن مُسْلِم، وبقية بن الوليد. وهذا النوع من التدليس يشترط فيه التحديث والإخبار من المدلس إلى آخره. الرابع: تدليس العطف: وَهُوَ مثل أن يقول الرَّاوِي: حَدَّثَنَا فُلان وفلان، وَهُوَ لَمْ يَسْمَع من الثاني. الخامس تدليس السكوت: وَهُوَ كأن يقول الرَّاوِي: حَدَّثَنَا أَوْ سَمِعْتُ، ثُمَّ يسكت برهة، ثُمَّ يقول: هشام بن عروة أو الأعمش موهماً أنه سَمِعَ منهما، وليس كذلك. السادس: تدليس القطع: وَهُوَ أن يحذف الصيغة ويقتصر عَلَى قوله مثلاً: الزهري عَنْ أنس. السابع: تدليس صيغ الأداء: وَهُوَ ما يقع من الْمُحَدِّثِينَ من التعبير بالتحديث أو الإخبار عن الإجازة موهماً للسماع، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ تحمله لِذَلِكَ المروي عن طريق السَّماع. وهذه الأنواع السبعة ليست كلها مشتهرة إنما المشتهر منها والشائع الأول والثاني وعند الإطلاق يراد الأول. وهذا القسم هُوَ الَّذِي لَهُ دورٌ في الاختلافات الحديثية متوناً وأسانيد، إذ قَدْ يكشف خلال البحث بَعْدَ التنقير والتفتيش عن سقوط رجل من الإسناد وربما كَانَ هَذَا الساقط ضعيفاً أَوْ في حفظه شيء، أو لَمْ يضبط حديثه هَذَا.
Second: Tadlis of Shuyukh: It is that he mentions his shaykh's name or nickname in a way contrary to his well-known name, to obscure his affair and make it difficult to ascertain his condition. This type is lighter in ruling than the previous. In this type there is waste of the narrated-from and the narrated, and making the way of knowing their condition difficult. Then the ruling on its dislike varies according to the purpose that motivates it, for the one who practices this tadlis may be motivated by his shaykh whose description he changed being not trustworthy, or younger than the narrator from him, or late of death such that a group below him shared in hearing from him, or he narrates much from him and does not like repeating a person in one form. Third: Tadlis al-Taswiyah: It is that he narrates from his shaykh, then drops a weak narrator between two trustworthy narrators, one of whom heard from the other or met him, and narrates it with a formula that is probable between the two trustworthy ones. Among those famous for this type: al-Walid ibn Muslim and Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid. This type of tadlis requires the mudallis to use the wording of tahdith and ikhbar to the end. Fourth: Tadlis al-'Atf: It is like the narrator saying: 'So-and-so and so-and-so narrated to us,' while he did not hear from the second. Fifth: Tadlis al-Sukut: It is like the narrator saying: 'Narrated to us' or 'I heard,' then pauses a moment, then says: 'Hisham ibn 'Urwah' or 'al-A'mash' giving the impression that he heard from them, but he did not. Sixth: Tadlis al-Qat': It is that he omits the formula and restricts himself to saying, for example: 'al-Zuhri from Anas.' Seventh: Tadlis al-Siyagh al-Ada': It is what occurs from the muhaddithun of expressing with 'tahdith' or 'ikhbar' about an ijazah, giving the impression of hearing, while his transmission of that narration was not through hearing. These seven types are not all well-known; rather, the well-known and prevalent ones are the first and second, and when the term is used absolutely, the first is meant. This section is the one that has a role in hadith differences in texts and chains, for it may be uncovered during research after careful investigation and examination that a person has dropped from the chain, and perhaps this dropped person is weak or there is something in his memory, or he did not preserve this hadith.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a classification of types of tadlis (concealment in isnad) from a work on the effect of hadith differences on fiqh differences. The author lists five types (second through seventh) after presumably covering the first type earlier. The second type, Tadlis al-Shuyukh, involves altering the name of one's shaykh to obscure his identity, which may be due to various motives such as the shaykh being weak or younger. Its ruling is lighter than the first type. The third type, Tadlis al-Taswiyah, drops a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones, requiring specific wording. Famous practitioners include al-Walid ibn Muslim and Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid. The fourth type, Tadlis al-'Atf, falsely claims hearing from a second narrator by using conjunctive phrasing. The fifth type, Tadlis al-Sukut, uses a pause to imply hearing from mentioned narrators. The sixth type, Tadlis al-Qat', omits the transmission formula entirely. The seventh type, Tadlis al-Siyagh al-Ada', uses language indicating hearing for narrations actually obtained through ijazah. The author notes that only the first two types are common, with 'tadlis' generally meaning the first type. This classification is crucial for understanding variations in hadith texts and chains, as tadlis can lead to hidden weaknesses that affect legal reasoning.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): The practice of concealing or obscuring a defect in the chain of transmission by using ambiguous wording or omitting a weak link.
تدليس الشيوخ (tadlis al-shuyukh): Altering the name or kunyah of one's shaykh to make him unrecognizable.
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiyah): Dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones and using a plausible transmission formula.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of tadlis involves dropping a weak narrator from between two trustworthy ones?
A) Tadlis al-Shuyukh
B) Tadlis al-Taswiyah
C) Tadlis al-Sukut
D) Tadlis al-'Atf

Key Takeaway
The six types of tadlis each conceal a different defect; knowing them is essential for hadith criticism and, by extension, for sound fiqh derivation.

Factors Affecting Hadith Narration and Their Impact on Ikhtilaf
Explains importance of hadith and factors affecting narrator reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two key factors that led to differences in hadith transmission among narrators and explain how these factors contributed to juristic ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Preoccupation with judgeship or fiqh weakened hadith precision, causing discrepancies that later contributed to juristic differences.

This passage from an introductory chapter sets the stage for understanding why jurists differed in their rulings. It explains that not all narrators were equally reliable, even if trustworthy, because factors like holding judgeship or deep involvement in fiqh could affect their ability to preserve hadith accurately. Understanding these factors helps us appreciate the origins of ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the status of hadith
Recognize the author's assertion that hadith is the second source of legislation after the Quran, citing Quran 16:44 and 33:6. This establishes the importance of accurate transmission.
2
Describe the hadith scholars' methodology
Note the rigorous practice of writing, comparing (mu'aradah), memorizing, and discussing hadith day and night. Only those who followed this method were considered true scholars of hadith.
This sets the ideal standard; deviations from it affected reliability.
3
Identify the first factor: judgeship
Extract the argument that occupying the position of judge (qada) required extensive time and reflection, distracting from hadith review. The author cites Shareek ibn Abdullah and Muhammad ibn Abi Layla as examples whose accuracy declined after becoming judges.
The footnote explains the concept of mu'aradah for review.
4
Identify the second factor: fiqh
Note that preoccupation with fiqh (Islamic jurisprudence) also diverted attention from hadith study, leading to weaker control and potential errors. The passage begins this discussion but is cut off.
This shows that specialization in fiqh itself could impact hadith mastery.
5
Connect to ikhtilaf
Understand that these factors created variation in which hadiths were accepted and how they were transmitted. When jurists later relied on different narrations or varying levels of precision, their rulings differed, producing ikhtilaf.
This is the bridge to usul al-fiqh: differences in source material lead to differences in rulings.

الفصل التمهيدي/ بيان ماهية الاختلاف

الْحَدِيث رِوَايَة ودراية من أشرف العلوم وأجلها، بَلْ هُوَ أجلها عَلَى الإطلاق بَعْدَ العلم بالقرآن الكريم الَّذِي هُوَ أصل الدين ومنبع الطريق المستقيم، فالحديث هو المصدر الثاني للتشريع الإسلامي، بعضه يستقل بالتشريع، وكثيرٌ مِنْهُ شارح لكتاب الله تَعَالَى مبين لما جاء فِيْهِ. قَالَ تعالى ﴿ وَأَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الذِّكْرَ لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ ﴾ (١) مِن هَذَا أدرك المسلمون أهمية الحَدِيث النبوي الشريف فعانوا ما عانوا من أجل حفظ الْحَدِيث النبوي الشريف فتخلوا عَنْ كُلّ شيء أمام هَذَا الهدف العزيز الغالي، وَهُوَ حَدِيث النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ ) . وللحرص الشديد على حفظ السنة اهتم المسلمون بمذاكرة الحَدِيث ومدارسته من أجل حفظه وضبطه وإتقانه، فكان الْمُحَدِّثُوْنَ يكتبون بالنهار ويعارضون (۳) بالليل ويحفظون بالنهار ويتذاكرون بالليل. وهكذا شأن الْمُحَدِّثِينَ، ومن لَمْ يَكُنْ كذلك فلا يسمى من أهل الْحَدِيث، وأسند الإمام مُسْلِم في مقدمة صحيحه (٤) عَنْ أبي الزناد (٥) قَالَ: «أدركت بالمدينة مئة، كلهم مأمونون ما يؤخذ عَنْهُمْ الْحَدِيْث يقال: ليس من أهله» (1) .
(°).

الرُّوَاة هي
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
وهناك أمور جعلت عدداً من جهابذة الْمُحَدِّثِيْنَ لا يأخذون عن عدد كبير من أن هؤلاء الرُّوَاة كانوا يتشاغلون عَنْ الْحَدِيث والتشاغل عَنْ الْحَدِيث مدعاة لعدم ضبط الْحَدِيث وعدم إتقانه وربما كَانَ مآل ذَلِكَ إلى دخول بعض الوهم والعلل والاختلافات؛ لأن المذاكرة والمراجعة يعينان عَلَى ضبط الْحَدِيث وإتقانه. والانشغال في بعض الأمور ربما يحول دون المذاكرة والمراجعة مِمَّا يؤدي إلى عدم ضبط الروايات. ومن تِلْكَ الأمور:
أ. ولاية القضاء:
إن ولاية القضاء من الأمور الدينية المهمة والمجتمع الإسلامي بحاجة لازمة إلى هَذَا المنصب قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَلَكُمْ فِي الْقِصَاصِ حَيَوَةٌ يَتأُولِي الْأَلْبَبِ ). ولمكانة هَذِهِ الوظيفة في الإسلام وأهميتها البالغة فالأمر يستدعي من القاضي توفيراً واسعاً لمزيد من الوقت، وتهيئة جوّ ملائم للقضاء؛ لأن القضاء مسؤولية دينية ودنيوية، وَقَدْ قَالَ : «مَنْ وُليَ القَضَاءَ، أو جُعِلَ قاضياً بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فَقَدْ ذُبِحَ بِغَيرِ سكين (٢). إذن فهذه المسؤولية تستدعي تفرغاً وتفكراً ومراجعة، والحديث النبوي يحتاج كَذَلِكَ إِلَى تفرُّغ نسبي للمراجعة والمذاكرة من أجل الحفاظ على الضبط. وقد وجدنا حِيْنَ استقرأناً حال كَثِير من الرُّوَاة الَّذِيْنَ ولوا القضاء أنهم قد خفّ ضبطهم لانشغالهم بهذا المنصب الوظيفي، ومن أولئك شريك بن عَبْد الله النخعي الْقَاضِي، حدّد ابن حبّان تخليطه بَعْدَ عام خمسين ومئة حين تولى قضاء الكُوفَةِ). وكذلك مُحَمَّد بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن بن أبي لیلی) قَالَ أبو حاتم الرازي: «شغل بالقضاء فساء حفظه»).
ب. الاشتغال بالفقه:
الفقه الإسلامي يمثل الشريعة الإسلامية الغراء وذلك لما احتواه من الأصول

The Introductory Chapter / Explanation of the Nature of Difference

Hadith, in narration and understanding, is one of the noblest and most sublime sciences; rather, it is the most sublime absolutely after knowledge of the Noble Qur'an, which is the foundation of the religion and the source of the straight path. Hadith is the second source of Islamic legislation; some of it independently legislates, and much of it is an explainer of the Book of Allah, clarifying what came in it. Allah Almighty said: 'And We sent down to you the Reminder that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them' (16:44). From this, Muslims realized the importance of the noble Prophetic hadith, so they endured what they endured for the sake of preserving the noble Prophetic hadith, abandoning everything in the face of this dear and precious goal, and it is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Allah Almighty said: 'The Prophet is more worthy of the believers than themselves' (33:6). Due to intense concern for preserving the Sunnah, Muslims attended to studying hadith and reviewing it for the sake of preserving, controlling, and perfecting it. The hadith scholars would write by day and compare (3) by night, and memorize by day and discuss by night. This is the way of the hadith scholars; whoever is not like this is not called a person of hadith. Imam Muslim narrated in the introduction to his Sahih (4) from Abu al-Zinad (5) who said: 'I encountered in Medina a hundred people, all trustworthy, but hadith was not taken from them; it was said: He is not among its people.' (1) 
And Malik ibn Anas said: 'I encountered teachers in Medina, seventy and eighty years old, but hadith was not taken from them, while Ibn Shihab would come forward, younger than them, and people would crowd around him.'

There are matters that caused a number of prominent hadith scholars not to take from a large number of narrators, because these narrators were preoccupied with hadith, and preoccupation with hadith is a cause for lack of control and perfection of hadith, and perhaps the outcome of that is the entry of some delusion, defects, and differences; because discussion and review help in controlling and perfecting hadith. Preoccupation with some matters may prevent discussion and review, leading to lack of control of narrations. Among those matters are:
A. The position of judgeship: Indeed, judgeship is an important religious matter, and the Islamic society is in necessary need of this position. Allah said: 'And there is for you in legal retribution life, O people of understanding' (2:179). Due to the status of this function in Islam and its great importance, the matter requires the judge to provide ample time and prepare a suitable atmosphere for judging; because judging is a religious and worldly responsibility. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever is placed in charge of judgment, or made a judge between people, has been slaughtered without a knife.' (2) Therefore, this responsibility requires dedication, reflection, and review, and Prophetic hadith likewise requires relative dedication for review and discussion in order to preserve accuracy. We found when we surveyed the condition of many narrators who held judgeship that their accuracy became weak due to their preoccupation with this official position. Among them is Shareek ibn 'Abdullah al-Nakha'i al-Qadi; Ibn Hibban specified his confusion as after the year 150 H when he assumed the judgeship of Kufa. (3) Likewise Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla (4); Abu Hatim al-Razi said: 'He was occupied with judgeship so his memory deteriorated.' (5)
B. Preoccupation with Fiqh: Islamic fiqh represents the pure Islamic Sharia due to its inclusion of principles...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a thematic introduction explaining the nature of ikhtilaf (difference) among jurists by tracing its origins to the science of hadith. The author begins by affirming the supreme status of hadith as the second source of legislation after the Quran, citing verses to establish its authority (Quran 16:44 and 33:6). He then describes the extraordinary dedication of early hadith scholars who wrote, compared, memorized, and discussed hadith continuously. Their devotion was such that those who did not adopt this rigorous method were not considered true hadith scholars (ahl al-hadith). The author cites Imam Muslim's report from Abu al-Zinad and a saying of Imam Malik to illustrate that even trustworthy individuals were not taken from if they were not specialists in hadith.

The author then turns to the main subject: factors that caused some narrators to be unreliable, leading to discrepancies. He identifies two key factors: preoccupation with judgeship and with fiqh. For judgeship, he explains that it demands time and reflection, making it difficult to maintain hadith accuracy. He gives examples of narrators whose precision suffered after assuming judicial roles, such as Shareek ibn 'Abdullah and Muhammad ibn Abi Layla, citing scholars like Ibn Hibban and Abu Hatim al-Razi. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 38 discussing fiqh as another distracting factor. The overall purpose is to show that external preoccupations can weaken hadith mastery, leading to differences in transmitted rulings.

Key Terms
الحديث (al-hadith): The second source of legislation after the Quran; includes sayings, actions, and approvals of the Prophet.
المعارضة (al-mu'aradah): The process of a student comparing his written copy of hadith with his teacher's original to ensure accuracy.
الضبط (al-dabt): Accuracy and control in narrating hadith, maintained through continuous study and review.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason some hadith scholars did not take narrations from certain trustworthy narrators?
A) They were not from Medina
B) They were preoccupied with judgeship or fiqh
C) They were too old
D) They were not students of Imam Malik

Key Takeaway
Differences in hadith transmission, often caused by narrators' other duties, are a key source of juristic ikhtilaf, as they affect the precision of narrations that later jurists rely upon.

The Jurist's Weakness in Hadith Preservation: A Usul al-Fiqh Analysis
Analyzing the tendency of fuqaha to prioritize fiqh over hadith preservation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the distinction between a jurist's fiqh expertise and their reliability in hadith transmission, and apply the rules of jarh wa ta'dil regarding fiqh-dominated narrators.

Core Idea
Fiqh mastery does not guarantee hadith precision—jurists often prioritize ra'y over textual preservation.

This passage investigates an epistemological tension: the same scholar praised as a supreme jurist may be criticized as a weak hadith narrator. By examining the case of Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, the teacher of Abu Hanifa, and the commentaries of Ibn Rajab and Ibn Hibban, we uncover a key principle in usul al-fiqh: the methodological difference between a faqih (jurist) and a muhaddith (hadith specialist) affects how their transmissions are evaluated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central figures and their evaluations
Locate the names: Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman (the jurist), Shu'ba ibn al-Hajjaj (the hadith critic), and the commentators Ibn Abi Hatim, Abu Hatim, Ibn Rajab, and Ibn Hibban. Note the contrasting statements: Abu Ishaq al-Shaybani called Hammad the most knowledgeable in fiqh, but Shu'ba said he 'did not memorize.'
The praise is for fiqh, the criticism is for hadith preservation.
2
Understand the jarh (criticism) from hadith critics
Analyze the specific criticisms: Shu'ba's 'did not memorize' means Hammad lacked accurate retention of hadith texts and chains. Ibn Abi Hatim explains that fiqh dominated him, so he was not granted preservation of narrations. Abu Hatim says he confuses things when it comes to narrations.
The critics do not question his truthfulness, only his precision in hadith.
3
Summarize the general principle formulated by later scholars
Ibn Rajab states that jurists devoted to opinion (ra'y) hardly preserve hadith properly, making errors in chains and texts, and narrate by meaning. Ibn Hibban adds that their preoccupation is with mastering the text, not the chain, so their 'raising' (marfu') reports are only accepted if written.
This principle explains why jurist-narrators are evaluated differently from pure muhaddithun.
4
Apply this principle to understand ikhtilaf among fuqaha
Recognize that differing rulings among schools can sometimes be traced back to reliance on hadiths transmitted by jurists who may have altered wording or confused chains. This is one source of legitimate ikhtilaf.
It also underscores why the Hanafi school often uses other sources (qiyas, istihsan) when hadith evidence is weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَد وجدنا بعض جهابذة الْحَدِيث تَكَلَّمَ في بعض الرُّوَاةِ لِقَصْرِ تهممهم الفقه، ومن أولئك حماد بن أبي سليمان من كبار الفقهاء وشيخ أبي حَنِيفَة النعمان قَالَ عَنْهُ أبو إسحاق الشيباني: «ما رأيت أحداً أفقه من حماد). ومع هَذَا فَقَدْ نقل عَبْد الرَّحْمن بن أبي حاتم عَنْ أمير المؤمنين في الْحَدِيث شعبة بن الحجاج قوله: «كَانَ حماد يعني: ابن أبي سليمان - لا يحفظ». ثُمَّ عقب ابن أبي حاتم عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ: «يعني: إن الغالب عَلَيْهِ الفقه وإنه لَمْ يرزق حفظ الآثار». وَقَالَ أبو حاتم: «هُوَ صدوق ولا يحتج بحديثه، هُوَ مستقيم في الفقه، وإذا جاء الآثار شوّش». هنا وضع علماء الجرح والتعديل قواعد في أنّ الفقهاء غَيْرِ الْمُحَدِّثِيْنَ يغلب عليهم الفقه دون حفظ المتون، قَالَ ابن رجب الحنبلي: «الفقهاء المعتنون بالرأي حَتَّى يغلب عليهم الاشتغال به، لا يكادون يحفظون الْحَدِيث كَمَا ينبغي، ولا يقيمون أسانيده ولا متونه، ويخطئون في حفظ الأسانيد كثيراً، ويروون المتون بالمعنى، ويخالفون الحفاظ في ألفاظه). وابن رجب مسبوق بهذا التنظير فَقَدْ قَالَ ابن حبان: «الفقهاء الغالب عليهم حفظ المتون وأحكامها وأداؤها بالمعنى دون حفظ الأسانيد وأسماء الْمُحَدِّثِيْنَ، فإذا رفع محدث خبراً، وَكَانَ الغالب عَلَيْهِ الفقه، لم أقبل رفعه إلا من كتابه؛ لأنه لا يعلم المسند من المرسل، ولا الموقوف من المنقطع، وإنما همته إحكام المثن فَقَط
And we have found some hadith giants speaking about some narrators due to their preoccupation with fiqh. Among them is Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, one of the great jurists and the teacher of Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man. Abu Ishaq al-Shaybani said about him: 'I have not seen anyone more knowledgeable in fiqh than Hammad.' Yet despite this, ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim narrated from the Commander of the Faithful in Hadith, Shu'ba ibn al-Hajjaj, his statement: 'Hammad – meaning Ibn Abi Sulayman – did not memorize.' Then Ibn Abi Hatim commented on that, saying: 'That is, fiqh dominated him, and he was not granted the preservation of narrations.' Abu Hatim said: 'He is truthful, but his hadith is not adduced as proof. He is sound in fiqh, but when it comes to narrations, he confuses things.' Here the scholars of jarh wa ta'dil established rules that jurists who are not hadith specialists are dominated by fiqh to the neglect of preserving texts. Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali said: 'The jurists who are devoted to opinion until it dominates their preoccupation, they hardly preserve hadith as they should, nor do they establish its chains or texts. They often make mistakes in preserving chains, narrate texts by meaning, and contradict the memorizers in wording.' Ibn Rajab was preceded in this theorization, for Ibn Hibban said: 'The jurists are mostly adept at preserving texts and their rulings and conveying them by meaning, without preserving chains and the names of hadith transmitters. So if a hadith transmitter raises a report and fiqh dominates him, I do not accept his raising except from his book, because he does not know the connected from the disconnected, nor the stopped from the broken, and his only concern is mastering the text.'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage examines the relationship between fiqh and hadith memorization, specifically the tendency of jurists to prioritize juristic reasoning (ra'y) over precise hadith preservation. The author provides examples: Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, a leading jurist and teacher of Abu Hanifa, was praised for his fiqh but criticized by hadith critics like Shu'ba for weak hadith memorization. This illustrates that expertise in fiqh does not guarantee accuracy in hadith transmission. The author then cites Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali and Ibn Hibban to establish a general principle: jurists who focus on legal reasoning often neglect precise hadith memorization, narrating by meaning and making errors in chains and wording. This explains one source of ikhtilaf among jurists: reliance on hadith relayed by those who prioritize fiqh over rigorous hadith discipline.

Key Terms
الجَرْحُ وَالتَّعْدِيل (al-jarḥ wa al-ta‘dīl): The science of criticizing and validating hadith narrators.
الفقهاء (al-fuqahā’): Jurists who specialize in deriving legal rulings from textual sources.
المحدثون (al-muḥaddithūn): Hadith specialists focused on preserving chains and texts accurately.
رفع الخبر (raf‘ al-khabar): The action of ascribing a report to the Prophet (marfu‘).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hibban, why might a jurist's 'raising' of a hadith be rejected without a written source?
A) Because jurists are always unreliable in hadith.
B) Because fiqh-dominated narrators do not distinguish connected from disconnected chains.
C) Because they only care about fiqh, not isnad.
D) Because they never write down their narrations.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh expertise does not guarantee hadith precision; jurist-narrators must be evaluated separately for their transmission reliability, often requiring written verification.

Piety Alone Does Not Guarantee Hadith Reliability
Discussing how devotional preoccupation leads to errors in hadith narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition of dabt (precision) and identify why excessive worship without hadith study can undermine a narrator's reliability.

Core Idea
Piety alone does not make a narrator reliable; precision (dabt) is essential, and worship without hadith study can cause errors.

This passage explores a critical distinction in hadith criticism: the difference between a narrator's righteousness (adala) and their precision (dabt). While piety is necessary, it is not sufficient. The passage illustrates how some devout individuals, due to their preoccupation with worship, neglected the review and repetition needed to preserve hadith accurately, leading to errors. This lesson will unpack the Hanafi principle that a narrator must possess both adala and dabt, and that excessive devotion without scholarly discipline can compromise reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
The passage states that preoccupation with worship leads to errors in hadith narration. What is the underlying cause? It is the lack of follow-up, review, and repetition needed to preserve narrations.
This highlights that hadith preservation requires active scholarly effort, not just piety.
2
Locate the Principle
Ibn Rajab's rule: 'The righteous who are not scholars – illusion and error dominate their hadith.' What does this distinguish between? It distinguishes between being righteous (adala) and being knowledgeable in hadith (dabt).
This is a foundational principle in hadith criticism.
3
Examine the Evidence
Imam Malik's practice: He refused to take hadith from pious elders who did not know what they narrated. Why? Because they lacked awareness of their own narrations, indicating lack of dabt.
Malik’s action shows the practical application of this principle.
4
Extract the Four Categories
List the four types from whom Malik said knowledge should not be taken: the foolish, the liar, the innovator calling to desires, and the pious ignorant who does not know what he narrates.
Each category has a specific flaw that violates either adala or dabt.
5
Apply to Hanafi Usul
How does this passage inform the Hanafi condition of dabt? A narrator must be not only upright but also meticulous. Excessive worship without scholarly training can harm dabt, thus making such narrators unacceptable.
In Hanafi usul, dabt is a separate condition from adala, and this passage reinforces its importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج. الاشتغال بالعبادة: سبق لنا أن ذكرنا مراراً أن الْحَدِيث النبوي يحتاج إلى متابعة ومذاكرة وتكرار من أجل حفظ الروايات وصونها من الخطأ والزيادة والنقص وأن ترك ذَلِكَ يؤول في نهاية المطاف إلى عدم ضبط الأحاديث ودخول الوهم والاختلاف فِيْهَا فِيْمَا بعد. ومن الأمور الَّتِي حَدَتْ ببعض الْمُحَدِّثِينَ للتقصير في ضبط مروياتهم انشغال بعضهم بالعبادة وصرف غالب أوقاتهم بِذَلِكَ دون متابعة ضبط رواياتهم. وَقَدْ أصل ابن رجب ذَلِكَ قاعدة فَقَالَ: «الصالحون غَيْر العلماء يغلب على حديثهم الوهم والغلط». والحافظ ابن رجب إنما أخذ ذَلِكَ من أقوال أئمة هَذَا الشأن العارفين بعلله الغواصين في معانيه وأسراره قَالَ نجم العلماء مالك بن أنس: أدركت بهذا البلد - يعني الْمَدِينَة - مشيخة لَهُمْ فضل وصلاح وعبادة يحدّثون، ما سَمِعْتُ من واحد مِنْهُمْ حديثاً قطُّ، فقيل لَهُ: وَلِمَ يا أبا عَبْد الله؟ قَالَ: لَمْ يكونوا يعرفون ما يحدّثون». وَقَالَ أَيْضاً: «لا يؤخذ العلم من أربعة، ويؤخذ ممن سوى ذَلِكَ، لا يؤخذ من سفيه مُعلن بالسفه وإن كَانَ أروى الناس، ولا يؤخذ من كذاب يكذب في أحاديث الناس، إذا جرب ذَلِكَ عَلَيْهِ، وإن كَانَ لا يُتَّهَمُ أن يكذب عَلَى رَسُول الله ، ولا من صاحب هوى يدعو الناس إلى هواه، ولا من شيخ لَهُ فضل وعبادة إذا كَانَ لا يعرف ما يحدث بِهِ».
C. Devotion to Worship: We have already mentioned repeatedly that prophetic hadith requires follow-up, review, and repetition in order to preserve narrations and safeguard them from error, addition, and omission, and that abandoning that ultimately leads to lack of precision in hadith and the entry of illusion and disagreement in them later. Among the matters that prompted some hadith transmitters to fall short in preserving their narrations was some of them being occupied with worship and spending most of their time on that without following up on preserving their narrations. Ibn Rajab established this as a principle and said: 'The righteous who are not scholars – illusion and error dominate their hadith.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Rajab took that from the statements of the imams of this field who know its defects and dive into its meanings and secrets. The star of the scholars, Malik ibn Anas, said: 'I encountered in this city – meaning Madinah – elders who had virtue, righteousness, and worship and would narrate hadith. I never heard a single hadith from any of them.' So it was said to him: 'Why, O Abu Abdullah?' He said: 'They did not know what they were narrating.' And he also said: 'Knowledge is not taken from four types, and it is taken from others besides them. It is not taken from a foolish person who openly acts foolishly, even if he is the most narrating of people. It is not taken from a liar who lies in people's talk, once that is experienced from him, even if he is not accused of lying about the Messenger of Allah. Nor from a person of desires who calls people to his desires. Nor from a shaykh who has virtue and worship if he does not know what he is narrating.'
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of factors that weaken hadith transmission. It highlights that excessive devotion to worship (without complementary focus on hadith science) leads to illusion (wahm) and error in narration. Ibn Rajab states that righteous non-scholars are prone to errors in hadith. Imam Malik’s practice illustrates this: despite the piety of many elders in Madinah, he refrained from taking hadith from them because they lacked knowledge of what they narrated. Malik lists four categories from whom knowledge should not be taken: the openly foolish (even if prolific), the liar (even if not lying about the Prophet), the innovator (da’i to his desires), and the pious ignorant (who does not know what he transmits). This underscores that piety alone does not guarantee reliable transmission; hadith mastery is essential.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): Illusion or error in hadith transmission due to lack of precision.
صاحب هوى (ṣāḥib hawan): A person following desires, especially bid‘ah, who calls others to it.
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in narration; the ability to accurately memorize and transmit hadith without error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four types from whom knowledge is not to be taken?
A) A foolish person who openly acts foolishly.
B) A liar who lies in people's talk.
C) A person of desires who calls people to his desires.
D) A righteous scholar who is precise in narration.

Key Takeaway
Piety (adala) is necessary but not sufficient for hadith reliability; precision (dabt) is equally essential, and excessive worship without scholarly discipline can undermine dabt.

Sanad and Isnad: Definitions and Significance
Defining sanad and isnad with their importance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sanad and isnad terminologically, distinguish between them, and explain their importance in preserving the integrity of hadith.

Core Idea
Isnad is the chain that authenticates hadith; without it, the religion would be vulnerable to fabrication.

This passage lays the foundational terminology for understanding how hadiths are transmitted and authenticated. The terms 'sanad' and 'isnad' are central to this process. The author not only defines them but also highlights the unique blessing of isnad for this Ummah, setting the stage for analyzing how differences in chains lead to juristic differences. Mastering these definitions is crucial for any student of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lexical definition of isnad
Find the definition given by al-Jawhari at the beginning of the passage: 'Isnad in hadith is attributing it to its speaker.'
This is the basic linguistic meaning before terminological refinement.
2
Understand the terminological definitions
Read the definitions of sanad ('informing about the path of the matn') and isnad ('narrating the path of the matn'). Note al-Subki's preference for 'path of the matn' over 'way of the matn'.
The precise wording matters in technical definitions.
3
Compare sanad and isnad usage
Analyze the statements that sanad and isnad are used interchangeably, but isnad is more general because it also includes the act of attribution.
This nuance is important for precise application.
4
Analyze the importance of isnad
Examine the quotes from Ibn al-Muzaffar, Abu Ali al-Jiyyani, and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi on how isnad distinguishes this Ummah and protects the religion from corruption.
This shows why isnad is indispensable for the science of hadith.

ب. تعريف السند اصطلاحاً:
السند: هُوَ الإخبار عن طريق الْمَتْن(۳).
قال السيوطي: «والحد المذكور للسند ذكره ابن الحاجب) في مختصره)، قَالَ القاضي تاج الدين السبكي (٦) في شرحه: وعندي لَوْ قَالَ: طريق الْمَتْنِ، كَانَ أولى»). وأما الإسناد فهو حكاية طريق المثن (۸).

أهمية الإسناد :
إن الله شرف هَذِهِ الأمة بشرف الإسناد، وَمَنَّ عَلَيْهَا بسلسلة الإسناد واتصاله، فهو خصيصة فاضلة لهذه الأمة وليس لغيرها من الأمم السابقة، وَقَد أسند الْخَطِيْب في كتاب " شرف أصحاب الْحَدِيث (۲) إلى مُحَمَّد بن حاتم بن المظفر قَالَ: «إنّ الله أَكْرَمَ هَذِهِ الأمة وشرفها وفضلها بالإسناد، وليس لأحد من الأمم كلها، قديمهم وحديثهم إسناد، وإنما هي صحف في أيديهم وَقَدْ خلطوا بكتبهم أخبارهم، وليس عندهم تمييز بَيْنَ ما نزل من التوراة والإنجيل مِمَّا جاءهم بِهِ أنبياؤهم، وتمييز بين ما ألحقوه بكتبهم من الأخبار الَّتِي أخذوا عن غير الثقات. وهذه الأمة إنما تنص الْحَدِيث من الثقة المعروف في زمانه المشهور بالصدق والأمانة عن مثله حَتَّى تتناهى أخبارهم، ثُمَّ يبحثون أشد البحث حَتَّى يعرفوا الأحفظ فالأحفظ، والأضبط فالأضبط والأطول مجالسةٌ لِمَنْ فوقه ممن كَانَ أقل مجالسة. ثُمَّ يكتبون الْحَدِيث من عشرين وجهاً وأكثر حَتَّى يهذبوه من الغلط والزلل ويضبطوا حروفه ويعدوه عداً. فهذا من أعظم نعم تَعَالَى عَلَى هَذِهِ الأمة». وَقَالَ أبو علي الجياني(۳): «خص الله تَعَالَى هَذِهِ الأمة بثلاثة أشياء لَمْ يعطها مَنْ قَبْلَهَا مِنَ الأمم الإسناد، والأنساب، والإعراب»(4). وَقَالَ الْحَاكِم النيسابوري: «فلولا الإسناد وطلب هَذِهِ الطائفة له، وكثرة مواظبتهم عَلَى حفظه لدرس منار الإسلام، ولتمكن أهل الإلحاد والبدع فِيْهِ بوضع الأحاديث، وقلب الأسانيد، فإنَّ الأخبار إذا تعرت عن وجود الأسانيد فِيهَا كانت مبتراً، كَمَا حَدَّثَنَا
Chapter One: Difference in the Chain. Al-Jawhari said: 'Isnad in hadith is attributing it to its speaker.' B. Definition of sanad terminologically: Al-Sanad: It is informing about the path of the text. Al-Suyuti said: 'The aforementioned definition of sanad was mentioned by Ibn al-Hajib in his Mukhtasar.' Al-Qadi Taj al-Din al-Subki said in his commentary: 'In my view, if he had said: the path of the text, it would have been better.' As for al-isnad, it is the narration of the path of the text. And it appears that sanad and isnad have the same meaning, because they are close in meaning to each other. Badr al-Din ibn Jama'ah said: 'The muhaddithun use sanad and isnad for one thing.' However, isnad is more general than sanad; for isnad is applied to the chain of narrators leading to the text. In summary: what is meant by sanad or isnad here is the chain of narrators who transmitted the hadith one from another, until they reach its speaker. The importance of isnad: Indeed Allah honored this Ummah with the honor of isnad, and bestowed upon it the chain of isnad and its continuity. It is a virtuous characteristic for this Ummah, not for any previous nations. Al-Khatib narrated in his book 'Sharaf Ashab al-Hadith' from Muhammad ibn Hatim ibn al-Muzaffar who said: 'Indeed Allah honored this Ummah and favored it with isnad. None of the previous or later nations have isnad. They only have scrolls in their hands, and they have mixed their books with their stories, and they have no distinction between what was revealed in the Torah and the Gospel from what their prophets brought them, and between what they added to their books from stories taken from unreliable sources. This Ummah only takes hadith from a reliable person known in his time for truthfulness and trustworthiness, from someone like him, until their reports reach them. Then they search most intensely until they know the more reliable and more precise, and the one who sat longer with his teacher than one who sat less. Then they write the hadith from twenty or more aspects until they remove it from error and slip, and they preserve its letters and count it. This is among the greatest blessings of Allah upon this Ummah.' Abu Ali al-Jiyyani said: 'Allah distinguished this Ummah with three things not given to previous nations: isnad, genealogy, and grammar.' Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi said: 'Were it not for isnad and this group's pursuit of it and their abundant perseverance in preserving it, the beacon of Islam would have been extinguished, and the people of heresy and innovation would have been able to insert fabricated hadiths and alter chains. For reports, when devoid of chains, become severed.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a definition and importance section from a work on the effect of differences in chains and texts on juristic differences. It opens by defining the technical term 'sanad' and 'isnad' according to hadith scholars. The author cites al-Jawhari's lexical definition of isnad as attributing a hadith to its speaker. Then the terminological definition: sanad is informing about the path of the matn (text). There is a discussion about the precise wording: al-Subki preferred saying 'path of the matn' over 'way of the matn'. The author concludes that sanad and isnad are used interchangeably by muhaddithun, but isnad is more comprehensive because it also means the act of attribution. The summary clarifies that for this book, both refer to the chain of narrators transmitting the hadith successively to its origin. The second part extols the importance of isnad as a unique blessing for this Ummah, quoting three scholars: Ibn al-Muzaffar emphasizes that no previous nation had a systematic chain of transmission; Abu Ali al-Jiyyani lists isnad, genealogy, and grammar as three unique gifts; and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi warns that without isnad, the religion would be vulnerable to fabrication. This foundation is crucial for understanding how juristic differences can arise from variations in chains and texts.

Key Terms
السند (al-sanad): The chain of transmitters that leads to the text of the hadith, i.e. the path of reporting the matn.
الإسناد (al-isnad): Attributing the hadith to its speaker, or the chain of narrators; broader than sanad as it includes the act of attribution.
المتن (al-matn): The text of the hadith, i.e. the content conveyed by the chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary function of isnad in hadith?
A) To list the names of narrators without verification.
B) To attribute the hadith to its speaker through a verified chain of narrators.
C) To provide commentary on the meaning of the hadith.
D) To determine the legal ruling from the hadith.

Key Takeaway
Sanad/isnad is the chain of narrators that authenticates hadith; its preservation is a unique blessing of this Ummah.

How Variations in Sanad and Matn Generate Fiqh Ikhtilaf
Presents two narrations of Prophet's ring hadith with different chains and texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify differences in sanad and matn across hadith narrations and explain how they lead to juristic disagreement in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Two narrations of the same event can differ in both chain and content — these differences are a primary source of fiqh ikhtilaf.

The passage you are about to read presents two versions of a well-known hadith about the Prophet's ring. At first glance, they seem to describe the same event, but a closer look reveals differences in the chain of narrators (sanad) and in the text (matn). Such variations are not merely historical curiosities; they form the raw material for juristic disagreement (ikhtilaf) among scholars. In this lesson, we will dissect these two narrations to see how even a small textual addition can lead to different rulings, and how the Hanafi school approaches such divergences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two chains
Name the two chains: one via 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Suhayb from Anas, the other via Qatadah from Anas. Note that both go back to Anas ibn Malik, but through different intermediate narrators.
The difference in sanad is a key factor in how scholars weigh narrations.
2
Compare the matn
Read the texts carefully: the first narration includes a prohibition ('let no one engrave on his ring'), while the second provides a reason (to seal letters to the Romans). Identify what is unique to each version.
The additional prohibition in the first version could have legal implications.
3
Connect to fiqh ikhtilaf
Consider how each text could be used to derive a ruling. The first might imply that copying the Prophet's ring inscription is forbidden, while the second might simply permit the use of a ring for sealing without addressing copying.
This is a classic example of how a small textual difference can lead to differing legal opinions.
4
Apply the Hanafi approach
Hanafi usul gives weight to both sanad and matn. The school would evaluate the reliability of each chain and the context of each text. In practice, Hanafis may favor the version that is more widely transmitted or that aligns with other principles, such as istihsan.
Understanding how Hanafi scholars prioritize narrations is essential for deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند. ورواه عبد العزيز بن صهيب عن أنس بن مالك: أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخذ خاتماً من فضة ونقش فيه: محمد رسول الله، وقال: إني اتخذت خاتماً ورق ونقشت فيه: محمد رسول الله فلا ينقشن أحد على نقشه. ورواه قتادة عن أنس بن مالك، قال: لما أراد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يكتب إلى الروم، قيل له: إنهم لن يقرؤا كتابك إذا لم يكن مختوماً، فاتخذ خاتماً من فضة ونقشه: محمد رسول الله، فكأنما أنظر إلى بياضه في يده.
Chapter One: Difference in the Chain. And 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Suhayb narrated from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took a ring of silver and engraved on it: Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'I have taken a ring of silver and engraved on it: Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. So let no one engrave (the same) on his ring.' And Qatadah narrated from Anas ibn Malik, who said: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) wanted to write to the Romans, it was said to him: They will not read your letter if it is not sealed. So he took a ring of silver and engraved on it: Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. It is as if I can see its whiteness in his hand.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents two narrations of the hadith concerning the Prophet's ring. The first narration, via 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Suhayb, includes a prohibition against others engraving the same inscription on their rings. The second narration, via Qatadah, provides the context: the ring was made for sealing letters to the Romans. The difference in the chain (isnad) accompanies a difference in the text (matn). Such variations are a key source of juristic disagreement (ikhtilaf) among scholars. For instance, the first text may imply that copying the Prophet's ring inscription is forbidden, while the second text focuses on the purpose of the ring for sealing. Hanafi scholars would consider both narrations when deriving rulings on rings, but the authentic and accepted version in the madhhab may vary.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith.
متن (matn): The text or content of the hadith.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement among scholars in a matter of fiqh or usul, often traced to diverging hadith narrations.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqah): An addition to the text made by a trustworthy narrator, which Hanafis generally accept if it does not contradict stronger evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between the two narrations of the Prophet's ring hadith given in this passage?
A) One mentions the ring was made of silver, the other of gold.
B) One includes a prohibition against copying the inscription, the other provides the reason for making the ring.
C) One says the ring was worn on the right hand, the other on the left.
D) One is narrated by Anas, the other by Qatadah.

Key Takeaway
Differences in both sanad and matn between narrations of the same event are a fundamental source of fiqh ikhtilaf, and Hanafi usul provides tools to evaluate and reconcile them.
