Idraj in the Middle: The Case of the Added Testicles and Pubes
Analysis of a documented case of idraj in the middle of a hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an instance of idraj fi al-wasat (interpolation in the middle) in a hadith and explain how hadith scholars detect it by comparing chains.

Core Idea
A narrator's addition in the middle of a hadith distorts the Prophetic text; critics identify it by cross‑checking narrator statements.

In hadith criticism, not every word in a marfu‘ report necessarily comes from the Prophet. One type of disruption is idraj fi al‑wasat, where a narrator inserts an explanatory phrase into the middle of the hadith. This lesson examines a documented case from al‑Daraqutni’s Sunan, where the words ‘or his two testicles or his pubes’ were added to a hadith about touching private parts. We will see how scholars like al‑Daraqutni and al‑Khatib al‑Baghdadi identified the interpolation and traced it back to the narrator’s teacher, Urwah ibn al‑Zubayr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its apparent wording
Read the hadith as transmitted: ‘Whoever touches his penis, or his two testicles, or his pubes, let him perform wudu’. Note the three items listed.
2
Mark the potentially interpolated phrase
Focus on the phrase ‘or his two testicles, or his pubes’. Ask: is this phrase present in other transmissions?
Al‑Daraqutni and al‑Khatib point to this specific phrase as the interpolation.
3
Examine the chain and narrator roles
The chain is: Basrah bint Safwan → Urwah ibn al‑Zubayr → Hisham ibn Urwah → Abd al‑Hamid ibn Ja‘far → al‑Daraqutni. Identify which narrator is known to have added commentary.
Abd al‑Hamid ibn Ja‘far is identified as the one who inserted the words.
4
Apply the critical method for idraj
Compare this narration with other transmissions of the same hadith. If the phrase appears only in this chain, it is suspect. Check if the phrase is known as a statement of a narrator (e.g., Urwah).
Al‑Daraqutni states: ‘The preserved [version] is that this is from the statement of Urwah, not marfu‘.’
5
Determine the correct marfu‘ text
After removing the interpolation, the authentic marfu‘ text is: ‘Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu’. The addition is not from the Prophet.
This distinction affects the fiqh ruling: the hadith is used as dalil that touching the penis breaks wudu; the added body parts are not in the original hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال ما وقع الإدراج في وسطه ما رواه الدارقطني في "سننه" من طريق عبد الحميد بن جعفر عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن بسرة بنت صفوان قالت: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «من مس ذكره، أو أنثييه أو رفعه فليتوضأ». فقد أدرج عبد الحميد بن جعفر ذكر «الأنثيين والرفغ» في الحديث المرفوع، قال الدارقطني: والمحفوظ أن ذلك من قول عروة غير مرفوع. وقال الخطيب البغدادي: (وذكر الأنثيين والرفغين ليس من كلام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وإنما من قول عروة بن الزبير فأدرجه الراوي في متن الحديث وقد بين ذلك حماد بن
An example of what occurred of idraj in the middle is what al-Daraqutni narrated in his 'Sunan' via the chain of Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far from Hisham ibn Urwah, from his father, from Basrah bint Safwan who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever touches his penis, or his two testicles, or his pubes, let him perform wudu'.' Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far inserted the mention of 'the two testicles and the pubes' into the marfu' hadith. Al-Daraqutni said: What is preserved is that this is from the statement of Urwah, not marfu'. And al-Khatib al-Baghdadi said: 'The mention of the two testicles and the pubes is not from the speech of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); rather it is from the statement of Urwah ibn al-Zubayr, so the narrator inserted it into the text of the hadith. Hammad ibn... has clarified that.'

Commentary
This passage presents a documented case of idraj (interpolation) occurring in the middle of a hadith. The hadith is about touching the private parts necessitating wudu. The narrator Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far added the words 'or his two testicles or his pubes' to the Prophetic statement. Both al-Daraqutni and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi clarify that these additional words are actually from Urwah ibn al-Zubayr, the father of Hisham, and were mistakenly inserted into the marfu' text. This example illustrates the critical work of hadith scholars in identifying interpolations and preserving the exact wording of the Prophet. The lesson highlights the importance of distinguishing the narrator's commentary from the Prophetic text.

Key Terms
الإدراج في الوسط (al-idraj fi al-wasat): Interpolation that occurs in the middle of a hadith, where a narrator inserts his own or another's words into the Prophetic text.
الرفغ (al-rafgh): The pubic region or the area above the genitals.
مرفوع (marfu'): A hadith attributed directly to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Idraj in the Middle: The Hadith of Busra
Textual analysis of idraj in the Busra hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify idraj in a hadith text, distinguish the inserted part from the original, and explain its impact on istinbat (derivation of rulings).

Core Idea
A single narrator's insertion can change a hadith; only careful comparison of chains reveals the authentic prophetic words.

Idraj (insertion) is a subtle error in hadith transmission where a narrator adds his own words into the prophetic text. This lesson examines a classic example from the hadith of Busra on ablution after touching the genitals. Understanding idraj is essential for reliable istinbat, as it directly affects the authenticity of proof texts used in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the phenomenon of idraj
Idraj occurs when a narrator mistakenly includes his own or another's speech into the hadith, attributing it to the Prophet. It can happen at the beginning, middle, or end of the hadith.
Idraj in the middle is very rare, as noted by Ibn Hajar.
2
Examine the Busra hadith
Al-Daraqutni narrates via Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far: 'Whoever touches his penis, or his testicles, or his pubic area, let him perform ablution.' Note the extra words: 'or his testicles or his pubic area.'
3
Identify the inserted words
Al-Daraqutni and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi state that the words 'testicles' and 'pubic area' are from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr, not the Prophet. Compare with narrations from other students of Hisham who omit these words.
The reliable narrators only mention 'penis'.
4
Compare multiple chains
Seven narrators from Hisham restrict the hadith to 'penis' only. This consistency shows that Abdul Hamid's version is mudraj.
The method of comparing chains helps detect idraj.
5
Apply to Hanafi istinbat
The Hanafi school relies on the authentic version (only 'penis') to derive the ruling that touching the penis necessitates wudu, but touching testicles or pubic area does not (based on this hadith alone).
This demonstrates how hadith criticism directly affects fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن

فهؤلاء خمسة عشر نفساً من أصحاب شعبة اتفقوا عَلَى جعل قوله: «أسبغوا الوضوء» من كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة، في حين أخطأ أبو قطن وشبابة فأدرجاه في الْحَدِيث (۱). وهذا القسم أقل الأقسام وروداً، وَهُوَ قليل جداً، الأمر الذي دفع الحافظ ابن لأن يقول: وفتشت ما جمعه الْخَطِيب في المدرج، ومقدار ما زدت عليه مِنْهُ فَلَمْ أجد له مثالاً آخر إلا ما جاء في بعض طرق حَدِيث بسرة الآتي من رواية مُحَمَّد بن دينار ()، عن هشام بن حسان»(۳). وهذا يناقض قول ابن الجلال المحلي وَهُوَ يتحدث عن الإدراج في أول الْحَدِيْثِ: «وَهُوَ أكثر مِمَّا في وسطه؛ لأن الرَّاوِي يقول كلاماً يريد أن يستدل عليه بالحديث فيأتي بلا فصل، فيتوهم أن الكل حديث»(4).

ومثال ما وقع الإدراج في وسطه ما رَوَاهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِي في " سننه " من طريق عبد الحميد بن جعفر عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن بسرة بنت صفوان قالت: سَمِعْتُ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «مَنْ مَسَ ذَكَرَهُ، أو أنثييه أو رفعه فليتوضأ». فَقَدْ أدرج عَبْد الحميد بن جعفر ذكر «الأنثيين والرفغ في الْحَدِيث المرفوع، قال الدَّارَقُطْني: والمحفوظ أن ذَلِكَ من قول عروة غير مرفوع»).

وَقَالَ الْخَطِيْب البغدادي: (وذكر الأنثيين والرفغين ليس من كلام رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وإنما من قول عروة بن الزبير فأدرجه الرَّاوِي في متن الْحَدِيث وَقَدْ بَين ذَلِكَ حماد بن زيد وأيوب السختياني في روايتهما عن هشام).

فوهم عبد الحميد بن جعفر وأدرج كلام عروة في الحديث، في حين اقتصر من أصحاب هشام عَلَى ذكر «الذكر»، وهم:

.١ أبو أسامة حماد بن أسامة، وروايته عِنْدَ الترمذي () ، وابن خزيمة)، وابن الجارود) والطبراني).

٢. إِسْمَاعِيل بن عياش، عِنْدَ الدَّارَ قُطْنِي).

. أنس بن عياض (۳)، عِنْدَ البيهقي (1) . أيوب السختياني، وسيأتي التفصيل في طريقه.

ه حماد بن زيد، عِنْدَ الدَّارَ قُطني ()، والطبراني (١)، والحاكم (۱۱)، والخطيب ()

٦. حماد بن سلمة، عِنْدَ الطبراني . ربيعة بن عثمان (۱٤)، عِنْدَ ابن حبان (۱۹)، والطبراني (١٦)، والحاكم (١٧).
Chapter Three / Difference in Chain and Text

These fifteen companions of Shu'ba agreed on making his statement: 'Perform ablution thoroughly' from the speech of Abu Hurayra, while Abu Qatan and Shababa erred and inserted it into the hadith (1). This category is the least frequent, and it is very rare, which led al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar to say: I searched what al-Khatib collected in al-Mudraj, and the amount I added to it, and I did not find another example except what came in some chains of the hadith of Busra via the narration of Muhammad ibn Dinar, from Hisham ibn Hassan (3). This contradicts the statement of Ibn al-Jalal al-Mahalli when he speaks about insertion at the beginning of the hadith: 'It is more frequent than in the middle, because the narrator says something intending to use the hadith as evidence, so he brings it without separation, and it is thought that all is hadith' (4).

An example of insertion in the middle is what al-Daraqutni narrated in his Sunan via Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far, from Hisham ibn Urwa, from his father, from Busra bint Safwan who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Whoever touches his penis, or his testicles, or his pubic area, let him perform ablution.' Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far inserted the mention of 'the testicles and the pubic area' into the marfu' hadith. Al-Daraqutni said: The preserved version is that this is from the statement of Urwa, not marfu' (6).

Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi said: The mention of the testicles and the pubic area is not from the speech of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), but rather from the statement of Urwa ibn al-Zubayr, so the narrator inserted it into the text of the hadith. This was clarified by Hammad ibn Zaid and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani in their narrations from Hisham.

Thus Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far erred and inserted the statement of Urwa into the hadith, while the companions of Hisham restricted themselves to mentioning 'the penis' only, and they are:

1. Abu Usama Hammad ibn Usama, his narration is with al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Khuzayma, Ibn al-Jarud, and al-Tabarani.

2. Isma'il ibn Ayyash, with al-Daraqutni.

3. Anas ibn Iyad, with al-Bayhaqi.
4. Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, the detail will come in his path.

5. Hammad ibn Zaid, with al-Daraqutni, al-Tabarani, al-Hakim, and al-Khatib.

6. Hammad ibn Salama, with al-Tabarani.
7. Rabi'a ibn Uthman, with Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and al-Hakim.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage discusses the phenomenon of idraj (insertion) in the middle of a hadith, providing a concrete example from the hadith of Busra regarding ablution after touching the genitals. The author first notes that idraj in the middle is much rarer than at the beginning, citing Ibn Hajar's difficulty in finding another example besides this one. He then presents the hadith as narrated by al-Daraqutni via Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far, where the words 'or his testicles or his pubic area' are included in the marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) version. However, the preserved and correct version is that these words are from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr's own commentary, not from the Prophet. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirms this, noting that reliable narrators like Hammad ibn Zaid and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani narrated from Hisham without the insertion. The text then lists seven narrators from among the students of Hisham who restricted the hadith to only mentioning 'the penis', thereby preserving the original wording. This example illustrates how a single narrator's mistake in insertion can create a variant text, potentially affecting juristic rulings, as the Hanafi school relies on the version without the extra words for the ruling on wudu from touching the genitals.

Key Terms
إدراج (idraj): Inserting a narrator's own words into the hadith text, mistakenly attributing them to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are from the narrator Abdul Hamid ibn Ja'far.
B) They are from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr, not the Prophet.
C) They are from Hisham ibn Urwa.
D) They are from Busra herself.

Key Takeaway
Detecting idraj is crucial for reliable istinbat; the Hanafi school uses the more authentic version of the Busra hadith to rule that touching the penis (alone) necessitates wudu.

Identifying Idraj Through Narrator Comparison
Listing narrators who preserved the correct matn without interpolation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify idraj (interpolation) in a hadith matn by comparing narrations of reliable transmitters and explain its impact on legal derivation.

Core Idea
Idraj corrupts hadith; the correct matn is preserved by the thiqat who transmitted only 'al-dhikr'.

In hadith criticism, one common error is 'idraj'—when a narrator inadvertently inserts explanatory words into the hadith text, conflating it with the saying of a Companion. This passage lists fourteen reliable narrators who all transmitted a specific hadith from Hisham without such interpolation, confining it to the word 'al-dhikr'. Understanding this method is crucial for Usul al-Fiqh, as the authenticity of a hadith directly affects the ruling derived from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Error
Locate the narrator 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far and note his mistake: he inserted (adraja) the speech of 'Urwa into the hadith. The correct version omits this addition.
2
List the Correct Narrators
Scan the list of fourteen thiqat (reliable narrators) who narrated only 'al-dhikr'. Note their names and the hadith collections where their narrations are found.
3
Understand the Critical Method
Recognize that the author uses the principle of 'weight of evidence' (kathrat al-turuq) to determine the correct matn. A large number of reliable transmitters agreeing on a shorter version outweighs a single narrator with an addition.
4
Apply to Legal Reasoning
Reflect on how this textual analysis impacts fiqh: if the hadith concerns an act of worship (e.g., dhikr in salah), the interpolation could change the ruling (e.g., whether a specific phrase is required or merely recommended).

The third chapter / Difference in chain and text. Zayd and Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani in their narration from Hisham. The reliable narrators: 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far erred and inserted the speech of 'Urwa into the hadith, while the companions of Hisham restricted [their narration] to mentioning 'al-dhikr', and they are: 1. Abu Usama Hammad ibn Usama, his narration in al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Khuzayma, Ibn al-Jarud, and al-Tabarani. 2. Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash, in al-Daraqutni. 3. Anas ibn 'Iyad, in al-Bayhaqi. 4. Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, details in his chain. 5. Hammad ibn Zayd, in al-Daraqutni, al-Tabarani, al-Hakim, and al-Khatib. 6. Hammad ibn Salama, in al-Tabarani. 7. Rabi'a ibn 'Uthman, in Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and al-Hakim. ... (continues listing narrators and references).
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a list of reliable narrators (thiqat) who transmitted a hadith from Hisham correctly, as opposed to 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Ja'far who committed an idraj (interpolation) by adding the words of 'Urwa into the hadith. The correct version mentions only 'al-dhikr' (the remembrance). The author enumerates fourteen narrators, each with references to major hadith collections, to establish the authentic text. This is a typical method in comparative hadith studies to identify the stronger transmission by weighing the number and reliability of narrators. The passage underscores the importance of textual criticism in Islamic legal methodology (usul al-fiqh) for determining the soundness of a hadith that may be used as evidence for a ruling.

Key Terms
إدراج (idraj): Inserting words that are not part of the original hadith into its text
ثقات (thiqat): Reliable narrators; those whose transmission is considered trustworthy for establishing a hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He narrated from a weak chain
B) He inserted ('adraja) the words of 'Urwa into the hadith
C) He omitted the word 'al-dhikr' entirely
D) He mixed up two different hadiths

Key Takeaway
A hadith's authenticity depends on textual integrity; idraj is exposed by comparing multiple reliable transmissions, and the consensus of thiqat on a shorter version is strong evidence for the correct matn.

Identifying Idraj: The Insertion of 'ولا تنافسوا'
Example of idraj in hadith transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify idraj in a hadith by comparing multiple chains and explain its impact on textual authenticity.

Core Idea
A narrator's insertion of a phrase from another hadith can create a false variant — verification requires comparing chains and texts.

This passage presents a concrete case of idraj (insertion) in hadith transmission. Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam added the phrase 'do not compete' (ولا تنافسوا) to a hadith from Anas (ra), but the majority of Muwatta' narrators transmitted it without this phrase. Al-Kinani identified that Sa'id inadvertently inserted it from another hadith (Abu Hurayra). Understanding this process is essential for authenticating hadith texts before using them as legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator and chain
Note that Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam narrated from Malik from al-Zuhri from Anas. This chain is unique in including the phrase 'ولا تنافسوا'.
2
Compare with the majority narration
The majority of narrators of the Muwatta' transmit the hadith without that phrase. The passage lists 15 reliable narrators who agree on the shorter text.
List includes giants like al-Qa'nabi, Ibn Wahb, and al-Shaybani.
3
Trace the source of insertion
Al-Kinani confirms that Sa'id took the phrase from another hadith (Abu Hurayra via Malik) that explicitly contains 'ولا تنافسوا'. This is the classic marker of idraj.
4
Recognize the scholarly method
Scholars like al-Khatib and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr transmitted Sa'id's version, but the majority's consistency exposes the error. The tara'iq (multiple paths) method is used to detect idraj.
5
Assess the impact on fiqh
Although the inserted prohibition is correct (established elsewhere), its inclusion in this specific hadith is an error. Hanafi usul relies on corroborated texts; a single narrator's insertion does not affect the established ruling but matters for textual criticism.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن

مثاله : ما رَوَاهُ أبو مُحَمَّد سعيد بن أبي مريم الحكم بن مُحَمَّد المصري، عن مالك، عن الزهري عن أنس، أن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ : لا تباغضوا، ولا تحاسدوا، ولا تدابروا، ولا تنافسوا وكونوا عباد الله إخواناً ... الْحَديث»، رَوَاهُ مَن هَذِهِ الطريق: الْخَطِيب، وابن عبد البر. قَالَ الحافظ حمزة بن مُحَمَّد الكناني: «لا أعلم أحداً قَالَ فِي هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن مالك: ولا تنافسوا غَيْر سعيد بن أبي مريم). فسعيد أدرج لفظ: ولا تنافسوا من متن حَدِيث آخر، رَوَاهُ مالك، عن أبي الزناد، عن الأعرج، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة مرفوعاً: «إياكم والظن فإن الظن أكذب الْحَديث، ولا تجسسوا ولا تحسسوا ولا تنافسوا، ولا تحاسدوا».

والحديثان عَلَى الصواب عِنْدَ رواة " الموطأ " كافة مِنْهُمْ:
١. أحمد بن أبي بكر: عِنْدَ ابن حبان.
٢. إسحاق بن عيسى الطباع: عِنْدَ أحمد.
٣. إسماعيل بن أبي أويس: عِنْدَ البخاري في " الأدب المفرد ".
٤. جويرية بن أسماء: عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب في " الفصل ".
٥. روح بن عبادة: عِنْدَ أحمد.
٦. سويد بن سعيد الحدثاني: كَمَا في " الموطأ " بروايته.
٧. عَبْد الرَّحْمٰن بن القاسم: كَمَا في " موطئه ".
٨. عبد الله بن مسلمة القعنبي: عِنْدَ أبي داود، وأبي نعيم، والخطيب.
٩. عبد الله بن وهب: عِنْدَ الطحاوي في " شرح المشكل ".
١٠. عبد الله بن يوسف التنيسي: عِنْدَ البخاري.
١١. الفضل بن دكين: عِنْدَ ابن عَبْد البر.
١٢. قتيبة بن سعيد: عِنْدَ أبي أحمد الْحَاكِم، والخطيب، والعلائي.
١٣. مُحَمَّد بن الحسن: كَمَا في " موطئه ".
١٤. مُحَمَّد بن سليمان المصيصي (لوين): عِنْدَ أبي أحمد الْحَاكِم.
١٥. أبو مصعب الزهري: كَمَا في " الموطأ " بروايته.
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text.
Example: What Abu Muhammad Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam al-Hakam ibn Muhammad al-Misri narrated from Malik, from al-Zuhri, from Anas, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not hate each other, do not envy each other, do not turn your backs on each other, and do not compete with each other, and be, O servants of Allah, brothers...' the hadith. It was narrated via this path by al-Khatib and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr. Al-Hafiz Hamza ibn Muhammad al-Kinani said: 'I do not know anyone who said in this hadith from Malik: "and do not compete with each other" except Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam.' So Sa'id inserted the phrase 'and do not compete with each other' from the text of another hadith, which Malik narrated from Abu al-Zinad, from al-A'raj, from Abu Hurayra, raised: 'Beware of suspicion, for suspicion is the most false of speech; do not spy, do not eavesdrop, do not compete with each other, and do not envy each other.'
And both hadiths are correct according to all the narrators of the Muwatta', among them:
1. Ahmad ibn Abi Bakr: with Ibn Hibban.
2. Ishaq ibn 'Isa al-Tabba': with Ahmad.
3. Isma'il ibn Abi Uways: with al-Bukhari in al-Adab al-Mufrad.
4. Juwayriyya ibn Asma': with al-Khatib in al-Fasl.
5. Ruh ibn 'Ubada: with Ahmad.
6. Suwayd ibn Sa'id al-Hadathani: as in the Muwatta' in his narration.
7. 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Qasim: as in his Muwatta'.
8. 'Abdullah ibn Maslama al-Qa'nabi: with Abu Dawud, Abu Nu'aym, and al-Khatib.
9. 'Abdullah ibn Wahb: with al-Tahawi in Sharh al-Mushkil.
10. 'Abdullah ibn Yusuf al-Tinnisi: with al-Bukhari.
11. al-Fadl ibn Dukayn: with Ibn 'Abd al-Barr.
12. Qutayba ibn Sa'id: with Abu Ahmad al-Hakim, al-Khatib, and al-'Ala'i.
13. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: as in his Muwatta'.
14. Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Misisi (Luwayn): with Abu Ahmad al-Hakim.
15. Abu Mus'ab al-Zuhri: as in the Muwatta' in his narration.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith variant. It provides an example of how a disagreement in the chain (sanad) can lead to a disagreement in the text (matn). The hadith reported by Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam includes the phrase 'ولا تنافسوا' (do not compete with each other), whereas the majority of narrators of the Muwatta' report the hadith without this phrase. Al-Hafiz al-Kinani confirms that Sa'id was the only one to include it. Sa'id inadvertently inserted this phrase from another hadith, namely the one from Abu Hurayra, which explicitly contains 'ولا تنافسوا'. The correct version of the hadith from Anas does not contain that phrase. The author then lists 15 narrators of the Muwatta' who transmitted the hadith correctly without the insertion. This example illustrates the critical importance of comparing multiple narrations to identify errors in transmission. In the Hanafi usul tradition, the reliability of a hadith is determined by both the chain and corroborating texts; such discrepancies can affect the ruling derived from the hadith. The phrase 'ولا تنافسوا' is a prohibition of competing in worldly matters, which is also found in other hadiths, but its presence or absence in this specific narration does not change the overall prohibition since it is established elsewhere. The focus here is on the methodological point of identifying idraj (insertion).

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators through which a hadith is transmitted.
متن (matn): The textual content of the hadith.
إدراج (idraj): The insertion of a phrase from one hadith into another hadith, often by a narrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam do according to this passage?
A) He narrated a hadith with a missing phrase.
B) He inserted a phrase from another hadith into the hadith he narrated.
C) He corrected a mistake in the chain.
D) He combined two hadiths into one.

Key Takeaway
Idraj can be detected by comparing multiple chains and identifying phrases that appear in other hadiths, as exemplified by Sa'id's insertion of 'ولا تنافسوا'.

Multiple Narrations of the Muwatta' and Their Impact on Fiqh Differences
Listing nineteen narrators of Muwatta' with references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key narrators of Imam Malik's Muwatta' and explain how multiple recensions of a hadith collection can lead to differences in fiqh rulings among jurists.

Core Idea
Different riwayaat of the Muwatta' produce variant hadith texts, generating legitimate ikhtilaf among fuqaha.

This passage is a biographical listing of nineteen narrators who transmitted Imam Malik's Muwatta'. It is part of a larger study on how differences in sanad (chain) and matn (text) cause differences among jurists. Recognizing the multiplicity of transmissions is crucial for understanding the sources of ikhtilaf, especially within the Hanafi school which engages with hadith from various recensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each narrator
Read through the list of nineteen names. Note that each narrator is a separate transmitter of the Muwatta', often with their own version (riwayah).
Some narrators are well-known hadith scholars, e.g., 'Abdullah ibn Maslama al-Qa'nabi, Qutayba ibn Sa'id.
2
Note the source reference
For each narrator, the passage provides a reference where that transmission can be found (e.g., al-Khatib, al-Bukhari, Abu Dawud). These references confirm the existence of distinct recensions.
The footnotes give precise page or hadith numbers.
3
Understand the significance of multiple recensions
Each recension may contain slight variations in wording, additions, or omissions. Such variations can influence the legal ruling derived from the hadith.
The Hanafi school often relies on transmissions that may differ from those favored by other schools.
4
Link to fiqh differences
Consider how a hadith transmitted by one narrator might be understood differently from the same hadith in another narration. This is a source of ikhtilaf among madhahib.
For example, differences in the wording of the hadith about the Prophet's wudu' can affect rulings on the obligation of rinsing the mouth.
5
Memorize the key narrators
For a student of Hanafi fiqh, knowing the major narrators of the Muwatta' helps in identifying which riwayah is being referenced in scholarly discussions.
Focus on narrators whose transmissions are frequently cited, e.g., Yahya ibn Yahya (not listed here but known), and those in this list such as Qutayba and al-Qa'nabi.

This listing serves as evidence of the multiple transmission paths of the Muwatta', which is foundational for understanding variant readings that can lead to fiqh differences.

The Fourth Type of Idraj: Insertion via Intermediary
Definition and example of the fourth type of idraj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth type of idraj, distinguish it from other types, and assess its impact on hadith authenticity in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A narrator inserts a part heard from an intermediary into a hadith, mixing chains without distinction.

Hadith transmission requires precision. When a narrator hears a hadith from his shaykh but also hears a part from an intermediary, and then combines them without clarification, the hadith becomes mudraj. This lesson defines the fourth type of idraj, using the example of the 'Uraniyyun hadith where the phrase 'and their urine' was inserted via Qatada. Understanding this helps you evaluate the reliability of hadith evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Read the definition carefully: the narrator has the text except a part he did not hear from his shaykh; instead he heard it from an intermediary. He then includes it in the narration without distinction.
This is subtle because the overall chain looks uniform.
2
Identify key elements in the example
In the 'Uraniyyun hadith, Isma'il ibn Ja'far narrated from Humaid from Anas. The phrase 'وأبوالها' was not heard by Humaid from Anas but from Qatada from Anas. Isma'il inserted it without separating.
The inserted part is only one phrase.
3
Analyze the source testimony
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirms the idraj. Note that other narrators like Ibn Abi 'Adi reported the hadith correctly by separating the two chains.
This shows the idraj was not intentional deception.
4
Compare with other idraj types
In the fourth type, the shaykh is the same, but the chain differs for the inserted part via an intermediary. In other types, the inserted part may come from a different shaykh altogether.
Distinguishing helps in hadith criticism.
5
Evaluate impact on authenticity
Such idraj makes the hadith mudraj. It is considered a defect that reduces reliability. Hanafi scholars require verification before using such hadith as legal evidence.
This affects istinbat (legal derivation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الرابع:
أن يَكُون الْمَتْن عِنْدَ راءٍ إلا جزءاً مِنْهُ، فإنه لَمْ يسمعه من شيخه فيه، وإنما سمعه من واسطة بينه وبين شيخه، فيدرج الرُّوَاة الجزء من الحَدِيث من غَيْر تفصيل (۱۹).

مثاله: الْحَدِيْثِ الَّذِي رَوَاهُ إسماعيل بن جعفر بن أبي كثير (١)، عن حميد الطويل، عن أنس في قصة العرنيين، وأن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لَهُمْ: «لَوْ خرجتم إلى إبلنا فشربتم من ألبانها وأبوالها» (٢). فلفظه: «وأبوالها» لَمْ يسمعها حميد من أنس مباشرة، وإنما سمعها من قتادة، عن أنس، فأدرجها إسماعيل في الْمَتْن الأول بإسناد الْحَدِيث الأول من غير تفصيل، قَالَ الحافظ الخطيب البغدادي: هكذا رَوَى إسماعيل بن جعفر بن أبي كثير الأنصاري هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن حميد الطويل، عن أنس بن مالك، وفيه لفظة واحدة لم يسمعها حميد عن أنس، وإنما رواها عن قتادة عن أنس، وَهِيَ قوله: «وأبوالها»(۳). وَقَدْ رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث عَلَى الصواب ففصل روَايَة قتادة عدة رواة من أصحاب حميد، مِنْهُمْ ابن أبي عدي): عِنْدَ : أَحْمَد)، والنسائي)، والخطيب). بشر بن المفضل : عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب (۸) . خالد بن الحارث ): عِنْدَ النسائي (١).
Section Four: That the text is with a narrator except a part of it, for he did not hear it from his shaykh in it, but rather heard it from an intermediary between him and his shaykh, so the narrator inserts the part of the hadith without distinction. Example: The hadith narrated by Isma'il ibn Ja'far ibn Abi Kathir, from Humaid at-Tawil, from Anas regarding the story of the 'Uraniyyun, and that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to them: 'If you go out to our camels and drink from their milk and their urine.' So the word 'and their urine' was not heard by Humaid from Anas directly, but rather he heard it from Qatada, from Anas. So Isma'il inserted it into the first text with the chain of the first hadith without distinction. Al-Hafiz al-Khatib al-Baghdadi said: This is how Isma'il ibn Ja'far ibn Abi Kathir al-Ansari narrated this hadith from Humaid at-Tawil, from Anas ibn Malik, and in it is one word that Humaid did not hear from Anas, but rather he narrated it from Qatada from Anas, and it is his saying: 'and their urine.' And this hadith was narrated correctly, separating the narration of Qatada, by several narrators from the companions of Humaid, among them: Ibn Abi 'Adi: in Ahmad, an-Nasa'i, and al-Khatib; Bishr ibn al-Mufaddal: in al-Khatib; Khalid ibn al-Harith: in an-Nasa'i.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage defines and exemplifies the fourth type of idraj (insertion) in hadith transmission. The author begins by stating the definition: when a narrator possesses the text of a hadith except for one part, which he did not hear directly from his shaykh but through an intermediary, and then he inserts that part into the full hadith using the original chain without distinguishing the source. This is a subtle form of idraj because the overall chain appears uniform. The example is the well-known hadith of the 'Uraniyyun (the people of 'Urayna) who were given permission to drink camel milk and urine. The narrator Isma'il ibn Ja'far narrated the hadith from Humaid at-Tawil from Anas, but the phrase 'and their urine' was not heard by Humaid directly from Anas. Rather, Humaid heard it from Qatada from Anas. Isma'il then inserted this phrase into the narration without explaining that it came via Qatada. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirms this. The passage then notes that several other narrators from Humaid's students correctly separated the two versions, indicating that this idraj was not intentional deception but a lapse. In Hanafi usul, such details matter because they affect the reliability of the hadith for deriving legal rulings. Students should note the difference between this type and the second type: here the shaykh is the same, but the chain differs for part of the text, whereas in the second type the inserted part comes from a different shaykh altogether.

Key Terms
إدراج (idraj): Insertion of a word or phrase into a hadith that is not from the original narration, here specifically when a narrator adds a part heard from an intermediary into the chain of the first hadith without distinction.
متن (matn): The text of the hadith, i.e., the actual words of the Prophet (ﷺ) or the report.
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fourth type of idraj, the inserted part is not heard directly from the primary shaykh but from an intermediary. In the given example, which phrase was inserted by Isma'il ibn Ja'far via an intermediary?
A) «لَوْ خرجتم إلى إبلنا»
B) «فشربتم من ألبانها»
C) «وأبوالها»
D) «ففصل روَايَة قتادة»

Key Takeaway
The fourth type of idraj occurs when a narrator inserts a part heard from an intermediary into a hadith without distinguishing the chain, affecting the hadith's reliability.

Identifying Idraj (Interpolation) in Hadith: The First Rule and an Example
Discussion of rules to identify interpolation (idraj) in hadith with detailed example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first rule of identifying idraj (impossibility of prophetic attribution) and use comparative chain analysis to distinguish marfu' from mudraj parts of a hadith.

Core Idea
A wording impossible for the Prophet to say is strong evidence of interpolation (idraj).

In hadith criticism, one of the methods to detect interpolation is to evaluate whether the claimed prophetic wording could ever be attributed to the Prophet. This lesson presents that rule through a detailed case study: the hadith about the slave having two rewards. By examining the content and comparing multiple chains of narration, scholars discovered that a key phrase was actually Abu Huraira's own speech, not the Prophet's. Understanding this process is essential for properly weighing hadith evidence in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for textual impossibility
Understand the first rule: if a phrase is impossible to attribute to the Prophet, it is likely an interpolation. Note the example: the Prophet cannot wish for slavery, nor did he have a mother to be dutiful to.
2
Analyze the example hadith
Read the hadith about the slave having two rewards and the disputed phrase 'By Him in Whose hand is my soul...' etc. Recognize that this phrase contradicts what we know about the Prophet.
3
Examine the chains of narration
See how the author lists multiple narrators who separated the interpolated part, and others who did not. Understand that comparing chains helps confirm which portion is marfu'.
4
Apply the methodology
In practice, when encountering a hadith with an unusual phrase, you would check if the wording is possible for the Prophet, then look at the transmission history to see if anyone reported it differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن لفظ الرسول ( ). والحق أنه إذا قامت قرائن ومرجحات تقوي في نفس الناقد الحكم عَلَى تِلْكَ اللفظة بالإدراج فلا مانع من ذَلِكَ، وفي هَذَا يقول الحافظ ابن حجر: «وفي الجملة إذا قام الدليل على إدراج جملة معينة بحيث يغلب على الظن ذَلِكَ، فسواء كَانَ في الأول أو الوسط أو الآخر، فإن سبب ذَلِكَ الاختصار من بعض الرُّوَاة بحذف أداة التفسير أو التفصيل، فيجيء من بعده فيرويه مدمجاً من غَيْر تفصيل فيقع ذَلِكَ». وقد وضع العلماء جملة من القواعد التي يعرف بها كون الْحَدِيث مدرجاً، يمكننا حصرها فيما يأتي: ١. أن يَكُوْن لفظه ممَّا تستحيل إضافته إلى النبي . مثاله : حَدِيث عَبْد الله بن المبارك، عن يونس بن يزيد الأيلي، عن الزهري، عن سعيد بن المسيب، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُول الله : للعبد المملوك أجران، والذي نفسي بيده لولا الجهاد في سبيل الله والحج وبر أمي لأحببت أن أموت وأنا مملوك»(۳). فقوله: «والذي نفسي بيده ... الخ الْحَدِيث»، مِمَّا تستحيل نسبته إلى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذْ لا يجوز في حقه أن يتمنى الرّق، وأيضاً لَمْ تكن لَهُ أم يبرها، ولما فتشنا وجدناه مدرجاً من كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة. فقد أخرجه البخاري (4) عن بشر بن محمد () ، عن عبد الله بن المبارك، عن يونس، عن الزهري، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، بِهِ. فأدرج كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة في المرفوع، وفصل القدر المدرج ثلاثة من الرُّوَاة عن ابن المبارك هم: .1 إبْرَاهِيم بن إسحاق الطالقاني: عِنْدَ أحمد (). 2 عبدان المروزي (۱): عِنْدَ البيهقي (۳). 3 حبان بن موسى المروزي (٣): عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب (٤). كما أن ابن المبارك متابع في روايته عن يونس متابعة تامة، تابعه: (ه): أبو صفوان الأموي (٥) : عِنْدَ مُسْلِم (3) (3) سليمان بن بلال: عِنْدَ البخاري في " الأدب المفرد ) . عبد الله بن وهب عِنْدَ مُسْلِم ) ، وأبي عوانة)، والخطيب (۱). عثمان بن عمر (١١): عِنْدَ أحمد (۱۳)، وأبي عوانة (۱۳). فظهر أن هَذَا الجزء من الْمَتْن مدرج في حَدِيث رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من كلام أبـي هُرَيْرَة، قَالَ الْخَطِيْب: وقول النَّبِي هو: اللعبد الصالح أجران» فَقَطْ، وما بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إنما هُوَ كلام أبي هُرَيْرَة (١٤).
Chapter Three: Difference in Sanad and Matn, the wording of the Messenger ( ). The truth is that if there are indications and preponderating factors that strengthen in the critic's mind the judgment that a particular word is idraj (interpolation), then there is no obstacle to that. In this regard, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'In summary, if the evidence establishes the interpolation of a specific phrase such that it becomes preponderant in opinion, then whether it is at the beginning, middle, or end, the reason for that is the abbreviation by some narrators by deleting the tool of explanation or detail, so one after him narrates it integrated without detail, so that occurs.' And the scholars have set a number of rules by which it is known that a hadith is mudraj. We can summarize them as follows: 1. That its wording be such that it is impossible to attribute it to the Prophet. Example: The hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak from Yunus ibn Yazid al-Ayli from al-Zuhri from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib from Abu Huraira who said: The Messenger of God said: 'For the owned slave there are two rewards. By Him in Whose hand is my soul, if it were not for jihad in the path of God, Hajj, and doing good to my mother, I would love to die while I am a slave.' His saying: 'By Him in Whose hand is my soul...' etc. is from what is impossible to attribute to the Prophet, because it is not permissible for him to wish for slavery, and also he did not have a mother to be dutiful to. When we investigated, we found it to be interpolated from the speech of Abu Huraira. Al-Bukhari narrated it from Bishr ibn Muhammad from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak from Yunus from al-Zuhri from Abu Huraira, thus. So the speech of Abu Huraira was interpolated into the marfu' part. And three narrators from Ibn al-Mubarak distinguished the interpolated part: 1. Ibrahim ibn Ishaq al-Taliqani: according to Ahmad. 2. Abdān al-Marwazi: according to al-Bayhaqi. 3. Habbān ibn Musa al-Marwazi: according to al-Khatib. Also Ibn al-Mubarak was fully followed in his narration from Yunus; those who followed him are: Abu Safwan al-Umawi: according to Muslim; Sulayman ibn Bilal: according to al-Bukhari in al-Adab al-Mufrad; Abdullah ibn Wahb: according to Muslim, Abu Awana, and al-Khatib; Uthman ibn Umar: according to Ahmad and Abu Awana. So it became clear that this part of the text is interpolated in the hadith of the Messenger of God from the speech of Abu Huraira. Al-Khatib said: The Prophet's saying is only 'For the righteous slave there are two rewards,' and what follows that is the speech of Abu Huraira.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the phenomenon of idraj (interpolation) in hadith texts, specifically focusing on how scholars identify such interpolations. The author begins by stating the principle that if sufficient evidence and indicators point to a particular word being interpolated, then it is acceptable to deem it as such. He cites Ibn Hajar's explanation that interpolation often results from narrators abbreviating and omitting the explanatory framework, causing later narrators to report the text as a continuous whole. Then, the author presents the first rule: the wording must be such that it is impossible to attribute to the Prophet. The example given is the hadith about the slave having two rewards, with an additional part where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) is claimed to have said 'By Him in Whose hand is my soul...' and expressed a wish to be a slave. By analyzing the content—since the Prophet cannot wish for slavery and did not have a mother to be dutiful to—and by examining the chains of narration, it becomes clear that this addition is from Abu Huraira's own speech, not the Prophet's. The author then lists the narrators who reported the hadith with and without the interpolation, showing that some transmitted it precisely, distinguishing the Prophet's words from Abu Huraira's. This demonstrates the meticulous methodology of hadith critics in preserving the authenticity of prophetic traditions.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idraj): The inclusion of someone's own words into the text of a prophetic hadith, making it appear as part of the hadith.
المدرج (al-mudraj): A hadith that contains an interpolation (idraj) within its text.
المرفوع (al-marfu): A saying, action, or tacit approval attributed directly to the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the primary evidence that the phrase starting with 'والذي نفسي بيده' was an interpolation?
A) The chain of narration contained a weak narrator.
B) The meaning was impossible to attribute to the Prophet.
C) The hadith was not found in any of the authentic collections.
D) Other scholars had unanimously declared it weak.

Key Takeaway
Interpolation in hadith is identified by impossibility of prophetic attribution and verified through comparative chain analysis; only the verified prophetic part holds legal authority.

Analyzing Narrator Error (Wahm) in Sanad and Matn
Example of narrator error in chain and text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a narrator's error (wahm) in both the chain (isnad) and text (matn) of a hadith and distinguish between the marfu' and mawquf parts using textual criticism.

Core Idea
A single narrator's error can corrupt both chain and text—textual criticism is essential to preserve the Sunnah.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the authenticity of hadith is paramount for deriving legal rulings. This lesson examines a concrete example where a narrator, Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Utaridi, made two mistakes in transmitting a hadith: he confused the chain of narrators and incorrectly combined the Prophet's statement with a Companion's statement. By working through this case, you will learn how scholars detect and correct such errors, a skill vital for evaluating the strength of a hadith used as legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator and the hadith
Locate the narrator who erred (Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar) and the hadith he transmitted. Note the full chain and text as he reported it.
The erroneous version: 'Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise, and whoever dies associating anything with Allah enters Hellfire.'
2
Detect the error in sanad
Compare the chain given by the erroneous narrator with the correct chain as reported by reliable narrators. Observe that Asim narrates from Abu Wail, not from Zirr.
The correct chain is: Asim → Abu Wail → Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.
3
Detect the error in matn
Identify which part of the text is genuinely prophetic (marfu') and which is the Companion's own statement (mawquf). The first sentence about dying as a polytheist is from the Prophet; the second is Ibn Mas'ud's addition.
The correct marfu' portion is only 'Whoever dies associating anything with Allah enters Hellfire' (or as in another narration: 'Whoever sets up a rival with Allah, Allah will place him in the Fire').
4
Cross-check with reliable narrators
List the other narrators who preserved the correct chain and distinguished the two parts. This strengthens the case that al-Utaridi's version is erroneous.
Narrators like Aswad ibn Amir, Abu Kurayb, and others transmitted the correct version.
5
Summarize the lesson for usul al-fiqh
Reflect on how this example illustrates the importance of textual and chain criticism in establishing authentic prophetic traditions for legal derivation (istidlal).
A hadith that is marfu' in part and mawquf in another must be handled carefully to avoid attributing a Companion's opinion to the Prophet.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
٢. أن يرد التصريح من الصَّحَابِي بأنه لَمْ يَسْمَع تِلْكَ الجملة من النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم (٣)
مثاله ما رواه أحمد بن عَبْد الجبار العطاردي (١) (هُوَ أَحمد بن عَبْد الجبار بن مُحَمَّد العطاردي أبو عَمْرو الكوفي: ضعيف، وسماعه للسيرة صحيح، توفي سنة (٢٧٢هـ). الجرح والتعديل ٦٢/٢ والكامل في ضعفاء الرجال ٣١٤/١-٣١٣، والتقريب (٦٤).) عن أبي بكر بن عياش(٢) (هُوَ أبو بكر بن عياش بن سالم الأسدي، الكوفي المقرئ الحناط، وَهُوَ مشهور بكنيته، واختلف اسمه فقيل: مُحَمَّد وَقِيلَ: عَبْد الله، وَقِيلَ: سالم وَقِيْلَ غَيْر ذَلِكَ: ثقة عابد، إلا أنَّه لما كبر ساء حفظه وكتابه صحيح، توفي سنة (١٩٤ هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (١٩٢ هـ). تهذيب الكمال ٢٨٢٥٧/٨ (٤٧)، والكاشف (٤١٢/٢) (٦٥٣٥)، والتقريب (٧٩٨٥).) عن عاصم بن أبي النجود عن زر بن حبيش (٣) (هُوَ زر بن حبيش - مصغر - بن حباشة الأسدي الكوفي أبو مريم ثقة جليل، مخضرم، توفي (٨١)، وَقِيلَ: (٨٢) هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (٨٣) هـ). التاريخ الكبير ٤٤٧/٣، والعبر ٩٥/١، والتقريب (٢٠٠٨).) عن عبد الله بن مسعود، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (من مات وَهُوَ لا يشرك بالله شَيْئاً دخل الجنة، ومن مات وَهُوَ يشرك بالله شَيْئاً دخل النار).
فأحمد بن عبد الجبار وهم في هَذَا الْحَدِيث، فأدرج الجملة الثانية في المرفوع من الْحَدِيث وَهُوَ الجملة الأولى، قَالَ الْخَطِيْب: هكذا رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث أَحمد بن عبد الجبار العطاردي، عن أبي بكر بن عياش ووهم في إسناده وفي متنه.
أما الوهم في إسناده فإن عاصماً إنما كَانَ يرويه عن أبي وائل شقيق بن سلمة، عن عبد الله لا عن زر، وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ كذلك عن أبي بكر: أسود بن عامر (٥) (هُوَ الأسود بن عامر الشامي نزيل بغداد يكنى أبا عَبْد الرَّحْمَان ويلقب بـ: شاذان: ثقة، توفي سنة (٢٠٨ هـ). تهذيب الكمال ٢٦١/١ (٤٩٥)، والكاشف (٢٥١/١) (٤٢٢)، والتقريب (٥٠٣).) شاذان، وأبو هشام مُحَمَّد بن يزيد الرفاعي (٦) (هُوَ مُحَمَّد بن يزيد بن مُحَمَّد العجلي، أبو هشام الرفاعي الكوفي قاضي المدائن: لَيْس بالقوي، توفي سنة (٢٤٨هـ). تهذيب الكمال ٥٦٥/٦ (٧٢٩٥)، والكاشف (٢٣١/٢) (٥٢٢٣)، والتقريب (٦٤٠٢).) وأبو كريب مُحَمَّد بن العلاء الهمداني، ووافقهم حماد ابن شعيب (٧) (هُوَ حماد بن شعيب الحماني التميمي، أبو شعيب الكوفي، قَالَ النسائي فيه: كوفي ضعيف، وَكَذَلِكَ يَحْيَى بن مَعِيْن، وغيرهم. الجرح والتعديل ١٤٣/٣، والكامل في الضعفاء ١٥/٣، وذيل الكاشف: ٨٢ (٣٢٠).) والهيثم بن جهم (٨) (قال أبو حاتم لَمْ أرَ في حديثه مكروهاً. الجرح والتعديل ٨٣/٩، وانظر: التاريخ الكبير ٢١٦/٨.) والد عثمان بن الهيثم المؤذن، فروياه عن عاصم، عن أبي وائل كذلك.
وأما الوهم في متن الْحَدِيث: فإن العطاردي في روايته جعله كله كلام النبيل وليس كذلك، وإنما الفصل في ذكر من مات مشركاً قَوْل رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، والفصل الثاني في ذكر من مات غَيْر مشرك قَوْل عَبْد الله بن مسعود(١).
وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ جمع من الرُّوَاة عن أبي بكر بن عياش وميزوا بين الفصلين، وهم:
أبو كريب مُحَمَّد بن العلاء: عِنْدَ الْخَطِيب في " الفصل الأسود بن عامر :(شاذان) عِنْدَ أحمد (٣)، ومن طريقه الخَطِيب).
مُحَمَّد بن يزيد أبو هاشم الرفاعي عِنْدَ أبي يعلى()، والخطيب).
ثُمَّ إن أبا بكر بن عياش متابع عليه في روايته عن عاصم، تابعه: حماد بن شعيب عند الخَطِيب ().
الهيثم بن جهم: عِنْدَ الْخَطِيْب أَيْضاً).
أبو أيوب الإفريقي (٩) (هُوَ عَبْد الله بن عَلِيّ الأزرق، أبو أيوب الإفريقي، ثُمَّ الكوفي: صدوق يخطئ، من السادسة. تهذيب الكمال ٢١٥/٤ (٣٤٢٤)، والكاشف (٢٨٦٩٥٧٦/١)، والتقريب (٣٤٨٧).): عِنْدَ الطبراني في " الكبير (١٠) و" الأوسط (١١). ورواه أحمد بن يونس، عن أبي بكر بن عياش مقتصراً عَلَى اللفظ المرفوع ) ولفظ الْحَدِيث كَمَا رَوَاهُ أحمد (١٣) من طريق أسود بن عامر: قَالَ عَبْد الله: سَمِعْتُ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «من جعل الله نداً جعله الله في النار»، وَقَالَ: وأخرى أقولها لَمْ أسمعها مِنْهُ: من مات لا يجعل الله نداً أدخله الله الجنة.
Chapter Three: Disagreement in the Chain and Text
2. That the Companion explicitly states that he did not hear that phrase from the Prophet, peace be upon him.
Example: What Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Utaridi narrated from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, from Asim ibn Abi al-Najud, from Zirr ibn Hubaysh, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, from the Prophet, peace be upon him: "Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise, and whoever dies associating anything with Allah enters Hellfire."
So Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar erred in this hadith, inserting the second sentence into the marfu' part of the hadith, while it is the first sentence. Al-Khatib said: Thus Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Utaridi narrated this hadith from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, and he erred in its chain and its text.
As for the error in its chain: Asim only used to narrate it from Abu Wail Shaqiq ibn Salama, from Abdullah, not from Zirr. And it has been narrated likewise from Abu Bakr by Aswad ibn Amir (Shadhan), and Abu Hisham Muhammad ibn Yazid al-Rifa'i, and Abu Kurayb Muhammad ibn al-Ala' al-Hamdani, and they were followed by Hammad ibn Shu'ayb and al-Haytham ibn Jahm (father of Uthman ibn al-Haytham al-Mu'adhdhin), and they narrated it from Asim, from Abu Wail likewise.
As for the error in the text of the hadith: al-Utaridi in his narration made it all the speech of the Prophet, but it is not like that. Rather, the first part mentioning those who die as polytheists is the saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the second part mentioning those who die not as polytheists is the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.
And a group of narrators have narrated it from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash and distinguished between the two parts, and they are:
Abu Kurayb Muhammad ibn al-Ala' (recorded by al-Khatib in al-Fasl), Aswad ibn Amir (Shadhan) (recorded by Ahmad and via him by al-Khatib), Muhammad ibn Yazid Abu Hashim al-Rifa'i (recorded by Abu Ya'la and al-Khatib).
Then Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash was followed in his narration from Asim, followed by: Hammad ibn Shu'ayb (recorded by al-Khatib), al-Haytham ibn Jahm (also recorded by al-Khatib), Abu Ayyub al-Ifriqi (recorded by al-Tabari in al-Kabir and al-Awsat). And Ahmad ibn Yunus narrated it from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, restricting to the marfu' wording, and the wording of the hadith as narrated by Ahmad from the path of Aswad ibn Amir: Abdullah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: "Whoever sets up a rival with Allah, Allah will place him in the Fire." And he said: And another thing I say which I did not hear from him: Whoever dies not setting up a rival with Allah, Allah will admit him to Paradise.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is an example of a textual analysis showing a narrator's error (wahm) in both the chain (isnad) and the text (matn) of a hadith. The author presents a case where Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Utaridi transmitted a hadith from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, but he made two mistakes. First, in the chain: he reported that Asim narrated from Zirr, but the correct chain is that Asim narrated from Abu Wail, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Several other narrators confirm the correct chain. Second, in the text: he combined two statements into a single marfu' (prophetic) saying, whereas in fact the first part (about dying as a polytheist) is the Prophet's words, and the second part (about dying not as a polytheist) is the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (a mawquf statement). The passage then lists other narrators who preserved the correct distinction between the two parts, and provides the correct wording from a reliable source. This lesson guards against the common misunderstanding that all narrations of a hadith are equally authentic, and shows the importance of textual criticism in Islamic legal scholarship.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): Error by a narrator in reporting a hadith, either in chain (isnad) or text (matn) or both.
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A statement or action attributed to the Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him.
الموقوف (al-mawquf): A statement or action attributed to a Companion of the Prophet.
الإسناد (al-isnad): The chain of narrators that traces a hadith back to its source.
المتن (al-matn): The text of the hadith, i.e., the actual words reported.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith example given, what was the error in the text (matn)?
A) The narrator added a word that changed the meaning.
B) The narrator combined the Prophet's saying with Ibn Mas'ud's saying as one marfu' statement.
C) The narrator reported the hadith with the wrong chain.
D) The narrator made the hadith mawquf when it should have been marfu'.

Key Takeaway
Textual criticism of hadith is essential to distinguish authentic prophetic statements from companion sayings mistakenly attributed to the Prophet.

Identifying Mudraj Hadith: The Case of Ibn Mas'ud's Statement
Example of a narrator mistakenly attributing a companion's statement to the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a mudraj (inserted) text in a hadith, distinguish between the marfu' and mawquf parts, and explain the significance for Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A narrator's error can elevate a companion's statement to prophetic status — distinguishing mudraj preserves Sunnah's integrity.

This passage exposes a common textual error in hadith transmission: idraj, where a narrator mistakenly includes a companion's explanation as part of the Prophet's words. By tracing chains of transmission, the author shows that the second part of the hadith about entering Paradise is actually Ibn Mas'ud's own saying, not a prophetic statement. Understanding this distinction is vital for correct legal derivation in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith text as transmitted by al-Ataridi
Read the full hadith as mistakenly transmitted — both parts appear as continuous prophetic speech.
Al-Ataridi's version merges the marfu' and mawquf parts.
2
Separate the two parts using the source analysis
The author splits it: first part (threat of Fire) is marfu'; second part (promise of Paradise) is mawquf from Ibn Mas'ud, as Ibn Mas'ud himself says 'I did not hear it from him'.
This explicit admission is key to detecting idraj.
3
Verify through alternative narrators
The author lists several narrators (Abu Kurayb, al-Aswad ibn Amir, etc.) who transmitted the hadith correctly, distinguishing between the two parts.
Cross-checking multiple chains confirms the error.
4
Recognize the type of error as idraj
This is idraj (insertion) — a narrator adds to the prophetic text a companion's statement, making it appear marfu'.
Hanafi scholars classify this as a serious flaw that can affect legal rulings.
5
Apply the distinction to fiqh derivation
The marfu' part establishes a ruling (shirk leads to Fire), while the mawquf part is only a companion's opinion, not prophetic law, thus not binding.
This affects whether the promise of Paradise is directly from the Prophet or Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوهم في متن الْحَدِيث: فإن العطاردي في روايته جعله كله كلام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وليس كذلك، وإنما الفصل في ذكر من مات مشركاً قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، والفصل الثاني في ذكر من مات غير مشرك قول عبد الله بن مسعود. وقد رواه جمع من الرواة عن أبي بكر بن عياش وميزوا بين الفصلين، وهم: أبو كريب محمد بن العلاء عند الخطيب في "الفصل"، الأسود بن عامر (شاذان) عند أحمد، ومن طريقه الخطيب، محمد بن يزيد أبو هاشم الرفاعي عند أبي يعلى والخطيب. ثم إن أبا بكر بن عياش متابع عليه في روايته عن عاصم، تابعه: حماد بن شعيب عند الخطيب، الهيثم بن جهم عند الخطيب أيضاً، أبو أيوب الإفريقي عند الطبراني في "الكبير" و"الأوسط". ورواه أحمد بن يونس عن أبي بكر بن عياش مقتصراً على اللفظ المرفوع. ولفظ الحديث كما رواه أحمد من طريق أسود بن عامر: قال عبد الله: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «من جعل الله نداً جعله الله في النار»، وقال: وأخرى أقولها لم أسمعها منه: من مات لا يجعل الله نداً أدخله الله الجنة.
As for the error in the text of the hadith: al-Ataridi in his narration made it all the speech of the Prophet, but it is not so. Rather, the first part about 'whoever died as a polytheist' is the saying of the Messenger of Allah, and the second part about 'whoever died not as a polytheist' is the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. A group of narrators narrated it from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash and distinguished between the two parts: Abu Kurayb Muhammad ibn al-Ala' (recorded by al-Khatib in al-Fasl), al-Aswad ibn Amir (Shadhan) (recorded by Ahmad and via him al-Khatib), Muhammad ibn Yazid Abu Hashim al-Rifa'i (recorded by Abu Ya'la and al-Khatib). Then Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash has followers in his narration from Asim: Hammad ibn Shu'ayb (recorded by al-Khatib), al-Haytham ibn Jahim (also recorded by al-Khatib), Abu Ayyub al-Ifriqi (recorded by al-Tabarani in al-Kabir and al-Awsat). And Ahmad ibn Yunus narrated it from Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash restricting to the marfu' wording. The wording of the hadith as narrated by Ahmad via al-Aswad ibn Amir: Abdullah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever sets up a rival to Allah, Allah will place him in the Fire.' And he said: And another thing I say which I did not hear from him: Whoever dies without setting up a rival to Allah, Allah will admit him to Paradise.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a case study in hadith analysis (naqd al-hadith) demonstrating a specific type of error: idraj (insertion) where a narrator mistakenly includes a companion's statement as part of the Prophet's speech. The author shows that al-Ataridi erred by attributing the entire narration to the Prophet, whereas in reality only the first sentence is marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and the second is a statement of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The passage then lists several narrators who correctly separated the two parts, thus preserving the integrity of the hadith. This distinction is crucial for fiqh, as the ruling about entering Paradise for those who die without shirk is based on Ibn Mas'ud's own ijtihad, not a direct prophetic statement. The hadith itself (the marfu' part) warns against setting up rivals to Allah. The author uses this example to illustrate how differences in chains and texts can lead to different fiqh conclusions if not properly identified.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): An error or mistake in the narration of a hadith, specifically in the text (matn).
المدرج (al-mudraj): An insertion where a narrator adds words from a companion or others into the prophetic text, making it appear part of the hadith.
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A hadith attributed to the Prophet Muhammad, whether in statement, action, or tacit approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith about 'man ja'ala lillahi niddan', what part is actually the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and not the Prophet?
A) The entire hadith is the Prophet's words.
B) The part stating 'Whoever sets up a rival to Allah, Allah will place him in the Fire' is from Ibn Mas'ud.
C) The part stating 'Whoever dies without setting up a rival to Allah, Allah will admit him to Paradise' is from Ibn Mas'ud.
D) The hadith is not authentic.

Key Takeaway
Idraj can elevate a companion's statement to prophetic status; rigorous isnad-matn analysis is necessary to preserve the integrity of Sunnah in Hanafi usul.

Identifying Mudraj in Hadith: The Case of Ibn Umar's Divorce
Example of narrators distinguishing the Prophet's words from Ibn Umar's explanation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mudraj in a hadith by comparing narrations and explain why distinguishing it from the marfu' is essential for correct istinbat.

Core Idea
A narrator's question is not prophetic—confusing mudraj with marfu' changes the legal weight.

This lesson examines a classic example of hadith criticism where narrators explicitly separated the Prophet's words from the words of a companion and a subordinate narrator. By analyzing the variant narrations, you will learn how to detect an insertion (idraj) and why it matters for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core prophetic statement
The marfu' part is only the command 'Order him to take her back, and when she becomes pure, then let him divorce her.'
This is the part attributed to the Prophet.
2
Spot the suspicious question
The question 'Does that count as one divorce?' appears to be an interruption. Does it come from the Prophet or someone else?
Due to the chain, it is ambiguous.
3
Compare with other narrations
Al-Khatib and other narrators clarified that the question is from Anas ibn Sirin and the answer from Ibn Umar. They explicitly separated them.
This is the second type of mudraj correction discussed.
4
Apply the rule for mudraj
Conclude that the question-answer pair is mudraj and not part of the marfu'. Hence, the ruling about counting the divorce is from Ibn Umar's ijtihad, not a direct prophetic command.
This affects the strength of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣. أن يفصل بعض الرُّوَاة فيبينوا المدرج ويَفْصِلُوه عن المتن المرفوع، ويضيفوه إلى قائله: مثاله: ما رواه عبد الله بن خيران عن شعبة عن أنس بن سيرين أنه سمع ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما يقول: طلقت امرأتي وهي حائض فذكر عمر ذلك للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: «مُره فليراجعها فإذا طهرت فليطلقها» قال: فتحتسب بالتطليقة؟ قال: فمه. قال الخطيب: «والصواب أن الاستفهام من قول أنس بن سيرين، وأن جوابه من قول ابن عمر». وقد بين ذلك جماعة الرواة عن شعبة وهم: بهز بن أسد عند أحمد ومسلم، الحجاج بن منهال عند الطحاوي، خالد بن الحارث عند مسلم، سليمان بن حرب عند البخاري، محمد بن جعفر (غندر) عند أحمد ومسلم والخطيب.
3. That some narrators separate and clarify the inserted part, distinguishing it from the marfu' text, and attribute it to its actual speaker. Example: What Abdullah ibn Khayran narrated from Shu'ba from Anas ibn Sirin that he heard Ibn Umar say: 'I divorced my wife while she was menstruating, so Umar mentioned that to the Prophet, and he said: 'Order him to take her back, and when she becomes pure, then let him divorce her.' He said: 'Then does that count as one divorce?' He said: 'What else?' Al-Khatib said: 'The correct view is that the question is from the saying of Anas ibn Sirin, and its answer is from the saying of Ibn Umar.' And a group of narrators clarified that from Shu'ba: Bahz ibn Asad (recorded by Ahmad and Muslim), al-Hajjaj ibn Minhal (recorded by al-Tahawi), Khalid ibn al-Harith (recorded by Muslim), Sulayman ibn Harb (recorded by al-Bukhari), Muhammad ibn Ja'far (Ghundar) (recorded by Ahmad, Muslim, and al-Khatib).
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents a second type of textual error correction: when narrators explicitly separate the inserted (mudraj) part from the prophetic statement. The example involves a hadith about divorce during menstruation. In the version narrated by Abdullah ibn Khayran, it appears as if the Prophet answers a question about counting the divorce, but al-Khatib clarifies that the question 'Does that count as one divorce?' and the answer 'What else?' come from Anas ibn Sirin (the subordinate narrator) and Ibn Umar respectively, not from the Prophet. This distinction is crucial for fiqh: the ruling about the divorce counting is actually Ibn Umar's ijtihad, not a direct prophetic command. The author then lists several narrators who correctly transmitted the hadith with this separation, confirming the mudraj nature. This example teaches that careful hadith criticism (naqd) is necessary to avoid attributing companion statements to the Prophet, which would otherwise change the legal weight.

Key Terms
المدرج (al-mudraj): An insertion in a hadith where words from a narrator or companion are mistakenly included in the prophetic text.
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A hadith attributed to the Prophet, which in this example is only the command to take her back and divorce later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Abdullah ibn Umar.

Key Takeaway
Identifying mudraj requires comparing multiple narrations; the marfu' part carries authority, while the mudraj does not bind.

The Ruling on Idraj (Insertion) in Hadith
States the ruling on idraj and its effect on narrator reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on idraj, distinguish between forbidden insertion and permissible explanatory glosses, and identify the effect on narrator reliability.

Core Idea
Deliberate insertion in hadith is forbidden and damns the narrator, except for clearly separated explanations of rare words.

Idraj (insertion) is a serious defect in hadith that can undermine authenticity. This lesson clarifies its ruling: deliberate idraj is prohibited and harms the narrator's credibility. However, a key exception exists for explanatory notes that are clearly marked separate from the original text, as practiced by early scholars like al-Zuhri. Understanding this distinction is essential for evaluating hadith in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Define idraj and identify its types
Idraj is the insertion of extraneous material into the text (matn) or chain (isnad) of a hadith. Note that it can be deliberate or unintentional; the ruling here focuses on deliberate insertion.
Idraj differs from tadlis (concealment) but can overlap.
2
State the general ruling on deliberate idraj
According to Imam al-Sam'ani and the majority, deliberate idraj is haram (forbidden). It impugns the narrator's 'adalah (integrity), rendering their narrations rejected (mardud).
The passage equates the mudallis (one who inserts) with liars.
3
Analyze the exception for explanatory glosses
Al-Hafiz al-Suyuti permitted idraj if it is an explanation of a gharib (rare) word and is clearly separated from the original hadith text. The author supports this view, citing the practice of al-Zuhri.
The key condition is the clear separation (fasl) indicating the inserted part.
4
Apply the ruling to narrator evaluation
If a narrator is known to deliberately insert without separation, they are considered jarh (impaired). If they insert explanatory notes with clear separation, they remain trustworthy.
This impacts the acceptance of their hadith in legal derivation (istinbat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الخامس: حكم الإدراج
اتضح لنا فيما مضى أن الإدراج علة يعل بها الحديث، سواء وقعت في المتن أو الإسناد، لذا فتعمد الإدراج حرام، بل هو أمر قادح في عدالة الراوي، لا سيما إذا انبنى على ذلك شيء من الأحكام العلمية أو العملية، قال الإمام أبو المظفر السمعاني: «وأما من يدلس في المتون فهذا مطرح الحديث مجروح العدالة، وهو ممن يحرف الكلم عن مواضعه وإن كان ملحقاً بالكذابين ولم يقبل حديثه» (١).
إلا أن الحافظ السيوطي رأى أن تفسير الغريب الذي يقع في متن الحديث غير ممنوع، واستدل بفعل الزهري وغيره من أساطين الرواية له. والذي أراه أن لا بأس بهذا الاستثناء لا سيما إذا أتي بفصل يبين المدرج، والله أعلم.
The Fifth Section: The Ruling on Idraj. It has become clear to us from what preceded that idraj is a defect by which the hadith is criticized, whether it occurs in the text or the chain. Therefore, deliberate idraj is forbidden; rather, it is a cause that impugns the narrator's integrity, especially if it entails any matters of knowledge or practice. Imam Abu al-Muzaffar al-Sam'ani said: 'As for one who inserts (yudallis) in the texts, he is a discarded narrator, his integrity is compromised, he is among those who distort words from their places, and he is considered akin to liars, and his hadith is not accepted.' However, al-Hafiz al-Suyuti held that explaining a rare word (gharib) occurring in the text of a hadith is not forbidden, citing the practice of al-Zuhri and other leading narrators. My opinion is that this exception is acceptable, especially if a distinct separation is made to indicate the inserted part. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on idraj (insertion) in hadith. It begins by stating that idraj is a defect that can affect either the text (matn) or the chain (isnad). Deliberate idraj is forbidden and damages the narrator's credibility. The author quotes Imam al-Sam'ani, who compares a mudallis (one who inserts) to a liar, leading to rejection of his hadith. However, al-Suyuti allows an exception: if the insertion is simply an explanation of an unfamiliar word (gharib), and is clearly marked as separate, it is permissible, citing the practice of early scholars. The author supports this exception. The passage thus establishes that intentional idraj is a serious defect, except for clearly separated explanatory glosses.

Key Terms
الإدراج (al-idraj): Insertion of additional material into a hadith text or chain, whether intentional or mistaken, considered a defect that impairs authenticity.
تدليس (tadlis): In this context, tadlis refers to deliberate insertion into the text of a hadith, synonymous with idraj in the matn.
الغريب (al-gharib): A rare or unfamiliar word in the hadith text that requires explanation.
الفصل (al-fasl): A clear separation or distinction, such as a verbal marker, indicating that the inserted material is not part of the original hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a narrator who adds an explanation of a rare word without any separation from the hadith text?
A) The narrator is still trustworthy because he is explaining.
B) The narrator's hadith is rejected because he committed forbidden idraj.
C) It depends on the narrator's overall reliability.
D) The insertion is permissible because it is beneficial.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate idraj without clear separation is forbidden and discredits the narrator, but clearly separated explanatory glosses are permissible.

Exception for Explaining Unfamiliar Words (Tafsir al-Gharib)
Discusses the permissibility of explaining unfamiliar words in hadith as an exception to prohibition of interpolation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited interpolation (idraj) and permissible explanation (tafsir al-gharib) in hadith texts, and apply the condition that the commentary must be clearly separated.

Core Idea
Explaining unfamiliar words in a hadith is an exception to the prohibition of interpolation, provided the commentary distinguishes itself from the original text.

In the study of hadith and its application to fiqh, precision in transmitting the Prophet's words is paramount. However, when a hadith contains rare or unfamiliar terms, scholars have differed on whether explaining them within the text constitutes a forbidden interpolation. This lesson explores a crucial exception advocated by al-Hafiz al-Suyuti and accepted by the author of our passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that altering the words of a hadith from their proper place is generally prohibited, and a narrator who does so is likened to liars and his hadith is rejected.
This is the standard position to prevent distortion of prophetic texts.
2
State the Exception
Al-Hafiz al-Suyuti holds that explaining unfamiliar (gharib) words occurring in the hadith text is not prohibited. This is an exception to the general rule.
The exception is based on the practice of early authorities like al-Zuhri.
3
Examine the Evidence
The evidence (dalil) for this exception is the action (fi'l) of al-Zuhri and other leading narrators, who would explain unusual terms. This is a form of precedent (qawl sahabi or tabi'i) that carries weight in Hanafi usul.
Al-Zuhri was a renowned tabi'i and hadith scholar; his practice is considered a strong proof.
4
Apply the Condition
The author accepts the exception only if a separate section (fasl) is provided that clearly marks the explanation as distinct from the original hadith text (mudraj). This prevents confusion.
The condition ensures that the original wording is not mixed with the explanation.
5
Recognize the Ikhtilaf
Understand that there is a legitimate difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) between those who strictly prohibit any addition and those who allow explanation of rare words. The Hanafi school, following the author, tends to accept the latter with the necessary caution.
This difference impacts how hadith commentaries are composed and how jurists derive rulings from such texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن الكلم عن مواضعه وإن كَانَ ملحقاً بالكذابين وَلَمْ يقبل حديثه»(۱). إلا أن الحافظ السيوطي رأى أن تفسير الغريب الذي يقع في متن الْحَدِيْثِ غَيْر ممنوع، واستدل بفعل الزهري وغيره من أساطين الرِّوَايَة لَهُ. والذي أراه أن لا بأس بهذا الاستثناء لا سيما إذا أتي بفصل يبين المدرج، والله أعلم.
The third chapter: Difference in chain and text. 'Words from their places, and whoever is included among the liars, his hadith is not accepted' (1). However, al-Hafiz al-Suyuti held that explaining the unfamiliar (gharib) that occurs in the text of a hadith is not prohibited, and he used as evidence the action of al-Zuhri and other leading narrators. What I see is that there is no harm in this exception, especially if a section is provided clarifying the interpolation (mudraj). And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on differences in chain and text discusses the issue of interpolation (idraj) in hadith. The author begins with a quote from another work (Qawati' al-Adillah) that states that altering words from their proper places makes a narrator akin to liars and renders his hadith unacceptable. However, the author notes an exception advocated by al-Hafiz al-Suyuti: explaining unfamiliar (gharib) words that occur in the hadith text is not considered prohibited interpolation. Al-Suyuti argues that this is permissible based on the practice of early scholars like al-Zuhri, who would explain unusual terms. The author agrees with this exception, especially if the commentary clearly distinguishes the explanation from the original text (mudraj). This exception is relevant in fiqh when interpreting prophetic traditions that contain uncommon words.

Key Terms
المدرج (al-mudraj): An addition inserted into the text of a hadith by a narrator, which is not part of the original prophetic wording.
تفسير الغريب (tafsir al-gharib): Explanation of unfamiliar or rare words in the hadith text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The explanation must be a separate section that clarifies what is interpolation.
C) The explanation is only allowed for fiqh-related hadith.
D) The explanation must be in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
Explaining rare words in a hadith is permissible as an exception to the prohibition of interpolation, provided the commentary is clearly separated from the original text.

Introduction to Al-Qalb (Inversion) and Its Three Topics
Section heading outlining three sub-sections on al-qalb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'al-qalb' (inversion) and state its three main divisions: definition, types, and causes.

Core Idea
Inversion in hadith chains or texts can alter legal rulings, making it a key source of ikhtilaf among jurists.

Differences in hadith transmission—especially inversions in chains or texts—often lead to divergent legal rulings among jurists. This lesson introduces the concept of al-qalb (inversion) and outlines its three core subtopics: definition, types, and causes. Understanding this framework is essential before delving into detailed examples and applications in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Delineate the term
Identify what 'al-qalb' means in hadith studies: an inversion in the chain of narrators (isnad) or the text (matn) where the order is reversed or a narrator/word is replaced.
Do not confuse with other defects like idraj (insertion) or ziyada (addition).
2
Identify the three subtopics
Note the three subsections announced: definition, types, and causes. This structure will be followed in the subsequent material.
These three headings organize the entire discussion of inversion.
3
Connect to ikhtilaf
Reflect on how inversion can lead to different juristic rulings. For example, an inverted chain may change the apparent reliability of narrators, affecting the legal weight of the hadith.
This section specifically studies the 'effect on disagreement of jurists' (أثره في اختلاف الفقهاء).

This sets the stage for a detailed analysis that follows in the subsequent pages.
