Definition of al-Maqlub (The Inverted Hadith)
Defining the hadith classification al-Maqlub linguistically and terminologically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Maqlub in both linguistic and terminological senses and explain its significance in hadith criticism for Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Al-Maqlub is a hadith whose narrator inverts part of the sanad or matn, intentionally or unintentionally.

This lesson unpacks the term 'al-Maqlub' as used in hadith criticism and its impact on Hanafi legal methodology. We start with the Arabic root meaning 'turning' or 'inverting', then move to its technical definition. Understanding this term is crucial for evaluating the authenticity of Prophetic traditions—the second source of Islamic law after the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Define linguistically
Examine the Arabic root ق-ل-ب (qalb) and its meanings: turning a thing from its face, inverting, or investigating. The passage quotes Quranic verses and Ibn Faris to illustrate this.
The linguistic sense carries the core idea of change or reversal.
2
Define terminologically
State the technical definition: a hadith in which the narrator changes something in the chain (sanad) or text (matn), deliberately or by mistake.
This definition is directly from the source.
3
Identify the components
Note that inversion can occur in either sanad or matn. Both are included.
This breadth is important for classification.
4
Understand the scope
Recognize that the definition covers both intentional (ʿamd) and unintentional (sahw) actions by the narrator.
This is explicitly stated and often misunderstood.
5
Connect to fiqh
Consider how a maqlub hadith may affect hadith authenticity and thus the derivation of rulings in Hanafi fiqh. A maqlub hadith is generally considered weak unless the inversion is harmless or corrected.
This links the definition to practical usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الأول: تعريفه
المقلوب: اسم مفعول من قَلَبَ، ومعناه: تحويل الشيء عن وجهه، وقَلَبَه يَقلِبُه قَلْباً، وَقَدْ انقلب وقَلَب الشيء وقلبه. تقول: قلبت الشيء فانقلب: إذا كببته، وقلبه بيده تقليباً، وكلام مقلوب: ليس وجهه، والقَلْبُ: صرفك إنساناً تَقْلِبُه عن وجهه الذي يريد، وقلب الأمور: بحثها ونظر في عواقبها، ومنه قوله تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَقَلَّبُوا لَكَ الْأُمُورَ ﴾ (١)، وتقلب في الأمور والبلاد: تصرف فيها كيفما شاء، وفي التنزيل: ﴿ فَلَا يَغْرُرْكَ تَقَلِّبُهُمْ فِي الْبِلَادِ ﴾ (٢) وَقَالَ ابن فارس: «القاف واللام والباء أصلان صحيحان: أحدهما يدل على خالص الشيء وشريفه، والآخرِ عَلَى ردّ شيء من جهة إلى جهة». ومنه المثل العربي: أَقْلِبْ قَلاب يضرب لِمَنْ تفرط مِنْه سقطة، فيتلافاها بقلبها إلى غير معناها (٣). أما في الاصطلاح فهو الْحَدِيث الَّذِي أبدل فِيْهِ راويه شَيْئاً بآخر في السند أو في الْمَتْن عمداً أو سهواً). العلاقة بَيْنَ المعنى اللغوي والاصطلاحي: نلاحظ أن معنى القلب متوافر في المعنى الاصطلاحي، فهو في اللغة تغيير الشيء عن وجهه، فسمي بِهِ هَذَا الفعل في الاصطلاح فكأن الرَّاوِي قلب الْحَدِيث وأخرجه عن وجهه الصَّحِيح، عمداً كَانَ فعله أم سهواً.
First section: Its definition. Al-Maqlub: a passive participle from qalaba, meaning turning the thing from its face. And you turned it (qalabtahu) so it turned, and you flipped the thing, and inverted it. You say: I turned the thing so it turned meaning I upset it, and he turned it with his hand turning, and inverted speech: not its face. And al-qalb: your turning a person from the direction he intends. And turning over affairs: investigating them and looking at their consequences. From it is the saying of Allah: 'And they turned over for you the affairs' (9:48). And to move about in affairs and lands: to act in them as one wishes. In the revelation: 'So let not their moving about in the lands deceive you' (40:4). Ibn Faris said: 'Qaf, lam, ba are two sound roots: one indicates the pure and noble of a thing, and the other indicates returning something from one direction to another.' From it is the Arabic proverb: 'Invert the inversion' applied to one who makes a slip and then corrects it by inverting its meaning. As for terminology, it is the hadith in which its narrator changes something for another in the chain or in the text, intentionally or by mistake. The relationship between the linguistic and terminological meaning: We note that the meaning of inversion is present in the terminological meaning. In language it is changing the thing from its face, so this action is called by it in terminology as if the narrator inverted the hadith and brought it out from its correct face, intentionally or by mistake.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'al-Maqlub' (the inverted). It first gives the linguistic meaning from classical Arabic sources, showing that 'qalb' fundamentally means turning something from its intended direction or changing it. The definition is then applied to hadith terminology: a hadith is maqlub when its narrator inverts part of the chain (sanad) or text (matn), whether deliberately or accidentally. The passage also clarifies the relationship between the linguistic and terminological senses: both involve changing something from its proper form. This classification is important in hadith criticism and its impact on fiqh disagreements, as inversion can alter the meaning of a ruling. The text emphasizes that the action may be intentional or by mistake, so both are included.

Key Terms
المقلوب (al-maqlub): الحديث الذي أبدل فيه راويه شيئاً بآخر في السند أو في المتن عمداً أو سهواً
القلب (al-qalb): تحويل الشيء عن وجهه، أو التغيير في الحديث بإبدال جزء بآخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Maqlub is a hadith inverted in sanad or matn, intentionally or by mistake, and recognizing it is crucial for authenticating Prophetic traditions that form the basis of Hanafi rulings.

Identifying Flipped Isnad and Matn: Two Case Studies
Textual analysis of two flipped hadith examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a flipped isnad or matn in a hadith narration and evaluate its impact on the legal derivation from that hadith.

Core Idea
A flipped chain can reverse the text, causing misattribution of legal rulings.

In this lesson, we examine two real examples of flipped (maqlub) chains and texts from hadith literature. By analyzing how narrators like Ali ibn Uthman and Abu Muawiyah made errors, we learn to detect such flaws and understand their consequences for fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct narration
First, determine the widely accepted chain and text of the hadith from reliable narrators. For the Abu Hurayrah hadith, the correct chain is Muhammad ibn Ziyad via Ziyad from Abu Hurayrah. For the Ibn Mas'ud hadith, the correct version has Ibn Mas'ud saying 'I said another' in the text.
The correct narration is the one agreed upon by the majority of reliable narrators.
2
Spot the flipped version
Look for a narration that reverses either the chain (e.g., via a different transmitter) or the text (e.g., attributing a statement to the wrong speaker). In the first example, Ali ibn Uthman narrated via Muhammad ibn Sirin instead of Muhammad ibn Ziyad, and reversed the order of the texts. In the second, Abu Muawiyah made it appear that the Prophet said both sentences.
The flipped version contradicts the stronger narrations.
3
Compare narrator reliability
Assess the narrators of the flipped version against those of the correct version. Ali ibn Uthman contradicted Waki' and Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, who are more numerous and more memorizers. Abu Muawiyah contradicted several narrators like Abu Hamzah al-Sukkari, Hafs, and Shu'bah.
The correct narration comes from a more reliable or larger group.
4
Determine the effect on legal content
The flipped text changes the attribution of statements, which can affect the legal ruling derived. In the Ibn Mas'ud hadith, the flipped version would make the Prophet state both the reward for tawhid and the punishment for shirk, whereas the correct version distinguishes the Prophet's words from Ibn Mas'ud's own comment. This affects how the ruling on entry into Paradise is understood.
Errors in isnad and matn can lead to incorrect fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: الاختلاف في السند والمتن

الثانية، وتابع حماد بن سلمة عَلَى الرِّوَايَة الثانية عن مُحَمَّد بن زياد: شعبة)، والربيع بن مُسْلِم (۳) القرشي (۳) فرووه عن مُحَمَّد بن زياد، عن زياد، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة برواية الثانية. كَما أن علي بن عثمان اللاحقي قد قلب الإسناد والمتن في موقع آخر فَقَدْ رَوَى عن حماد سلمة، عن أيوب وهشام، عن بن مُحَمَّد بن سيرين، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة برواية الأولى المقلوبة المَتْن فَقَد خالف هنا وكيعاً، وعبد الرَّحْمن بن مهدي الَّذِينَ الْحَدِيث بن روياه عن حماد سلمة، عن بن زياد، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، برواية الثانية كما مَرَّ، مُحَمَّد فعلي بن عثمان خالف هنا من هم أحفظ مِنْهُ عدداً وحفظاً أَيضاً وخالفهم هنا في السند والمتن، كَمَا أَن هَذَا الْحَدِيث لَمْ يرو من طريق مُحَمَّد بن سيرين، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة، إلا من رواية علي بن عثمان، فَقَدْ روي من عدة تابعين عن أبي هُرَيْرَة وليس فِيهِمْ مُحَمَّد بن سيرين (٤) (۱) عِنْدَ ابن الجعد (۱۱۷۲)، وإسحاق بن راهويه (٩١) ، وأحمد ٤٥٦/٢، ومسلم ٩١/٧ (١٣٣٧) (۱۳۱). (۲) هُوَ الربيع بن مُسْلِم القرشي الجمحي، أبو بكر البصري : ثقة، توفي سنة (١٦٧ هـ). تهذيب الكمال ٤٦٥/٢ (١٨٥٦) ، والكاشف (۳۹۲/۱ (١٥٤٠)، والتقريب (۱۹۰۱). (۳) عِنْدَ إسحاق بن راهويه (٦٠) ، وأحمد ٥٠۸/٢ ، ومسلم (۱۰۲٤ (۱۳۳۷) (٤١٢)، والنسائي ٥/ ١١٠ وفي الكبرى لَهُ (۳۵۹۸) وابن خزيمة (٢٥٠٨)، والطحاوي في شرح مشكل الآثار (١٤٧٢) ، وابن حبان (٣٧٠٤) (۳۷۰۵) ، والدارقطني ٢٨١/٢، والبيهقي ٣٢٦/٤. (٤) إذ روي من طريق مُحَمَّد بن زياد عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا تقدم تخريجه. وروي من طريق أبي سلمة بن عبد الرحمان وسعيد بن المسيب كَمَا أخرجه مُسْلِم ٩١/٧ (۱۳۳۷) (۱۳۰)، والطحاوي في شرح المشكل (٥٤٨) (٥٥١) (٥٥٢)، عن أبي سلمة وحده وروي من طريق أبي صالح عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه أحمد ٣٥٥/٢ و ٤٩٥، ومسلم ٩١/٧ (۱۳۳۷) (۱۳۱)، وابن ماجه (۱) و (۲)، والترمذي (٢٦۷۹)، والطحاوي في شرح المشكل (٥٥٤) (٥٥٣). وروي من طريق الأعرج عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه مالك في الموطأ (٩٩٦) برواية مُحَمَّد بن الحسن الشيباني، والشافعي في المسند (۱۸۰۲) بتحقيقنا، والحميدي (١١٢٥)، وأحمد ٢٥٨/٢ والبخاري ۱۱۶/٩ (۷۲۸۸)، ومسلم (۹۱/۷ (۱۳۳۷) (۱۳۱)، وأبو يعلى (٦٣٠٥)، والطحاوي في شرح المشكل (٥٤٩ ) (٥٥٠) ، وابن حبان (۱۸) (۱۹) (۲۰) (۲۱). وروي من طريق الحارث عم الحارث بن عَبْد الرحمان بن عَبْد الله، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه أبو يعلى (٦٦٧٦). وروي من طريق عبد الرحمان بن أبي عمرة، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه أحمد ٤٨٢/٢. وروي من طريق عجلان، عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه الشَّافِعِي في المسند (۱۸۰۱) بتحقيقنا، والحميدي (۱۱۲٥)، وأحمد ۲٤٧/٢ و ٤۲۸ و ٥١٧، وابن حبان (١٨) (٢١٠٦). وروي من طريق همام بن منبه عن أبي هُرَيْرَة كَمَا أخرجه عَبْد الرزاق (٢٠٣٧٤)، واحمد ٢ ۳۱۳، ومسلم ۱/۷ (۱۳۳۷) (۱۳۱)، وابن حبان (۲۰) (۲۱) (۲۱۰۵)، والبغوي في شرح السنة

ومثاله: ما سبق في نوع المدرج في حَدِيث عبد الله بن مسعود، إِذْ روي مقلوباً من طريق أبي معاوية، عن الأعمش، عن شقيق بن سلمة، عن عبد الله بن مسعود، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُول الله الله كلمة وقلت أخرى، قَالَ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (من مات لا يشرك بالله شَيْئاً دخل الجنة) قَالَ: وقلت أنا من مات يشرك بالله شَيْئاً دخل النار). فَقَدْ خالف أبو معاوية بقية الرُّوَاة عن الأعمش، إِذْ رَوَاهُ عَنْهُ: ١. أبو حمزة السكري عِنْدَ البخاري (°) (٤) حفص بن غياث عِنْدَ البخاري ) ، وابن منده ,(V) (1) (۱۱) شعبة: عِنْدَ الطيالسي ، وأحمد ()، والنسائي)، وابن خزيمة(١٠)، والشاشي (١١)، والخطيب (۱۳) .(۹۹) (۹۸) فجميعهم رووه عن أبي هُرَيْرَة وفيه جعلوا إعطاء الاستطاعة عَلَى القيام بالعمل المأمور بالقيام به ووجوب عدم إتيان العمل المنهي عَنْهُ مطلقاً كَمَا في الرِّوَايَة الثانية وهذا يدل على خطأ راويه علي بن عثمان.
Chapter Three: Differences in Isnad and Matn. Secondly, Hammad ibn Salamah followed the second narration from Muhammad ibn Ziyad: Shu'bah and al-Rabi' ibn Muslim al-Qurashi narrated it from Muhammad ibn Ziyad, from Ziyad, from Abu Hurayrah as the second narration. Likewise, Ali ibn Uthman al-Lahiqi flipped the isnad and matn in another place: he narrated from Hammad ibn Salamah, from Ayyub and Hisham, from Muhammad ibn Sirin, from Abu Hurayrah as the first flipped matn. So he contradicted Waki' and Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, who narrated it from Hammad ibn Salamah, from Muhammad ibn Ziyad, from Abu Hurayrah as the second narration as passed. Ali ibn Uthman contradicted those who were more numerous and more memorizers than him, and he contradicted them in isnad and matn. Also this hadith was not narrated via Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayrah except through the narration of Ali ibn Uthman. It has been narrated from several followers from Abu Hurayrah, and Muhammad ibn Sirin is not among them. (Footnote 1) from Ibn al-Ja'd, etc. (Footnote 2) He is al-Rabi' ibn Muslim... (Footnote 3) from Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, etc. (Footnote 4) It has been narrated via Muhammad ibn Ziyad from Abu Hurayrah as previously referenced. And via Abu Salamah, etc. And via Abu Salih, etc. And via al-A'raj, etc. And via al-Harith, etc. And via Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Amrah, etc. And via Ajlan, etc. And via Hammam ibn Munabbih, etc. And an example of it: what preceded in the type of mudraj in the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, when it was narrated flipped via Abu Muawiyah, from al-A'mash, from Shaqiq ibn Salamah, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: The Messenger of Allah said a word and I said another. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise.' He said: And I said: Whoever dies associating anything with Allah enters Hellfire.' So Abu Muawiyah contradicted the rest of the narrators from al-A'mash, when they narrated it from him: 1. Abu Hamzah al-Sukkari according to al-Bukhari; Hafs ibn Ghiyath according to al-Bukhari and Ibn Mandah; Shu'bah according to al-Tayalisi, Ahmad, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Shashi, and al-Khatib. So all of them narrated it from Abu Hurayrah, and in it they placed the giving of ability to perform the commanded action and the obligation of not committing the prohibited action absolutely, as in the second narration. And this indicates the error of its narrator Ali ibn Uthman.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis discussing two cases of flipped (maqlub) chains and texts in hadith, demonstrating how such errors affect the reliability of narrations. The author first discusses a hadith of Abu Hurayrah about 'giving ability to perform commanded actions and avoiding prohibited ones'. The correct narration (second version) comes from Muhammad ibn Ziyad via Ziyad from Abu Hurayrah, narrated by Hammad ibn Salamah and others like Shu'bah and al-Rabi'. However, Ali ibn Uthman al-Lahiqi flipped both the chain and text: he narrated via Muhammad ibn Sirin instead of Muhammad ibn Ziyad, and reversed the content such that the first narration became flipped. He contradicted trustworthy narrators like Waki' and Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi. The author notes that this hadith is not known from Muhammad ibn Sirin except through Ali ibn Uthman, and lists multiple other chains from Abu Hurayrah that do not include Ibn Sirin, indicating Ali's error. The second example is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about 'whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise'. The correct version has Ibn Mas'ud saying: 'The Prophet said a word and I said another. The Prophet said: Whoever dies not associating anything with Allah enters Paradise. And I said: Whoever dies associating anything with Allah enters Hellfire.' Abu Muawiyah flipped this by attributing the statement 'and I said another' to the Prophet, making it appear that the Prophet said both sentences. Other reliable narrators from al-A'mash narrated it correctly, so Abu Muawiyah's version is erroneous. The passage concludes that all those correct narrators narrated from Abu Hurayrah with the second version, confirming Ali ibn Uthman's error.

Key Terms
مقلوب (maqlub): A hadith where the chain (isnad) or text (matn) is flipped or reversed by a narrator.
الإسناد (al-isnad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith.
المتن (al-matn): The text or content of a hadith.
مدرج (mudraj): A hadith where a narrator inserts his own words into the text, making them appear part of the prophetic statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about tawhid, what error did Abu Muawiyah commit?
A) He added extra narrators to the chain.
B) He flipped the chain by attributing the statement 'and I said another' to the Prophet instead of himself.
C) He changed the wording of the hadith entirely.
D) He narrated a different hadith altogether.

Key Takeaway
Flipped chains and texts distort the attribution of statements, compromising the reliability of the hadith for legal derivation.

Causes of Inversion in Hadith – First Two Causes
Listing and explaining two causes of inversion in hadith chains

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the first two causes of inversion (qalb) in hadith chains and state the scholarly response to each.

Core Idea
Qalb can be deliberate (to seek fame) or due to narrator negligence; both undermine hadith reliability.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work examines why inversion occurs in hadith chains. The author lists three causes, but the present passage covers two: the narrator's desire to appear unique, and the narrator's lack of precision. Understanding these causes helps us evaluate the strength of transmitted proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes
Read carefully to find the two causes mentioned: (1) the narrator's desire to introduce strangeness (gharaba), (2) the narrator's lack of precision or vigilance.
The third cause is not given in this passage.
2
Analyze the first cause: seeking gharaba
The narrator deliberately inverts parts of the hadith to make it appear unique, so people will seek to learn from him. This is a form of deception.
Imam Ahmad condemned seeking strange hadith because they are often weak.
3
Analyze the second cause: narrator negligence
The narrator may be trustworthy but not a precise memorizer; he may not notice inversion. Scholars must vet narrators for vigilance and memory.
The second cause is about inherent capability, not deliberate intent.
4
Apply the scholarly response
For the first cause, scholars avoided gharaba. For the second, they closely examined narrators' memory and awareness of inversion.
Al-Bukhari and others practiced this vetting.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul
In Hanafi fiqh, the reliability of hadith is paramount. These causes help a mufti assess whether a narration can be used as evidence (dalil).
This is a practical tool for evaluating transmitted proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثالث / أسباب القلب
مِمَّا لا شك فيه أن قابليات الرُّوَاة تتفاوت ما بَيْنَ إتقان وضبط وتعاهد للمحفوظ، ثُمَّ إنهم مختلفون في ما ركزه الله فيهم من العدالة أو ضدها، وعليه فقد اختلفت دوافع القلب في المرويات تبعاً لهذا التفاوت، ويمكن أن نجعل جملة الأسباب التي تؤدي بوقوع القلب في حَدِيْثِ الرُّوَاة ثلاثة هِيَ
: رغبة الرَّاوِي في إيقاع الغرابة في حديثه ليُرَغْبَ الناس حَتَّى يظنوا أنه يروي ما ليس عِنْدَ غيره فيقبلوا عَلَى التحمل مِنْهُ عَلَى نحو ما وقع في حَدِيث حماد بن عمرو النصيبي الَّذِي سقناه قبل قليل. ولهذا السبب كره أهل الْحَدِيث تتبع الغرائب، قَالَ الإمام أحمد: «لا تكتبوا هَذِهِ الأحاديث الغرائب فإنها مناكير وعامتها عن الضعفاء». الإمعان في التثبت من حال المحدّث أحافظ هُوَ أم غَيْر حافظ؟ وهل يفطن لما وقع في الحديث من القلب أم لا؟ فإن تبين له أنه حافظ متيقظ يطمئن القلب في الْحَدِيث عَنْهُ، أَقبل عَلَى التحمل عَنْهُ، وإن تبين لَهُ خلاف ذَلِكَ، بأن كانت فيه غفلة أو بلادة ذهن أعرض عنه وتركه. وقع للبخاري والعقيلي والفضل بن دكين ومحمد بن عجلان والمزي وغيرهم - مِمَّا أسلفنا ذكرهم
The third requirement / Causes of Inversion. There is no doubt that the capabilities of narrators vary in terms of mastery, precision, and care for what is memorized. Furthermore, they differ in what Allah has instilled in them of integrity or its opposite. Accordingly, the motives for inversion in narrations differ according to this variation. It is possible to make the total causes that lead to the occurrence of inversion in the hadith of narrators three: 1. The narrator's desire to introduce strangeness in his hadith so that people will desire it, until they think that he narrates what is not with others, so they accept taking from him, similar to what occurred in the hadith of Hammad ibn Amr al-Nasibi which we mentioned a short while ago. For this reason, hadith scholars disliked pursuing strange hadith. Imam Ahmad said: 'Do not write these strange hadiths, for they are rejected (munkar) and most of them come from weak narrators.' 2. Thorough investigation of the state of the narrator: is he a memorizer or not? And does he perceive what has occurred in the hadith of inversion or not? If it becomes clear that he is a vigilant memorizer whose heart is comfortable with his hadith, he accepts taking from him. And if the opposite becomes clear, that there is in him negligence or dullness of mind, he turns away from him and leaves him. This was done by al-Bukhari, al-Aqeeli, al-Fadl ibn Dukayn, Muhammad ibn Ajlan, al-Mizzi, and others - as we have previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on differences in chain and text introduces the third sub-topic: Causes of Inversion (قلب). The author begins by acknowledging that narrators vary in their capabilities like mastery, precision, and care, as well as in their integrity. Consequently, the motives for inversion differ. He then promises three causes, but only the first two are detailed in this portion. The first cause is the narrator's deliberate desire to make his hadith appear strange or unique, to attract listeners and make them think he possesses rare narrations. This leads to students seeking him out. An example is given of Hammad ibn Amr al-Nasibi. Because of this, hadith scholars strongly discouraged seeking out strange hadith. Imam Ahmad is quoted saying not to write such strange hadith because they are munkar (rejected) and mostly from weak narrators. The second cause is the thorough vetting of a narrator's reliability. The investigator examines whether the narrator is a precise memorizer who would notice any inversion in his own hadith. If he is a vigilant memorizer, one is comfortable taking from him; if he is negligent or dull-witted, his hadith is abandoned. This method was employed by major scholars like al-Bukhari, al-Aqeeli, and others. The third cause is not provided in this passage but is presumably given in the following pages.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): Inversion in the chain or text of a hadith, where parts are reversed or rearranged, affecting its authenticity or meaning.
الغرابة (al-gharābah): Strangeness or uniqueness of a hadith, often indicating that it has few narrators or is unfamiliar.
المنكر (al-munkar): A hadith that is rejected due to weakness or contradiction with stronger narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the second cause of inversion according to the passage?
A) The narrator deliberately changes the chain to impress his teachers.
B) The narrator is reliable but may have inversion due to poor memory or inattentiveness.
C) The narrator is a fabricator who invents false chains.
D) The narrator copies from written sources that contain errors.

Key Takeaway
Inversion in hadith can be either deliberate (to attract attention) or unintentional (due to narrator negligence); both require careful scrutiny by hadith scholars.

Narrator Error: Inversion (Qalb) in Hadith Chains
Defines narrator error (inversion) and gives an example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an inverted hadith chain (qalb) and apply the Hanafi rule that accidental inversion is excusable unless frequent.

Core Idea
An inverted chain is serious only if intentional; accidental inversions are excused unless they recur.

In this lesson, we examine a specific type of narrator error: inversion (qalb) of a hadith chain. Using the example of the hadith about standing for prayer, the passage shows how a single narrator's mistake can create a false chain, and how hadith scholars detect and correct it. Understanding this error is crucial for evaluating the reliability of narrations in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of qalb
Locate the passage's definition: qalb is an inversion of the chain that occurs out of forgetfulness, not intent.
The author contrasts accidental and deliberate qalb.
2
Note the condition for excusing the narrator
The narrator is excused if the error is infrequent; frequent errors lead to abandonment.
This is key for evaluating narrators in practice.
3
Trace the erroneous chain and the correct chain
Jarir ibn Hazim narrated via Thabit from Anas. The correct chain is via Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father.
The passage lists many corroborators of the correct chain.
4
Recognize the method of correction
Scholars compare multiple transmissions; the majority of reliable narrators support the correct chain, revealing the error.
This method is often used in hadith criticism.

خطأ الرَّاوِي وغلطه بأن يقع القلب في حديثه من باب السهو لا العمد، وهذا النوع راويه معذور فيه؛ لأنه لم يقصد إيقاعه، إلا أنه إذا كثر في حديثه استحق الترك(1). مثاله: الْحَدِيث الَّذِي رَوَاهُ جرير بن حازم، عن ثابت البناني، عن أنس قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُول الله إذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا تقوموا حَتَّى تروني(2). فهذا الْحَدِيث انقلب إسناده عَلَى جرير، وإنما هُوَ مشهور ليحيى بن أبي كثير، عن عبد الله بن أبي قتادة عن أبيه، عن النبي الله، وهكذا رَوَاهُ الجمع، عن يحيى بن أبي كَثِير مِنْهُمْ: ١ أبان: عِند أبي داود(3). ٢ حجاج بن أبي عثمان الصواف: عِنْدَ مُسْلِم، وابن خزيمة، وأبي عوانة، وابن حبان، وأبي نعيم في المستخرج. ٣ شيبان: عِنْدَ البُخَارِيّ، ومسلم، وأبي عوانة، وأبي نعيم في المستخرج. ٤ علي بن المبارك: عِنْدَ البخاري، وأبي عوانة، وابن حبان. ٥ معاوية بن سلام: عِنْدَ ابن خزيمة. ٦ معمر: عِنْدَ عَبْد الرزاق، وابن أبي شيبة، ومسلم، والترمذي، وأبي عوانة، وابن حبان، وأبي نعيم في المستخرج. ٧ هشام: عِنْدَ البُخَارِيّ، والدارمي، وأبي نعيم في مستخرجه، والبيهقي. ٨ همام: عِنْدَ الدارمي. قال الترمذي: «سألت محمداً هَذَا الْحَدِيث فَقَالَ: هُوَ حَدِيْث خطأ، أخطأ فِيْهِ جرير بن حازم. ذكروا أن الحجاج الصوّاف كَانَ عِنْدَ ثابت البناني، وجرير بن حازم في المجلس، فحدّث الحجاج، عن يحيى بن أبي كثير، عن عبد الله بن أبي قتادة، عن أبيه، عن النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا تقوموا حَتَّى تروني»، فوهم فيه جرير بن حازم فظن أن ثابتاً حدثه عن أنس بهذا(20).
The narrator's error and mistake: that a heart (inversion) occurs in his hadith out of forgetfulness, not intentionally. This type, its narrator is excused because he did not intend to commit it, but if it becomes frequent in his hadith, he deserves to be abandoned. Example: The hadith narrated by Jarir ibn Hazim from Thabit al-Bunani from Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When the prayer is established, do not stand until you see me.' This hadith's chain was inverted upon Jarir; rather it is well-known from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father from the Prophet. Thus the group narrated it from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir, among them: 1. Aban: in Abu Dawud. 2. Hajjaj ibn Abi Uthman al-Sawwaf: in Muslim, Ibn Khuzayma, Abu Awana, Ibn Hibban, and Abu Nu'aym in al-Mustakhraj. 3. Shayban: in al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Awana, and Abu Nu'aym in al-Mustakhraj. 4. Ali ibn al-Mubarak: in al-Bukhari, Abu Awana, and Ibn Hibban. 5. Muawiya ibn Sallam: in Ibn Khuzayma. 6. Ma'mar: in Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, Abu Awana, Ibn Hibban, and Abu Nu'aym in al-Mustakhraj. 7. Hisham: in al-Bukhari, al-Darimi, Abu Nu'aym in his Mustakhraj, and al-Bayhaqi. 8. Hammam: in al-Darimi. Al-Tirmidhi said: 'I asked Muhammad (al-Bukhari) about this hadith, and he said: It is a mistaken hadith; Jarir ibn Hazim made an error in it. They mentioned that al-Hajjaj al-Sawwaf was with Thabit al-Bunani and Jarir ibn Hazim in the gathering, and al-Hajjaj narrated from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir, from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada, from his father, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: "When the prayer is established, do not stand until you see me." Jarir ibn Hazim made a mistake in it, thinking that Thabit narrated it to him from Anas with this.'
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage defines a category of hadith error: qalb (inversion) caused by forgetfulness, not deliberate. The narrator is excused unless it becomes frequent. Then it provides an example of an inverted chain: the famous hadith about not standing for prayer until seeing the imam. The correct chain is via Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father, but Jarir mistakenly thought it came from Thabit from Anas. The passage lists many reliable narrators who transmitted the correct version. This shows how a single narrator's error can create a variant chain, and how hadith critics identify and correct such errors. In Hanafi fiqh, this hadith is used to derive the ruling that the congregation should not stand until the imam is visible, which is a practice in some schools.

Key Terms
قلب (qalb): Inversion of a hadith chain, where the nurse was mistakenly changed.
خطأ الراوي (khatʾ al-rāwī): The narrator's unintentional mistake in transmission, such as inversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Jarir ibn Hazim from Thabit al-Bunani from Anas from the Prophet
B) Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father from the Prophet

D) Shayban from Anas from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
An accidental inversion (qalb) in a hadith chain does not automatically invalidate the narrator; it is considered in context of frequency.

Tashif and Tahrif: Definitions and Distinction
Defining and distinguishing tashif and tahrif as causes of textual disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tashif and tahrif, distinguish them according to Ibn Hajar, and explain their significance in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Tashif changes dots; tahrif changes vowels – both distort hadith and can alter rulings.

Understanding textual errors like tashif and tahrif is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh, because a single mis-dotted word can transform a command into a prohibition. This lesson examines the definitions and the critical distinction made by Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani that separates these two types of error.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the category of textual error
Identify that tashif and tahrif are two types of textual distortion in hadith transmission, both in chain and text.
They belong to the broader category of narrator errors that lead to juristic disagreement.
2
Define tashif precisely
Tashif is a change in the dots (nuqat) or vowel signs (harakat) of letters while the skeletal script (rasm) remains unchanged. Example: changing ب into ت.
Ibn Hajar specifies: if the change is in dots, it's tashif; if in vowel signs, it's tahrif.
3
Define tahrif precisely
Tahrif is a broader distortion: addition, deletion, substitution, or misplacement that changes the intended meaning. It includes but is not limited to vowel changes.
Early scholars used both terms interchangeably before Ibn Hajar.
4
Apply Ibn Hajar's distinction
Memorize the rule: error in dots = tashif; error in vowel signs = tahrif. This distinction helps in categorizing errors and assessing their impact on hadith authenticity.
This differentiation is a standard in hadith criticism.
5
Connect to fiqh implications
A single tashif can convert a legal command into a different ruling. Hanafi usul requires careful examination of hadith wording to avoid deriving rulings from corrupted texts.
Works with concepts like 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' but here the focus is textual accuracy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثامن: الاختلاف بسبب التصحيف والتحريف. التصحيف والتحريف من الأمور الطارئة الَّتِني تقع في الْحَدِيث سنداً أو متناً عِنْدَ بعض الرُّوَاة، وَهُوَ من الأمور المؤدية إلى الاختلاف في الْحَدِيث. فيحصل لبعض الرُّوَاة أوهام تقع في السند أو في الْمَتْن بتغيير النقط أو الشكل أو الحروف. وهذا النوع من الخطأ عِنْدَ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ بـ (التصحيف والتحريف). والتصحيف هُوَ: تغيير في نقط الحروف أو حركاتها مع بقاء صورة الخط ). والتحريف: هُوَ العدول بالشيء عن جهته، وحرَّف الكلام تحريفاً عدل به عن جهته، وَقَدْ يَكُون بالزيادة فيه، أو النقص مِنْهُ، وَقَدْ يَكُون بتبديل بعض كلماته، وَقَدْ يَكُون بجعله عَلَى غَيْر المراد مِنْهُ؛ فالتحريف أعم من التصحيف. ولا بدّ من الإشارة إلى أن المتقدمين كانوا يطلقون المصحف والمحرف جميعاً عَلَى شيء واحد، ولكن الحافظ ابن حجر جعلهما شيئين وخالف بينهما، فَقَدْ قَالَ: «إن كانت المخالفة بتغيير حرف أو حروف مع بقاء صورة الخط في السياق فإن كَانَ ذَلِكَ بالنسبة إلى النقط فالمصحف، وإن كَانَ بالنسبة إلى الشكل فالمحرّف).
Eighth Section: Disagreement due to tashif and tahrif. Tashif and tahrif are among the incidental matters that occur in hadith, in chain or text, by some narrators, and they are among the matters leading to disagreement in hadith. Some narrators have illusions occurring in the chain or text by changing dots, vowel signs, or letters. And this type of error by the muhaddithun is called (tashif and tahrif). And tashif is: a change in the dots of letters or their vowel signs while the form of the script remains. And tahrif is: turning something away from its intended direction; one has 'harrafa' speech when he turns it away from its intended direction. It can be by adding to it, or subtracting from it, or by changing some of its words, or by placing it in a way other than what is intended. So tahrif is more general than tashif. It must be noted that the early scholars used to apply the terms 'musahhaf' and 'muharraf' to the same thing, but al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar made them two separate things and differentiated between them. He said: 'If the discrepancy is by changing a letter or letters while the form of the script remains in the context, then if that is concerning the dots, it is tashif; if it is concerning the vowel signs, it is tahrif.'
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage defines two technical terms in hadith criticism: tashif and tahrif. Both are errors that cause discrepancies in narration. Tashif specifically refers to changing the diacritical dots (e.g., changing 'bā'' to 'tā'' or 'thā'') or the vowel marks while the skeletal script (rasm) remains unchanged. Tahrif is broader: it means distorting the text by addition, omission, substitution, or misplacement, resulting in a change of meaning. The author notes that early scholars used the terms interchangeably, but Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani distinguished them: if the error is in the dots, it's tashif; if in the vowel signs, it's tahrif. This distinction is important because misreading hadith due to dotting errors can lead to different juristic rulings, especially in Hanafi fiqh where precise textual transmission is critical for deduction.

Key Terms
تصحيف (tashif): Changing the dots or vowel signs of a letter while the script form remains intact.
تحريف (tahrif): Distorting the text by addition, deletion, substitution, or misplacement, changing the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hajar's distinction, what is the difference between tashif and tahrif?
A) Tashif is a grammatical error, while tahrif is a spelling error
B) Tashif involves changing the dots of letters, tahrif involves changing the vowel signs
C) Tashif occurs only in the text, tahrif only in the chain
D) There is no difference; they are the same thing

Key Takeaway
Tashif and tahrif are distinct textual errors: dot changes = tashif, vowel changes = tahrif, both potentially altering legal rulings.

Using Lexical Authority to Refute a Fiqh Objection
Refutation using lexical citations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Hanafi usul uses lexical authority to refute a fiqh-related claim and apply this method to similar textual ambiguities.

Core Idea
Lexicographers are authoritative for word meanings; their statements can refute a fiqh objection.

Sometimes a fiqh dispute hinges on the correct meaning of a word. In this passage, the author refutes an opponent who claimed that camel knees are not in their forelegs, a point relevant to prostration in prayer. The refutation relies not on hadith or qiyas, but on the explicit statements of renowned Arabic lexicographers. This shows that in Hanafi usul, linguistic consensus is a valid source for determining the proper meaning of terms used in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim Being Refuted
The opponent stated that camel knees are not in their hands (forelegs) and that this is unknown among linguists. First, pinpoint the exact claim.
2
Note the Refutation Method
The author does not use a revealed text but cites three major lexicographers (Al-Azhari, Ibn Sidah, Ibn Manzur) who explicitly state the opposite. Observe the weight given to lexical authority.
This is an example of istishhad bi-ahl al-lughah.
3
Connect to Fiqh Application
The camel knee location affects the description of prostration (sajdah) because the sunnah is to prostrate like a camel on its hands. Understanding the word 'knee' correctly is essential for the proper ruling.
The Hanafi school holds that the camel's knees are in the forelegs, so prostration on the hands is analogous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما قوله بأن ركبتي البعير ليست في يديه، وأنه لا يعرف عن أهل اللغة ذلك، فمنقوض بتصريح كبار أئمة اللغة بأن ركبتي البعير في يديه مِنْهُمْ: الأزهري، وابن سیده، وابن منظور، وغيرهم
As for his statement that the knees of a camel are not in its hands, and that this is not known from the people of language, it is refuted by the explicit statements of the major imams of language that the knees of a camel are in its hands, among them: Al-Azhari, Ibn Sidah, Ibn Manzur, and others.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. Someone claimed that the knees of a camel are not located in its forelegs (hands), and that this is not a known usage among Arabic linguists. The author refutes this by citing major lexicographers (Al-Azhari, Ibn Sidah, Ibn Manzur) who explicitly state that the knees of a camel are in its hands. This is important in Hanafi fiqh because the position of the camel's knees relates to rulings on prostration and the description of prayer. The Hanafi position holds that the camel's knees are in its forelegs, consistent with these linguistic authorities.

Key Terms
ركبة البعير (rukbat al-ba‘īr): The knee of a camel; a point on the foreleg that is analogous to the human knee.

Distinguishing Tashif and Tahrif in Hadith
Defines and distinguishes tashif and tahrif in hadith transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tashif and tahrif, distinguish between them according to Ibn Hajar's classification, and explain their impact on hadith preservation and fiqh derivation.

Core Idea
Tashif alters diacritical dots; tahrif alters vowel marks or words—both corrupt hadith and must be identified.

Errors in hadith transmission can arise from changes in writing or meaning. Among these, tashif and tahrif are two critical types that lead to variation in textual understanding. This lesson unpacks their definitions, the early interchangeability of terms, and Ibn Hajar's precise distinction—essential knowledge for any student of usul al-fiqh aiming to safeguard the prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Read the passage and locate the definitions of tashif and tahrif. Note that both are errors in hadith transmission, either in the chain or text.
Tashif is specifically about dots/vowels; tahrif is broader.
2
Recognize early usage
Understand that early scholars used both terms for the same type of error. The passage notes this to show the evolution of terminology.
This is a historical point—terminology refined over time.
3
Apply Ibn Hajar's distinction
Ibn Hajar differentiated: if the change is in diacritical dots, it is tashif; if in vowel marks, it is tahrif. This is the standard later distinction.
Remember: dots vs. vowel marks.
4
Understand the impact on fiqh
Errors in hadith can lead to different rulings. For example, a misread word might change an obligation to a recommendation. Knowledge of these errors helps prevent incorrect derivation.
This links to usul al-fiqh: accuracy of source texts is foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثامن
الاختلاف بسبب التصحيف والتحريف
يسمى التصحيف والتحريف من الأمور الطارئة الَّتِني تقع في الْحَدِيث سنداً أو متناً عِنْدَ بعض الرُّوَاة، وَهُوَ من الأمور المؤدية إلى الاختلاف في الْحَدِيث. فيحصل لبعض الرُّوَاة أوهام تقع في السند أو في الْمَتْن بتغيير النقط أو الشكل أو الحروف. الخطأ وهذا النوع من عِنْدَ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ بـ (التصحيف والتحريف). والتصحيف هُوَ: تغيير في نقط الحروف أو حركاتها مع بقاء صورة الخط ). والتحريف: هُوَ العدول بالشيء عن جهته، وحرَّف الكلام تحريفاً عدل به عن جهته، وَقَدْ يَكُون بالزيادة فيه، أو النقص مِنْهُ، وَقَدْ يَكُون بتبديل بعض كلماته، وَقَدْ يَكُون بجعله عَلَى غَيْر المراد مِنْهُ؛ فالتحريف أعم من التصحيف (۸).
ولا بدّ من الإشارة إلى أن المتقدمين كانوا يطلقون المصحف والمحرف جميعاً عَلَى شيء واحد، ولكن الحافظ ابن حجر جعلهما شيئين وخالف بينهما، فَقَدْ قَالَ: «إن كانت المخالفة بتغيير حرف أو حروف مع بقاء صورة الخط في السياق فإن كَانَ ذَلِكَ بالنسبة إلى النقط فالمصحف، وإن كَانَ بالنسبة إلى الشكل فالمحرّف).
وعلى هَذَا فالتصحيف هُوَ الَّذِي يَكُون في النقط؛ أي في الحروف المتشابهة الَّتِي تختلف في قراءتها مثل : الباء والتاء والثاء والجيم والحاء المهملة والخاء المعجمة، والدال المهملة والذال المعجمة والراء والزاي.
ومعرفة هَذَا الفن من فنون علم الْحَدِيث لَهُ أهمية كبيرة)؛ وذلك لما فيه من تنقية الأحاديث النبوية مِمَّا شابها في بعض الألفاظ سواء كان في متونها أم في رجال أسانيدها.
وعندما كثر التصحيف والتحريف بَيْنَ الناس شرع الحفاظ من أهل الحديث في تأليف المصنفات لضبط الروايات. وقد صنف في هذا الفن عدة كتب منها: [ثم يسرد قائمة طويلة من الكتب]
The eighth section: Difference due to tashif and tahrif. Tashif and tahrif are among the incidental matters that occur in hadith, whether in the chain or the text, by some narrators. They are among the things leading to difference in hadith. Some narrators make mistakes in the chain or text by changing the diacritical points or the vowel marks or the letters. This type of error is called by hadith scholars 'tashif and tahrif'. Tashif is: change in the diacritical points of letters or their vowel marks while the form of the writing remains. Tahrif is: turning something away from its proper direction; one 'harrafa' speech means he altered it from its proper direction. It may be by increase, or decrease, or by replacing some words, or by making it contrary to its intended meaning; thus tahrif is more general than tashif. It must be noted that the early scholars used to apply 'musahhaf' and 'muharraf' both to the same thing, but al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar made them two distinct things and differentiated between them. He said: 'If the discrepancy is by changing a letter or letters while the form of the line remains in the context, then if that concerns the diacritical points, it is musahhaf; if it concerns the vowel marks, it is muharraf.' Accordingly, tashif is that which occurs in the diacritical points; i.e., in letters that are similar and differ in reading such as ba, ta, tha, jim, ha (without dot), kha (with dot), dal (without dot), dhal (with dot), ra, and zay. Knowledge of this art among the arts of hadith science is of great importance; because it purifies the prophetic hadiths from what has tainted them in some expressions, whether in their texts or in their chains of narrators. When tashif and tahrif became widespread among people, the hadith preservers began to compile works to correct the narrations. Several books have been written on this art, including: [list of books]
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of tashif and tahrif as sources of difference in hadith transmission. Tashif specifically refers to changes in the diacritical dots of letters (e.g., confusing 'ba' and 'ta', 'jim' and 'kha'), while tahrif is a broader term for any alteration of words—by addition, subtraction, substitution, or distortion of meaning. The early scholars often used the terms interchangeably, but Ibn Hajar distinguished them: tashif is dot-related, tahrif is vowel-mark-related. This distinction is crucial for understanding how textual corruption can lead to differing rulings among jurists. The Hanafi school, like all major schools, relies on hadith verification; errors in transmission can affect fiqh rulings. Hence, knowledge of tashif and tahrif is important for accurate textual analysis. The passage also notes that scholars wrote many works to address this issue, emphasizing its significance in preserving the integrity of the Prophetic tradition.

Key Terms
التصحيف (al-tashīf): Change in the diacritical points or vowel marks of letters while the form of the writing remains.
التحريف (al-taḥrīf): Altering a word by addition, deletion, substitution, or changing its meaning; more general than tashif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hajar's distinction, what is the key difference between tashif and tahrif?
A) Tashif involves changes in meaning, tahrif involves changes in letters
B) Tashif affects diacritical dots, tahrif affects vowel marks
C) Tashif occurs in the chain, tahrif occurs in the text
D) Tashif is intentional, tahrif is unintentional

Key Takeaway
Proper identification of tashif and tahrif is essential for preserving the prophetic text and ensuring accurate fiqh derivations.

Tashif: Definition, Causes, and Its Division in Chain (Isnad)
Defines tashif, its importance, cause, and first division in isnad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tashif, distinguish it from tahrif, and identify an example of tashif in isnad.

Core Idea
Tashif corrupts the dots of similar letters — a danger that only oral transmission prevents.

This lesson introduces tashif (تصحيف), a critical concept in hadith criticism that preserves the integrity of prophetic traditions. You will learn its precise definition, its root cause in relying on written sources without oral guidance, and the first of its six divisions: tashif in the chain of narrators. Understanding tashif is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh who wishes to trace rulings back to sound prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define tashif precisely
Locate the definition in the text: corruption in the dotting of graphically similar letters. Note the explicit list of letter pairs (e.g., ba/ta/tha, jim/ha/kha).
Tashif is distinct from tahrif (تحريف), which changes the form of the letter itself, not just the dots.
2
Understand the importance and cause
The author stresses that this art purifies hadith from errors. The cause is reliance on written sources (suhuf) without oral transmission from a qualified teacher — hence the warning against the 'suhufi'.
Ibn al-Salah is cited: only skilled memorizers (huffaz) can master this field.
3
Identify the first division: tashif in isnad
The text lists six types of tashif. The first is tashif in the chain of narrators. Note the example given: Shu'bah from al-'Awwam ibn Murajim from Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi.
The example is incomplete in the window, but it illustrates how a misdotting in a narrator's name could change the chain.
4
Apply to Hanafi fiqh
Reflect on how a misidentified narrator (e.g., due to tashif) could affect the authentication of a hadith used as a dalil in Hanafi rulings.
For instance, confusing two narrators with similar names could weaken or strengthen a proof.

الفصل الثَّالِث الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وعلى هَذَا فالتصحيف هُوَ الَّذِي يَكُون في النقط؛ أي في الحروف المتشابهة الَّتِي تختلف في قراءتها مثل : الباء والتاء والثاء والجيم والحاء المهملة والخاء المعجمة، والدال المهملة والذال المعجمة والراء والزاي.
ومعرفة هَذَا الفن من فنون علم الْحَدِيث لَهُ أهمية كبيرة)؛ وذلك لما فيه من تنقية الأحاديث النبوية مِمَّا شابها في بعض الألفاظ سواء كان في متونها أم في رجال أسانيدها.
وعندما كثر التصحيف والتحريف بَيْنَ الناس شرع الحفاظ من أهل الحديث في تصنيف كتب التصحيف والتحريف وكتب المؤتلف والمختلف)(١)، وهذا الفن فن جليل لما يحتاج إلَيْهِ من الدقة والفهم واليقظة، وَلَمْ ينهض بِهِ إلا الحفاظ الحاذقون قَالَ ابن الصَّلاحِ: «هَذَا فن جليل إنما ينهض بأعبائه الحذاق الحفاظ» (٢). من والسبب في وقوع التصحيف والإكثار مِنْهُ إنما يحصل غالباً للآخذ من الصحف وبطون الكتب، دون تلق للحديث عن أستاذ من ذوي الاختصاص؛ لذلك حذر أئمة الْحَدِيث من عمل هَذَا شأنه، قَالَ سعيد بن عبد العزيز التنوخي (٣): (لا تحملوا العلم عن صحفي، ولا تأخذوا القرآن من مصحفي).

مثاله: حَدِيث شعبة، عن العوام بن مراجم (٤)، عن أبي عثمان النهدي (٥)، عن
(١) ولأهمية هَذَا الفن من فنون علم الْحَدِيث فَقَدْ صنف فِيْهِ العلماء عدة كَتَبَ مِنْهَا: تصحيف العلماء: لأبي مُحَمَّد عَبْد الله بن مُسْلِم بن قتيبة الدينوري (ت ٢٧٦ هـ). التنبيه على حدوث التصحيف لحمزة بن الحسن الأصفهاني (ت ٣٦٠ هـ)، وَهُوَ مطبوع. التنبيهات عَلَى أغاليط الرُّوَاة: لأبي نعيم علي بن حمزة البصري (ت ٣٧٥ هـ). شرح ما يقع فيه التصحيف والتحريف : لأبي أحمد الحسن بن عَبْد الله العسكري (ت ۳۸۲ هـ). تصحيفات الْمُحَدِّثِينَ : لأبي أحمد الحسن بن عبد الله العسكري، وَهُوَ مطبوع. تصحيفات الْمُحَدِّثِينَ : للإمام الحافظ أبي الحسن علي بن عمر الدَّارَ قُطْنِي (ت ٣٨٥ هـ). إصلاح خطأ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ : لأبي سليمان حمد بن مُحَمَّد الخطابي (ت ۳۸۸ هـ). الرد على حمزة في حدوث التصحيف لإسحاق بن أحمد بن شبيب (ت ٤٠٥ هـ). متفق التصحيف لأبي علي الحسن بن رشيق القيرواني (ت ٤٥٦ هـ). تلخيص المتشابه في الرسم، وحماية ما أشكل مِنْهُ عن بوادر التصحيف والوهم للخطيب البغدادي (ت ٤٦٣ هـ). تالي التلخيص: لأبي بكر أحمد بن علي الْخَطِيب (ت ٤٦٣ هـ). مشارق الأنوار عَلَى صَحِيح الآثار: لأبي الفضل عياض بن موسى اليحصبي (ت ٥٤٤ هـ). ما يؤمن فيه التصحيف من رجال الأندلس لأبي الوليد يوسف بن عبد العزيز المعروف بابن الدباغ (ت ٥٤٦ هـ). مطالع الأنوار: لأبي إسحاق إِبْرَاهِيم بن يوسف بن إِبْرَاهِيم المعروف بابن قرقول (ت ٥٦٩ هـ). التصحيف والتحريف لأبي الفتح عثمان بن عيسى الموصلي (ت ٦٠٠ هـ). تصحيح التصحيف وتحرير التحريف لخليل بن أيبك الصفدي (ت ٧٦٤ هـ). تحبير الموشين فيما يقال لَهُ بالسين والشين للفيروزآبادي (ت ۸۱۷ هـ). التطريف في التصحيف لأبي الفضل السيوطي (ت ۹۱۱ هـ). التنبيه عَلَى غلط الجاهل والتنبيه لابن كمال باشا (ت ٩٤٠ هـ). وَقَدْ ساق هَذِهِ الكتب ورتبها موفق بن عَبْد الله في كتابه " توثيق النصوص .۱۷۸-۱٧٤ :"

(٣) هُوَ سعيد بن عَبْد العزيز التنوخي الدمشقي : ثقة إمام، لكنه اختلط في آخر أمره، توفي سنة (١٦٧هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (١٦٣ هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (١٦٤هـ). سير أعلام النبلاء ٣٢/٨ ، والكاشف ١٩٢٦٤٤٠/١)، والتقريب (٢٣٥٨).

Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. And accordingly, tashif is that which occurs in the dots; i.e., in similar letters that differ in their reading, such as: ba, ta, tha, jim, ha without dot, kha with dot, dal without dot, dhal with dot, ra, and zay. Knowledge of this art among the arts of hadith science is of great importance; because through it the prophetic hadiths are purified from what has tainted them in some wordings, whether in their texts or in the narrators of their chains. When tashif and tahrif became widespread among people, the hadith memorizers began to author books on tashif and tahrif and books on mu'talif and mukhtalif (1). This art is a noble art because it requires precision, understanding, and alertness, and only skilled memorizers undertake it. Ibn al-Salah said: 'This is a noble art, only the skilled memorizers can bear its burdens.' (2) The reason for the occurrence of tashif and its abundance mostly happens from one who takes from papers and the interiors of books, without receiving hadith from a teacher of specialization; therefore the leading hadith scholars warned against doing such. Sa'id ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tanukhi (3) said: 'Do not take knowledge from a suhufi, and do not take the Qur'an from a mus'hafi.' Sections of Tashif: Tashif according to its existence and branching has divisions. It is divided into six types: The First Section: Tashif in the Chain. Example: The hadith of Shu'bah, from al-'Awwam ibn Murajim (4), from Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi (5), from...(6)
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of tashif (تصحيف) in hadith studies. The author defines tashif as corruption in the dotting of letters that are graphically similar, such as ba and ta, etc. He emphasizes the importance of this field for purifying hadith texts and chains from errors. He notes that when tashif and tahrif (تحريف) became widespread, scholars compiled works on these topics, listing numerous books. The passage then cites Ibn al-Salah on the nobility of this art and explains that tashif often occurs from relying solely on written sources without oral instruction from a qualified teacher. A warning is given by Sa'id al-Tanukhi against taking knowledge from a 'suhufi' (one who learns only from sheets). Finally, the author begins enumerating the six divisions of tashif, giving the first: tashif in the chain (isnad), with an example from Shu'bah's narration that is cut off in this window.

Key Terms
تصحيف (tashif): Corruption in the dotting of letters that are graphically similar, causing a change in reading
تحريف (tahrif): Corruption in the form of a letter beyond dotting, such as changing a word entirely
المؤتلف والمختلف (al-mu'talif wa al-mukhtalif): Terms in hadith that agree in writing but differ in pronunciation
صحفي (suhufi): A person who learns only from sheets/papers without oral instruction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the example given for tashif in the chain (isnad)?
A) Hadith of Shu'bah, from al-'Awwam ibn Murajim, from Abu 'Uthman al-Nahdi
B) Hadith of al-Zuhri, from 'Urwa, from 'Aisha
C) Hadith of Abu Hurairah, from the Prophet, about the cat
D) Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, from the Prophet, about prayer

Key Takeaway
Tashif corrupts the dots of similar letters; it affects both text and chain, and oral transmission from a teacher is the primary safeguard.

Tashif al-Sam': Corruption by Hearing in Hadith
Defines tashif al-sam' with example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tashif al-sam', explain its cause, and distinguish it from tashif al-basar using the example of 'Asim al-Ahwal and Wasil al-Ahdab.

Core Idea
Tashif al-sam' corrupts a hadith through mishearing, not misreading—distinguishing the cause determines reliability.

You are probably familiar with errors in copying text. But what about errors in hearing? This lesson introduces a key concept in hadith criticism: tashif al-sam' (corruption by hearing). The passage explains how similar pronunciation can lead a narrator to mishear and mis-report a hadith. Understanding this helps you evaluate the authenticity of a hadith report, a skill important for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first sentence to understand what tashif al-sam' is: a corruption due to similarity in points of articulation (makharij).
Contrast with tashif al-basar (visual error).
2
Understand the cause
The cause is auditory confusion: words sound alike when pronounced, leading to mishearing.
This is a transmission error, not a writing error.
3
Analyze the example
The hadith from 'Asim al-Ahwal was misnarrated as 'an Wasil al-Ahdab. Notice how the names are different in writing but similar in sound.
Daraqutni identified this as tashif of hearing because the written forms are distinct.
4
Distinguish from tashif al-basar
If the error could be due to misreading similar letters, it would be tashif of sight. Here, the mistake is only possible through hearing.
Ibn al-Salah supports Daraqutni's reasoning.
5
Assess the impact on hadith acceptance
In Hanafi usul, a hadith with tashif al-sam' becomes weak (da'if) if the error is proven, unless there is corroboration.
This affects the use of ahad hadith in deriving legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الرابع: تصحيف السمع
ويحدث بسبب تشابه مخارج الكلمات في النطق فيختلط الأمر على السامع فيقع في التصحيف أو التحريف. نحو حَدِيث لـ: «عاصم الأحول»، رَوَاهُ بعضهم فَقَالَ: «عن واصل الأحدب وَقَدْ ذَكَرَ الإمام الدَّارَ قُطْنِي أَنَّهُ من تصحيف السمع لا من تصحيف البصر قال ابن الصلاح: «كأنه ذهب - والله أعلم - إلى أن ذَلِكَ مِمَّا لا يشتبه من حَيْثُ الكتابة، وإنما أخطأ فِيهِ سمع من رَوَاهُ»
Section Four: Tashif of Hearing. It occurs due to the similarity of the points of articulation of words in pronunciation, so the matter becomes confused for the listener, leading to tashif or alteration. Example: the hadith of ‘Asim al-Ahwal, narrated by some as ‘an Wasil al-Ahdab. Imam al-Daraqutni mentioned that this is tashif of hearing, not tashif of sight. Ibn al-Salah said: 'It seems — and Allah knows best — that he deemed that this is not confusing from the perspective of writing, but the one who narrated it made a mistake in hearing.'
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth type of tashif (corruption in hadith): tashif al-sam‘ (corruption by hearing). The author explains that this occurs when words have similar points of articulation (makharij) in pronunciation, making it easy for a listener to confuse them. This leads to either tashif (changing the word while preserving the meaning) or tahrif (changing the meaning). The example given is a hadith from ‘Asim al-Ahwal, which was narrated by some as ‘an Wasil al-Ahdab. The important point is that Imam al-Daraqutni identified this as tashif of hearing, not of sight, because the written forms are distinct, but the mishearing led to the error. Ibn al-Salah supports this reasoning. This classification is crucial for hadith criticism and directly impacts the acceptance of ahad hadith in Hanafi usul, as errors in transmission affect the reliability of the report.

Key Terms
تصحيف السمع (taṣḥīf al-sam‘): A type of hadith corruption resulting from mishearing similar-sounding words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary cause of tashif al-sam‘ as described in the passage?
A) Similarity in written letters
B) Similarity in the points of articulation of words
C) Intentional alteration by narrators
D) Lack of written records

Key Takeaway
Tashif al-sam' is a corruption caused by mishearing due to similar pronunciation, and its identification is vital for hadith criticism.
